## Points of Interest

* [Genesis 1:6-8](#GEN1V6) seems to suggest that there is water below us and above us. It seems to describe God creating a tunnel between waters. I believe some people site this as "the firmament."
* [Genesis 1:14](#GEN1V14) suggests that night and day weren't made until the fourth day, yet somehow "evening" and "morning" had been passing for the previous three days. What, then, is morning and evening?
* [Genesis 1:26](#GEN1V26) Who is the "us" that God would refer to?
* [Genesis 1:29](#GEN1V29) God gave every seed-bearing plant as food for all creatures with life. I was expecting God to also give all creatures to men and woman as food, as well.
* [Genesis 2:2](#GEN2V2) Why does God need to rest? What does he do to relax?
* [Genesis 2:5](#GEN2V5) It seems weird that God created vegetation on the third day, but this verse states (in the NIV version) that "no shrub of the field had yet appeared on earth and no plant of the field had yet sprung up, for the LORD God had not sent rain on the earth..."
* [Genesis 2:7](#GEN2V7) Man was made from a combination of dust and "breath of life."
* [Genesis 2:9](#GEN2V9) The tree of life and the tree of the knowledge of good and evil were two separate trees.
* [Genesis 2:16-17](#GEN2V16) This is "the lie."
* [Genesis 2:10-2:14](#GEN2V10) Can these rivers be identified today to reveal the location of the location of the Garden of Eden?
* [Genesis 2:19](#GEN2V19) Man got to name every living creature.
* [Genesis 2:22](#GEN2V22) A woman was made from the rib of man while he was in a deep sleep, like it was a surgical operation.
* [Genesis 2:25](#GEN2V25) Famous nudity and shame verse.
* [Genesis 3:4](#GEN3V4) I guess this suggests that knowledge of good and evil is innate.
* [Genesis 3:6](#GEN3V6) It's not clear that Adam knew what he was eating.
* [Genesis 3:7](#GEN3V7) The first thing they felt guilt for was being naked. 
* [Genesis 3:8](#GEN3V8) God was just walking around, talking.
* [Genesis 3:12](#GEN3V12) Adam does not take responsibility. 
* [Genesis 3:13](#GEN3V13) The woman says the serpent deceived her, but it seems like he just convinced her.
* [Genesis 3:14](#GEN3V14) Did the serpent have legs before this? 
* [Genesis 3:15](#GEN3V15) Are serpents and humans destined to be the worst of enemies? 
* [Genesis 3:16](#GEN3V16) Women were curses with painful child birth and to be ruled over by their husband.
* [Genesis 3:17-19](#GEN3V17) Man's curse just seems to be to have to work more, to farm.
* [Genesis 3:22](#GEN3V22) Who's the "us" that God refers to? Why shouldn't man live forever?
* [Genesis 3:24](#GEN3V24) When were "cherubim" created? 
* [Genesis 4:2-5](#GEN4V2) Cain and Abel were able to just walk up to God to give him offerings. God preferred fat to fruit.
* [Genesis 4:6-7](#GEN4V6) It seems like God thinks Cain should know that jealousy or envy is a sin. The Bible doesn't mention, yet, what exactly constitutes sin, or what training any of the humans have yet had.
* [Genesis 4:9](#GEN4V9) Similar to when God called out Adam, he first asked him a question, and let Cain respond. This is the brother's keeper verse.
* [Genesis 4:14](#GEN4V14) Who are the people that may find Cain?
* [Genesis 4:15](#GEN4V15) Mark of Cain.
* [Genesis 4:17](#GEN4V17) Who was to be Cain's wife that was not his sister? What concept did Cain have of a city?
* [Genesis 5:21-24](#GEN5V21) It seems Enoch lived 365 years and then was taken somewhere by God.
* [Genesis 5:25](#GEN5V25) Methuselah is often cited as the longest living person at 969 years.
* [Genesis 6:1-6:4](#GEN6V1) God's sons mated with women. Who, or what, were God's sons?
* [Genesis 6:4](#GEN6V4) Nephilim.
* [Genesis 7:2](#GEN7V2) This is the numbers of animals for Noah's Ark. I think just remember two of every animal from this story as a kid. Was is a clean animal?
* [Genesis 9:1-4](#GEN9V1) It seems like people were supposed to be vegetarians before the flood, but were permitted to eat animals after the flood.
* [Genesis 9:6](#GEN9V6) It seems a curse was placed, that any man who kills another will be killed.
* [Genesis 9:12-17](#GEN9V12) God created rainbows as a reminder to himself not to kill every living creature on the Earth via flood again.
* [Genesis 9:20-28](#GEN9V20) Where is Noah's sense of personal accountability? How was this the only redeeming man at the time of the flood? It seems drastic to curse the lineage of your own son because you got drunk and passed out naked.
* [Genesis 11:1-9](#GEN11V1) I remembered the Tower of Babel as being about the sinful pride of a ruler, but it just kind of seems like God was concerned that men working together would be able to achieve too much. It also seems strange that God is using plural language again ("let's go down...").
* [Genesis 12:12-20](#GEN12V12) No comment is made on whether Abram's lie is a sin.

## World English Bible Text

### 1

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V1">
    1
  </span>
  In the beginning, God

  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V5">

  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V8">
    8

</div>
<div class="p">

  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V10">
    10

  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V11">
    11

  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V12">
    12
  </span>

  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V13">
    13
  </span>

</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V14">

  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V15">
    15
  </span>
  and let them be for lights in the expanse of the sky to give light on the earth;” and it was so.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V16">
    16
  </span>

  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V17">
    17
  </span>
  God set them in the expanse of the sky to give light to the earth,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V18">
    18
  </span>
  and to rule over the day and over the night, and to divide the light from the darkness. God saw that it was good.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V19">
    19
  </span>
  There was evening and there was morning, a fourth day.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V20">
    20
  </span>
  God said, “Let the waters abound with living creatures, and let birds fly above the earth in the open expanse of the sky.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V21">
    21
  </span>
  God created the large sea creatures and every living creature that moves, with which the waters swarmed, after their kind, and every winged bird after its kind. God saw that it was good.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V22">
    22
  </span>
  God blessed them, saying, “Be fruitful, and multiply, and fill the waters in the seas, and let birds multiply on the earth.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V23">
    23
  </span>
  There was evening and there was morning, a fifth day.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V24">
    24
  </span>
  God said, “Let the earth produce living creatures after their kind, livestock, creeping things, and animals of the earth after their kind;” and it was so.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V25">
    25
  </span>
  God made the animals of the earth after their kind, and the livestock after their kind, and everything that creeps on the ground after its kind. God saw that it was good.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V26">
    26
  </span>
  God said, “Let’s make man in our image, after our likeness. Let them have dominion over the fish of the sea, and over the birds of the sky, and over the livestock, and over all the earth, and over every creeping thing that creeps on the earth.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V27">
    27
  </span>
  God created man in his own image. In God’s image he created him; male and female he created them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V28">
    28
  </span>
  God blessed them. God said to them, “Be fruitful, multiply, fill the earth, and subdue it. Have dominion over the fish of the sea, over the birds of the sky, and over every living thing that moves on the earth.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V29">
    29
  </span>
  God said, “Behold,
  <a href="#GEN1FN2" class="notemark">

    <span class="popup">

    </span>
  </a>
  I have given you every herb yielding seed, which is on the surface of all the earth, and every tree, which bears fruit yielding seed. It will be your food.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V30">
    30
  </span>
  To every animal of the earth, and to every bird of the sky, and to everything that creeps on the earth, in which there is life, I have given every green herb for food;” and it was so.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN1V31">

  </span>

  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V3">
    3

</div>
<div class="p">

    4
  </span>
  This is the history of the generations of the heavens and of the earth when they were created, in the day that Yahweh
  <a href="#GEN2FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      “Yahweh” is God’s proper Name, sometimes rendered “LORD” (all caps) in other translations.
    </span>

  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V5">
    5
  </span>
  No plant of the field was yet in the earth, and no herb of the field had yet sprung up; for Yahweh God had not caused it to rain on the earth. There was not a man to till the ground,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V6">
    6
  </span>
  but a mist went up from the earth, and watered the whole surface of the ground.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V7">
    7
  </span>
  Yahweh God formed man from the dust of the ground, and breathed into his nostrils the breath of life; and man became a living soul.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V8">
    8
  </span>
  Yahweh God planted a garden eastward, in Eden, and there he put the man whom he had formed.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V9">
    9
  </span>
  Out of the ground Yahweh God made every tree to grow that is pleasant to the sight, and good for food, including the tree of life in the middle of the garden and the tree of the knowledge of good and evil.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V10">
    10
  </span>
  A river went out of Eden to water the garden; and from there it was parted, and became the source of four rivers.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V11">
    11
  </span>
  The name of the first is Pishon: it flows through the whole land of Havilah, where there is gold;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V12">
    12
  </span>
  and the gold of that land is good. Bdellium
  <a href="#GEN2FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      or, aromatic resin
    </span>
  </a>
  and onyx stone are also there.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V13">
    13
  </span>

  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V14">
    14
  </span>
  The name of the third river is Hiddekel. This is the one which flows in front of Assyria. The fourth river is the Euphrates.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V15">
    15
  </span>
  Yahweh God took the man, and put him into the garden of Eden to cultivate and keep it.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V16">
    16
  </span>
  Yahweh God commanded the man, saying, “You may freely eat of every tree of the garden;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V17">
    17
  </span>
  but you shall not eat of the tree of the knowledge of good and evil; for in the day that you eat of it, you will surely die.”
</div>

  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V20">
    20
  </span>

  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V21">
    21
  </span>

  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V23">
    23

    24

  <span class="verse" id="GEN2V25">
    25
  </span>

### 3

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V1">
    1
  </span>
  Now the serpent was more subtle than any animal of the field which Yahweh God had made. He said to the woman, “Has God really said, ‘You shall not eat of any tree of the garden’?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V2">
    2
  </span>
  The woman said to the serpent, “We may eat fruit from the trees of the garden,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V3">
    3
  </span>
  but not the fruit of the tree which is in the middle of the garden. God has said, ‘You shall not eat of it. You shall not touch it, lest you die.’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V4">
    4
  </span>
  The serpent said to the woman, “You won’t really die,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V5">
    5
  </span>
  for God knows that in the day you eat it, your eyes will be opened, and you will be like God, knowing good and evil.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V6">
    6
  </span>
  When the woman saw that the tree was good for food, and that it was a delight to the eyes, and that the tree was to be desired to make one wise, she took some of its fruit, and ate. Then she gave some to her husband with her, and he ate it, too.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V7">
    7
  </span>
  Their eyes were opened, and they both knew that they were naked. They sewed fig leaves together, and made coverings for themselves.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V8">
    8
  </span>
  They heard Yahweh God’s voice walking in the garden in the cool of the day, and the man and his wife hid themselves from the presence of Yahweh God among the trees of the garden.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V9">
    9
  </span>
  Yahweh God called to the man, and said to him, “Where are you?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V10">
    10
  </span>
  The man said, “I heard your voice in the garden, and I was afraid, because I was naked; so I hid myself.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V11">
    11
  </span>
  God said, “Who told you that you were naked? Have you eaten from the tree that I commanded you not to eat from?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V12">
    12
  </span>
  The man said, “The woman whom you gave to be with me, she gave me fruit from the tree, and I ate it.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V13">
    13
  </span>
  Yahweh God said to the woman, “What have you done?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  The woman said, “The serpent deceived me, and I ate.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V14">
    14
  </span>
  Yahweh God said to the serpent,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “Because you have done this,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  you are cursed above all livestock,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and above every animal of the field.
</div>
<div class="q">
  You shall go on your belly
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and you shall eat dust all the days of your life.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V15">
    15
  </span>
  I will put hostility between you and the woman,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and between your offspring and her offspring.
</div>
<div class="q">
  He will bruise your head,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and you will bruise his heel.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V16">
    16
  </span>
  To the woman he said,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “I will greatly multiply your pain in childbirth.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  You will bear children in pain.
</div>
<div class="q">
  Your desire will be for your husband,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and he will rule over you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V17">
    17
  </span>
  To Adam he said,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “Because you have listened to your wife’s voice,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and have eaten from the tree,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  about which I commanded you, saying, ‘You shall not eat of it,’
</div>
<div class="q2">
  the ground is cursed for your sake.
</div>
<div class="q">
  You will eat from it with much labor all the days of your life.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V18">
    18
  </span>
  It will yield thorns and thistles to you;
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and you will eat the herb of the field.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V19">
    19
  </span>
  You will eat bread by the sweat of your face until you return to the ground,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  for you were taken out of it.
</div>
<div class="q">
  For you are dust,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and you shall return to dust.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V20">
    20
  </span>
  The man called his wife Eve because she would be the mother of all the living.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V21">
    21
  </span>
  Yahweh God made garments of animal skins for Adam and for his wife, and clothed them.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V22">
    22
  </span>
  Yahweh God said, “Behold, the man has become like one of us, knowing good and evil. Now, lest he reach out his hand, and also take of the tree of life, and eat, and live forever—”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V23">
    23
  </span>
  Therefore Yahweh God sent him out from the garden of Eden, to till the ground from which he was taken.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN3V24">
    24
  </span>
  So he drove out the man; and he placed cherubim
  <a href="#GEN3FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      cherubim are powerful angelic creatures, messengers of God with wings. See Ezekiel 10.
    </span>
  </a>
  at the east of the garden of Eden, and a flaming sword which turned every way, to guard the way to the tree of life.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN3FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN3V24">
      3:24
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      cherubim are powerful angelic creatures, messengers of God with wings. See Ezekiel 10.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 4

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V1">
    1
  </span>
  The man knew
  <a href="#GEN4FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      or, lay with, or, had relations with
    </span>
  </a>
  Eve his wife. She conceived,
  <a href="#GEN4FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      or, became pregnant
    </span>
  </a>
  and gave birth to Cain, and said, “I have gotten a man with Yahweh’s help.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V2">
    2
  </span>
  Again she gave birth, to Cain’s brother Abel. Abel was a keeper of sheep, but Cain was a tiller of the ground.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V3">
    3
  </span>
  As time passed, Cain brought an offering to Yahweh from the fruit of the ground.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V4">
    4
  </span>
  Abel also brought some of the firstborn of his flock and of its fat. Yahweh respected Abel and his offering,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V5">
    5
  </span>
  but he didn’t respect Cain and his offering. Cain was very angry, and the expression on his face fell.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V6">
    6
  </span>
  Yahweh said to Cain, “Why are you angry? Why has the expression of your face fallen?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V7">
    7
  </span>
  If you do well, won’t it be lifted up? If you don’t do well, sin crouches at the door. Its desire is for you, but you are to rule over it.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V8">
    8
  </span>
  Cain said to Abel, his brother, “Let’s go into the field.” While they were in the field, Cain rose up against Abel, his brother, and killed him.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V9">
    9
  </span>
  Yahweh said to Cain, “Where is Abel, your brother?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “I don’t know. Am I my brother’s keeper?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V10">
    10
  </span>
  Yahweh said, “What have you done? The voice of your brother’s blood cries to me from the ground.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V11">
    11
  </span>
  Now you are cursed because of the ground, which has opened its mouth to receive your brother’s blood from your hand.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V12">
    12
  </span>
  From now on, when you till the ground, it won’t yield its strength to you. You will be a fugitive and a wanderer in the earth.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V13">
    13
  </span>
  Cain said to Yahweh, “My punishment is greater than I can bear.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V14">
    14
  </span>
  Behold, you have driven me out today from the surface of the ground. I will be hidden from your face, and I will be a fugitive and a wanderer in the earth. Whoever finds me will kill me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V15">
    15
  </span>
  Yahweh said to him, “Therefore whoever slays Cain, vengeance will be taken on him sevenfold.” Yahweh appointed a sign for Cain, so that anyone finding him would not strike him.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V16">
    16
  </span>
  Cain left Yahweh’s presence, and lived in the land of Nod, east of Eden.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V17">
    17
  </span>
  Cain knew his wife. She conceived, and gave birth to Enoch. He built a city, and named the city after the name of his son, Enoch.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V18">
    18
  </span>
  Irad was born to Enoch. Irad became the father of Mehujael. Mehujael became the father of Methushael. Methushael became the father of Lamech.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V19">
    19
  </span>
  Lamech took two wives: the name of the first one was Adah, and the name of the second one was Zillah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V20">
    20
  </span>
  Adah gave birth to Jabal, who was the father of those who dwell in tents and have livestock.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V21">
    21
  </span>
  His brother’s name was Jubal, who was the father of all who handle the harp and pipe.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V22">
    22
  </span>
  Zillah also gave birth to Tubal Cain, the forger of every cutting instrument of bronze and iron. Tubal Cain’s sister was Naamah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V23">
    23
  </span>
  Lamech said to his wives,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “Adah and Zillah, hear my voice.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  You wives of Lamech, listen to my speech,
</div>
<div class="q">
  for I have slain a man for wounding me,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  a young man for bruising me.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V24">
    24
  </span>
  If Cain will be avenged seven times,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  truly Lamech seventy-seven times.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V25">
    25
  </span>
  Adam knew his wife again. She gave birth to a son, and named him Seth, saying, “for God has given me another child instead of Abel, for Cain killed him.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN4V26">
    26
  </span>
  A son was also born to Seth, and he named him Enosh. At that time men began to call on Yahweh’s name.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN4FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN4V1">
      4:1
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      or, lay with, or, had relations with
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN4FN2">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN4V1">
      4:1
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      or, became pregnant
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 5

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V1">
    1
  </span>
  This is the book of the generations of Adam. In the day that God created man, he made him in God’s likeness.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V2">
    2
  </span>
  He created them male and female, and blessed them. On the day they were created, he named them Adam.
  <a href="#GEN5FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      “Adam” and “Man” are spelled with the exact same consonants in Hebrew, so this can be correctly translated either way.
    </span>
  </a>
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V3">
    3
  </span>
  Adam lived one hundred thirty years, and became the father of a son in his own likeness, after his image, and named him Seth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V4">
    4
  </span>
  The days of Adam after he became the father of Seth were eight hundred years, and he became the father of other sons and daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V5">
    5
  </span>
  All the days that Adam lived were nine hundred thirty years, then he died.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V6">
    6
  </span>
  Seth lived one hundred five years, then became the father of Enosh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V7">
    7
  </span>
  Seth lived after he became the father of Enosh eight hundred seven years, and became the father of other sons and daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V8">
    8
  </span>
  All of the days of Seth were nine hundred twelve years, then he died.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V9">
    9
  </span>
  Enosh lived ninety years, and became the father of Kenan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V10">
    10
  </span>
  Enosh lived after he became the father of Kenan eight hundred fifteen years, and became the father of other sons and daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V11">
    11
  </span>
  All of the days of Enosh were nine hundred five years, then he died.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V12">
    12
  </span>
  Kenan lived seventy years, then became the father of Mahalalel.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V13">
    13
  </span>
  Kenan lived after he became the father of Mahalalel eight hundred forty years, and became the father of other sons and daughters
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V14">
    14
  </span>
  and all of the days of Kenan were nine hundred ten years, then he died.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V15">
    15
  </span>
  Mahalalel lived sixty-five years, then became the father of Jared.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V16">
    16
  </span>
  Mahalalel lived after he became the father of Jared eight hundred thirty years, and became the father of other sons and daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V17">
    17
  </span>
  All of the days of Mahalalel were eight hundred ninety-five years, then he died.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V18">
    18
  </span>
  Jared lived one hundred sixty-two years, then became the father of Enoch.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V19">
    19
  </span>
  Jared lived after he became the father of Enoch eight hundred years, and became the father of other sons and daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V20">
    20
  </span>
  All of the days of Jared were nine hundred sixty-two years, then he died.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V21">
    21
  </span>
  Enoch lived sixty-five years, then became the father of Methuselah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V22">
    22
  </span>
  After Methuselah’s birth, Enoch walked with God for three hundred years, and became the father of more sons and daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V23">
    23
  </span>
  All the days of Enoch were three hundred sixty-five years.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V24">
    24
  </span>
  Enoch walked with God, and he was not found, for God took him.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V25">
    25
  </span>
  Methuselah lived one hundred eighty-seven years, then became the father of Lamech.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V26">
    26
  </span>
  Methuselah lived after he became the father of Lamech seven hundred eighty-two years, and became the father of other sons and daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V27">
    27
  </span>
  All the days of Methuselah were nine hundred sixty-nine years, then he died.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V28">
    28
  </span>
  Lamech lived one hundred eighty-two years, then became the father of a son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V29">
    29
  </span>
  He named him Noah, saying, “This one will comfort us in our work and in the toil of our hands, caused by the ground which Yahweh has cursed.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V30">
    30
  </span>
  Lamech lived after he became the father of Noah five hundred ninety-five years, and became the father of other sons and daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V31">
    31
  </span>
  All the days of Lamech were seven hundred seventy-seven years, then he died.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN5V32">
    32
  </span>
  Noah was five hundred years old, then Noah became the father of Shem, Ham, and Japheth.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN5FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN5V2">
      5:2
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Adam” and “Man” are spelled with the exact same consonants in Hebrew, so this can be correctly translated either way.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 6

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V1">
    1
  </span>
  When men began to multiply on the surface of the ground, and daughters were born to them,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V2">
    2
  </span>
  God’s sons saw that men’s daughters were beautiful, and they took any that they wanted for themselves as wives.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V3">
    3
  </span>
  Yahweh said, “My Spirit will not strive with man forever, because he also is flesh; so his days will be one hundred twenty years.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V4">
    4
  </span>
  The Nephilim
  <a href="#GEN6FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      or, giants
    </span>
  </a>
  were in the earth in those days, and also after that, when God’s sons came in to men’s daughters and had children with them. Those were the mighty men who were of old, men of renown.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V5">
    5
  </span>
  Yahweh saw that the wickedness of man was great in the earth, and that every imagination of the thoughts of man’s heart was continually only evil.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V6">
    6
  </span>
  Yahweh was sorry that he had made man on the earth, and it grieved him in his heart.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V7">
    7
  </span>
  Yahweh said, “I will destroy man whom I have created from the surface of the ground—man, along with animals, creeping things, and birds of the sky—for I am sorry that I have made them.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V8">
    8
  </span>
  But Noah found favor in Yahweh’s eyes.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V9">
    9
  </span>
  This is the history of the generations of Noah: Noah was a righteous man, blameless among the people of his time. Noah walked with God.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V10">
    10
  </span>
  Noah became the father of three sons: Shem, Ham, and Japheth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V11">
    11
  </span>
  The earth was corrupt before God, and the earth was filled with violence.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V12">
    12
  </span>
  God saw the earth, and saw that it was corrupt, for all flesh had corrupted their way on the earth.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V13">
    13
  </span>
  God said to Noah, “I will bring an end to all flesh, for the earth is filled with violence through them. Behold, I will destroy them and the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V14">
    14
  </span>
  Make a ship of gopher wood. You shall make rooms in the ship, and shall seal it inside and outside with pitch.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V15">
    15
  </span>
  This is how you shall make it. The length of the ship shall be three hundred cubits,
  <a href="#GEN6FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      A cubit is the length from the tip of the middle finger to the elbow on a man’s arm, or about 18 inches or 46 centimeters.
    </span>
  </a>
  its width fifty cubits, and its height thirty cubits.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V16">
    16
  </span>
  You shall make a roof in the ship, and you shall finish it to a cubit upward. You shall set the door of the ship in its side. You shall make it with lower, second, and third levels.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V17">
    17
  </span>
  I, even I, will bring the flood of waters on this earth, to destroy all flesh having the breath of life from under the sky. Everything that is in the earth will die.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V18">
    18
  </span>
  But I will establish my covenant with you. You shall come into the ship, you, your sons, your wife, and your sons’ wives with you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V19">
    19
  </span>
  Of every living thing of all flesh, you shall bring two of every sort into the ship, to keep them alive with you. They shall be male and female.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V20">
    20
  </span>
  Of the birds after their kind, of the livestock after their kind, of every creeping thing of the ground after its kind, two of every sort will come to you, to keep them alive.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V21">
    21
  </span>
  Take with you some of all food that is eaten, and gather it to yourself; and it will be for food for you, and for them.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN6V22">
    22
  </span>
  Thus Noah did. He did all that God commanded him.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN6FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN6V4">
      6:4
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      or, giants
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN6FN2">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN6V15">
      6:15
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      A cubit is the length from the tip of the middle finger to the elbow on a man’s arm, or about 18 inches or 46 centimeters.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 7

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V1">
    1
  </span>
  Yahweh said to Noah, “Come with all of your household into the ship, for I have seen your righteousness before me in this generation.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V2">
    2
  </span>
  You shall take seven pairs of every clean animal with you, the male and his female. Of the animals that are not clean, take two, the male and his female.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V3">
    3
  </span>
  Also of the birds of the sky, seven and seven, male and female, to keep seed alive on the surface of all the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V4">
    4
  </span>
  In seven days, I will cause it to rain on the earth for forty days and forty nights. I will destroy every living thing that I have made from the surface of the ground.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V5">
    5
  </span>
  Noah did everything that Yahweh commanded him.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V6">
    6
  </span>
  Noah was six hundred years old when the flood of waters came on the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V7">
    7
  </span>
  Noah went into the ship with his sons, his wife, and his sons’ wives, because of the floodwaters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V8">
    8
  </span>
  Clean animals, unclean animals, birds, and everything that creeps on the ground
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V9">
    9
  </span>
  went by pairs to Noah into the ship, male and female, as God commanded Noah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V10">
    10
  </span>
  After the seven days, the floodwaters came on the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V11">
    11
  </span>
  In the six hundredth year of Noah’s life, in the second month, on the seventeenth day of the month, on that day all the fountains of the great deep burst open, and the sky’s windows opened.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V12">
    12
  </span>
  It rained on the earth forty days and forty nights.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V13">
    13
  </span>
  In the same day Noah, and Shem, Ham, and Japheth—the sons of Noah—and Noah’s wife and the three wives of his sons with them, entered into the ship—
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V14">
    14
  </span>
  they, and every animal after its kind, all the livestock after their kind, every creeping thing that creeps on the earth after its kind, and every bird after its kind, every bird of every sort.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V15">
    15
  </span>
  Pairs from all flesh with the breath of life in them went into the ship to Noah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V16">
    16
  </span>
  Those who went in, went in male and female of all flesh, as God commanded him; then Yahweh shut him in.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V17">
    17
  </span>
  The flood was forty days on the earth. The waters increased, and lifted up the ship, and it was lifted up above the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V18">
    18
  </span>
  The waters rose, and increased greatly on the earth; and the ship floated on the surface of the waters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V19">
    19
  </span>
  The waters rose very high on the earth. All the high mountains that were under the whole sky were covered.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V20">
    20
  </span>
  The waters rose fifteen cubits
  <a href="#GEN7FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      A cubit is the length from the tip of the middle finger to the elbow on a man’s arm, or about 18 inches or 46 centimeters.
    </span>
  </a>
  higher, and the mountains were covered.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V21">
    21
  </span>
  All flesh died that moved on the earth, including birds, livestock, animals, every creeping thing that creeps on the earth, and every man.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V22">
    22
  </span>
  All on the dry land, in whose nostrils was the breath of the spirit of life, died.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V23">
    23
  </span>
  Every living thing was destroyed that was on the surface of the ground, including man, livestock, creeping things, and birds of the sky. They were destroyed from the earth. Only Noah was left, and those who were with him in the ship.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN7V24">
    24
  </span>
  The waters flooded the earth one hundred fifty days.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN7FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN7V20">
      7:20
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      A cubit is the length from the tip of the middle finger to the elbow on a man’s arm, or about 18 inches or 46 centimeters.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 8

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V1">
    1
  </span>
  God remembered Noah, all the animals, and all the livestock that were with him in the ship; and God made a wind to pass over the earth. The waters subsided.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V2">
    2
  </span>
  The deep’s fountains and the sky’s windows were also stopped, and the rain from the sky was restrained.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V3">
    3
  </span>
  The waters continually receded from the earth. After the end of one hundred fifty days the waters receded.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V4">
    4
  </span>
  The ship rested in the seventh month, on the seventeenth day of the month, on Ararat’s mountains.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V5">
    5
  </span>
  The waters receded continually until the tenth month. In the tenth month, on the first day of the month, the tops of the mountains were visible.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V6">
    6
  </span>
  At the end of forty days, Noah opened the window of the ship which he had made,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V7">
    7
  </span>
  and he sent out a raven. It went back and forth, until the waters were dried up from the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V8">
    8
  </span>
  He himself sent out a dove to see if the waters were abated from the surface of the ground,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V9">
    9
  </span>
  but the dove found no place to rest her foot, and she returned into the ship to him, for the waters were on the surface of the whole earth. He put out his hand, and took her, and brought her to him into the ship.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V10">
    10
  </span>
  He waited yet another seven days; and again he sent the dove out of the ship.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V11">
    11
  </span>
  The dove came back to him at evening and, behold, in her mouth was a freshly plucked olive leaf. So Noah knew that the waters were abated from the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V12">
    12
  </span>
  He waited yet another seven days, and sent out the dove; and she didn’t return to him any more.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V13">
    13
  </span>
  In the six hundred first year, in the first month, the first day of the month, the waters were dried up from the earth. Noah removed the covering of the ship, and looked. He saw that the surface of the ground was dry.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V14">
    14
  </span>
  In the second month, on the twenty-seventh day of the month, the earth was dry.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V15">
    15
  </span>
  God spoke to Noah, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V16">
    16
  </span>
  “Go out of the ship, you, your wife, your sons, and your sons’ wives with you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V17">
    17
  </span>
  Bring out with you every living thing that is with you of all flesh, including birds, livestock, and every creeping thing that creeps on the earth, that they may breed abundantly in the earth, and be fruitful, and multiply on the earth.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V18">
    18
  </span>
  Noah went out, with his sons, his wife, and his sons’ wives with him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V19">
    19
  </span>
  Every animal, every creeping thing, and every bird, whatever moves on the earth, after their families, went out of the ship.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V20">
    20
  </span>
  Noah built an altar to Yahweh, and took of every clean animal, and of every clean bird, and offered burnt offerings on the altar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V21">
    21
  </span>
  Yahweh smelled the pleasant aroma. Yahweh said in his heart, “I will not again curse the ground any more for man’s sake because the imagination of man’s heart is evil from his youth. I will never again strike every living thing, as I have done.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN8V22">
    22
  </span>
  While the earth remains, seed time and harvest, and cold and heat, and summer and winter, and day and night will not cease.”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 9

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V1">
    1
  </span>
  God blessed Noah and his sons, and said to them, “Be fruitful, multiply, and replenish the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V2">
    2
  </span>
  The fear of you and the dread of you will be on every animal of the earth, and on every bird of the sky. Everything that moves along the ground, and all the fish of the sea, are delivered into your hand.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V3">
    3
  </span>
  Every moving thing that lives will be food for you. As I gave you the green herb, I have given everything to you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V4">
    4
  </span>
  But flesh with its life, that is, its blood, you shall not eat.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V5">
    5
  </span>
  I will surely require accounting for your life’s blood. At the hand of every animal I will require it. At the hand of man, even at the hand of every man’s brother, I will require the life of man.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V6">
    6
  </span>
  Whoever sheds man’s blood, his blood will be shed by man, for God made man in his own image.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V7">
    7
  </span>
  Be fruitful and multiply. Increase abundantly in the earth, and multiply in it.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V8">
    8
  </span>
  God spoke to Noah and to his sons with him, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V9">
    9
  </span>
  “As for me, behold, I establish my covenant with you, and with your offspring after you,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V10">
    10
  </span>
  and with every living creature that is with you: the birds, the livestock, and every animal of the earth with you, of all that go out of the ship, even every animal of the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V11">
    11
  </span>
  I will establish my covenant with you: All flesh will not be cut off any more by the waters of the flood. There will never again be a flood to destroy the earth.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V12">
    12
  </span>
  God said, “This is the token of the covenant which I make between me and you and every living creature that is with you, for perpetual generations:
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V13">
    13
  </span>
  I set my rainbow in the cloud, and it will be a sign of a covenant between me and the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V14">
    14
  </span>
  When I bring a cloud over the earth, that the rainbow will be seen in the cloud,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V15">
    15
  </span>
  I will remember my covenant, which is between me and you and every living creature of all flesh, and the waters will no more become a flood to destroy all flesh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V16">
    16
  </span>
  The rainbow will be in the cloud. I will look at it, that I may remember the everlasting covenant between God and every living creature of all flesh that is on the earth.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V17">
    17
  </span>
  God said to Noah, “This is the token of the covenant which I have established between me and all flesh that is on the earth.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V18">
    18
  </span>
  The sons of Noah who went out from the ship were Shem, Ham, and Japheth. Ham is the father of Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V19">
    19
  </span>
  These three were the sons of Noah, and from these the whole earth was populated.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V20">
    20
  </span>
  Noah began to be a farmer, and planted a vineyard.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V21">
    21
  </span>
  He drank of the wine and got drunk. He was uncovered within his tent.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V22">
    22
  </span>
  Ham, the father of Canaan, saw the nakedness of his father, and told his two brothers outside.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V23">
    23
  </span>
  Shem and Japheth took a garment, and laid it on both their shoulders, went in backwards, and covered the nakedness of their father. Their faces were backwards, and they didn’t see their father’s nakedness.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V24">
    24
  </span>
  Noah awoke from his wine, and knew what his youngest son had done to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V25">
    25
  </span>
  He said,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “Canaan is cursed.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  He will be a servant of servants to his brothers.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V26">
    26
  </span>
  He said,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “Blessed be Yahweh, the God of Shem.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Let Canaan be his servant.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V27">
    27
  </span>
  May God enlarge Japheth.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Let him dwell in the tents of Shem.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Let Canaan be his servant.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V28">
    28
  </span>
  Noah lived three hundred fifty years after the flood.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN9V29">
    29
  </span>
  All the days of Noah were nine hundred fifty years, and then he died.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 10

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V1">
    1
  </span>
  Now this is the history of the generations of the sons of Noah and of Shem, Ham, and Japheth. Sons were born to them after the flood.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V2">
    2
  </span>
  The sons of Japheth were: Gomer, Magog, Madai, Javan, Tubal, Meshech, and Tiras.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V3">
    3
  </span>
  The sons of Gomer were: Ashkenaz, Riphath, and Togarmah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V4">
    4
  </span>
  The sons of Javan were: Elishah, Tarshish, Kittim, and Dodanim.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V5">
    5
  </span>
  Of these were the islands of the nations divided in their lands, everyone after his language, after their families, in their nations.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V6">
    6
  </span>
  The sons of Ham were: Cush, Mizraim, Put, and Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V7">
    7
  </span>
  The sons of Cush were: Seba, Havilah, Sabtah, Raamah, and Sabteca. The sons of Raamah were: Sheba and Dedan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V8">
    8
  </span>
  Cush became the father of Nimrod. He began to be a mighty one in the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V9">
    9
  </span>
  He was a mighty hunter before Yahweh. Therefore it is said, “like Nimrod, a mighty hunter before Yahweh”.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V10">
    10
  </span>
  The beginning of his kingdom was Babel, Erech, Accad, and Calneh, in the land of Shinar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V11">
    11
  </span>
  Out of that land he went into Assyria, and built Nineveh, Rehoboth Ir, Calah,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V12">
    12
  </span>
  and Resen between Nineveh and the great city Calah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V13">
    13
  </span>
  Mizraim became the father of Ludim, Anamim, Lehabim, Naphtuhim,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V14">
    14
  </span>
  Pathrusim, Casluhim (which the Philistines descended from), and Caphtorim.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V15">
    15
  </span>
  Canaan became the father of Sidon (his firstborn), Heth,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V16">
    16
  </span>
  the Jebusites, the Amorites, the Girgashites,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V17">
    17
  </span>
  the Hivites, the Arkites, the Sinites,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V18">
    18
  </span>
  the Arvadites, the Zemarites, and the Hamathites. Afterward the families of the Canaanites were spread abroad.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V19">
    19
  </span>
  The border of the Canaanites was from Sidon—as you go toward Gerar—to Gaza—as you go toward Sodom, Gomorrah, Admah, and Zeboiim—to Lasha.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V20">
    20
  </span>
  These are the sons of Ham, after their families, according to their languages, in their lands and their nations.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V21">
    21
  </span>
  Children were also born to Shem (the elder brother of Japheth), the father of all the children of Eber.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V22">
    22
  </span>
  The sons of Shem were: Elam, Asshur, Arpachshad, Lud, and Aram.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V23">
    23
  </span>
  The sons of Aram were: Uz, Hul, Gether, and Mash.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V24">
    24
  </span>
  Arpachshad became the father of Shelah. Shelah became the father of Eber.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V25">
    25
  </span>
  To Eber were born two sons. The name of the one was Peleg, for in his days the earth was divided. His brother’s name was Joktan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V26">
    26
  </span>
  Joktan became the father of Almodad, Sheleph, Hazarmaveth, Jerah,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V27">
    27
  </span>
  Hadoram, Uzal, Diklah,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V28">
    28
  </span>
  Obal, Abimael, Sheba,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V29">
    29
  </span>
  Ophir, Havilah, and Jobab. All these were the sons of Joktan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V30">
    30
  </span>
  Their dwelling extended from Mesha, as you go toward Sephar, the mountain of the east.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V31">
    31
  </span>
  These are the sons of Shem, by their families, according to their languages, lands, and nations.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN10V32">
    32
  </span>
  These are the families of the sons of Noah, by their generations, according to their nations. The nations divided from these in the earth after the flood.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 11

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V1">
    1
  </span>
  The whole earth was of one language and of one speech.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V2">
    2
  </span>
  As they traveled east,
  <a href="#GEN11FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      LXX reads “from the east”.
    </span>
  </a>
  they found a plain in the land of Shinar, and they lived there.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V3">
    3
  </span>
  They said to one another, “Come, let’s make bricks, and burn them thoroughly.” They had brick for stone, and they used tar for mortar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V4">
    4
  </span>
  They said, “Come, let’s build ourselves a city, and a tower whose top reaches to the sky, and let’s make a name for ourselves, lest we be scattered abroad on the surface of the whole earth.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V5">
    5
  </span>
  Yahweh came down to see the city and the tower, which the children of men built.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V6">
    6
  </span>
  Yahweh said, “Behold, they are one people, and they all have one language, and this is what they begin to do. Now nothing will be withheld from them, which they intend to do.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V7">
    7
  </span>
  Come, let’s go down, and there confuse their language, that they may not understand one another’s speech.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V8">
    8
  </span>
  So Yahweh scattered them abroad from there on the surface of all the earth. They stopped building the city.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V9">
    9
  </span>
  Therefore its name was called Babel, because there Yahweh confused the language of all the earth. From there, Yahweh scattered them abroad on the surface of all the earth.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V10">
    10
  </span>
  This is the history of the generations of Shem: Shem was one hundred years old when he became the father of Arpachshad two years after the flood.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V11">
    11
  </span>
  Shem lived five hundred years after he became the father of Arpachshad, and became the father of more sons and daughters.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V12">
    12
  </span>
  Arpachshad lived thirty-five years and became the father of Shelah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V13">
    13
  </span>
  Arpachshad lived four hundred three years after he became the father of Shelah, and became the father of more sons and daughters.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V14">
    14
  </span>
  Shelah lived thirty years, and became the father of Eber.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V15">
    15
  </span>
  Shelah lived four hundred three years after he became the father of Eber, and became the father of more sons and daughters.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V16">
    16
  </span>
  Eber lived thirty-four years, and became the father of Peleg.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V17">
    17
  </span>
  Eber lived four hundred thirty years after he became the father of Peleg, and became the father of more sons and daughters.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V18">
    18
  </span>
  Peleg lived thirty years, and became the father of Reu.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V19">
    19
  </span>
  Peleg lived two hundred nine years after he became the father of Reu, and became the father of more sons and daughters.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V20">
    20
  </span>
  Reu lived thirty-two years, and became the father of Serug.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V21">
    21
  </span>
  Reu lived two hundred seven years after he became the father of Serug, and became the father of more sons and daughters.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V22">
    22
  </span>
  Serug lived thirty years, and became the father of Nahor.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V23">
    23
  </span>
  Serug lived two hundred years after he became the father of Nahor, and became the father of more sons and daughters.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V24">
    24
  </span>
  Nahor lived twenty-nine years, and became the father of Terah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V25">
    25
  </span>
  Nahor lived one hundred nineteen years after he became the father of Terah, and became the father of more sons and daughters.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V26">
    26
  </span>
  Terah lived seventy years, and became the father of Abram, Nahor, and Haran.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V27">
    27
  </span>
  Now this is the history of the generations of Terah. Terah became the father of Abram, Nahor, and Haran. Haran became the father of Lot.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V28">
    28
  </span>
  Haran died in the land of his birth, in Ur of the Chaldees, while his father Terah was still alive.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V29">
    29
  </span>
  Abram and Nahor married wives. The name of Abram’s wife was Sarai, and the name of Nahor’s wife was Milcah, the daughter of Haran, who was also the father of Iscah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V30">
    30
  </span>
  Sarai was barren. She had no child.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V31">
    31
  </span>
  Terah took Abram his son, Lot the son of Haran, his son’s son, and Sarai his daughter-in-law, his son Abram’s wife. They went from Ur of the Chaldees, to go into the land of Canaan. They came to Haran and lived there.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN11V32">
    32
  </span>
  The days of Terah were two hundred five years. Terah died in Haran.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN11FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN11V2">
      11:2
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      LXX reads “from the east”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 12

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V1">
    1
  </span>
  Now Yahweh said to Abram, “Leave your country, and your relatives, and your father’s house, and go to the land that I will show you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V2">
    2
  </span>
  I will make of you a great nation. I will bless you and make your name great. You will be a blessing.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V3">
    3
  </span>
  I will bless those who bless you, and I will curse him who treats you with contempt. All the families of the earth will be blessed through you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V4">
    4
  </span>
  So Abram went, as Yahweh had told him. Lot went with him. Abram was seventy-five years old when he departed from Haran.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V5">
    5
  </span>
  Abram took Sarai his wife, Lot his brother’s son, all their possessions that they had gathered, and the people whom they had acquired in Haran, and they went to go into the land of Canaan. They entered into the land of Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V6">
    6
  </span>
  Abram passed through the land to the place of Shechem, to the oak of Moreh. At that time, Canaanites were in the land.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V7">
    7
  </span>
  Yahweh appeared to Abram and said, “I will give this land to your offspring.”
  <a href="#GEN12FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      or, seed
    </span>
  </a>
</div>
<div class="p">
  He built an altar there to Yahweh, who had appeared to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V8">
    8
  </span>
  He left from there to go to the mountain on the east of Bethel and pitched his tent, having Bethel on the west, and Ai on the east. There he built an altar to Yahweh and called on Yahweh’s name.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V9">
    9
  </span>
  Abram traveled, still going on toward the South.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V10">
    10
  </span>
  There was a famine in the land. Abram went down into Egypt to live as a foreigner there, for the famine was severe in the land.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V11">
    11
  </span>
  When he had come near to enter Egypt, he said to Sarai his wife, “See now, I know that you are a beautiful woman to look at.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V12">
    12
  </span>
  It will happen that when the Egyptians see you, they will say, ‘This is his wife.’ They will kill me, but they will save you alive.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V13">
    13
  </span>
  Please say that you are my sister, that it may be well with me for your sake, and that my soul may live because of you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V14">
    14
  </span>
  When Abram had come into Egypt, Egyptians saw that the woman was very beautiful.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V15">
    15
  </span>
  The princes of Pharaoh saw her, and praised her to Pharaoh; and the woman was taken into Pharaoh’s house.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V16">
    16
  </span>
  He dealt well with Abram for her sake. He had sheep, cattle, male donkeys, male servants, female servants, female donkeys, and camels.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V17">
    17
  </span>
  Yahweh afflicted Pharaoh and his house with great plagues because of Sarai, Abram’s wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V18">
    18
  </span>
  Pharaoh called Abram and said, “What is this that you have done to me? Why didn’t you tell me that she was your wife?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V19">
    19
  </span>
  Why did you say, ‘She is my sister,’ so that I took her to be my wife? Now therefore, see your wife, take her, and go your way.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN12V20">
    20
  </span>
  Pharaoh commanded men concerning him, and they escorted him away with his wife and all that he had.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN12FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN12V7">
      12:7
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      or, seed
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 13

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V1">
    1
  </span>
  Abram went up out of Egypt—he, his wife, all that he had, and Lot with him—into the South.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V2">
    2
  </span>
  Abram was very rich in livestock, in silver, and in gold.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V3">
    3
  </span>
  He went on his journeys from the South as far as Bethel, to the place where his tent had been at the beginning, between Bethel and Ai,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V4">
    4
  </span>
  to the place of the altar, which he had made there at the first. There Abram called on Yahweh’s name.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V5">
    5
  </span>
  Lot also, who went with Abram, had flocks, herds, and tents.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V6">
    6
  </span>
  The land was not able to bear them, that they might live together; for their possessions were so great that they couldn’t live together.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V7">
    7
  </span>
  There was strife between the herdsmen of Abram’s livestock and the herdsmen of Lot’s livestock. The Canaanites and the Perizzites lived in the land at that time.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V8">
    8
  </span>
  Abram said to Lot, “Please, let there be no strife between you and me, and between your herdsmen and my herdsmen; for we are relatives.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V9">
    9
  </span>
  Isn’t the whole land before you? Please separate yourself from me. If you go to the left hand, then I will go to the right. Or if you go to the right hand, then I will go to the left.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V10">
    10
  </span>
  Lot lifted up his eyes, and saw all the plain of the Jordan, that it was well-watered everywhere, before Yahweh destroyed Sodom and Gomorrah, like the garden of Yahweh, like the land of Egypt, as you go to Zoar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V11">
    11
  </span>
  So Lot chose the Plain of the Jordan for himself. Lot traveled east, and they separated themselves from one other.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V12">
    12
  </span>
  Abram lived in the land of Canaan, and Lot lived in the cities of the plain, and moved his tent as far as Sodom.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V13">
    13
  </span>
  Now the men of Sodom were exceedingly wicked and sinners against Yahweh.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V14">
    14
  </span>
  Yahweh said to Abram, after Lot was separated from him, “Now, lift up your eyes, and look from the place where you are, northward and southward and eastward and westward,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V15">
    15
  </span>
  for I will give all the land which you see to you and to your offspring forever.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V16">
    16
  </span>
  I will make your offspring as the dust of the earth, so that if a man can count the dust of the earth, then your offspring may also be counted.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V17">
    17
  </span>
  Arise, walk through the land in its length and in its width; for I will give it to you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN13V18">
    18
  </span>
  Abram moved his tent, and came and lived by the oaks of Mamre, which are in Hebron, and built an altar there to Yahweh.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 14

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V1">
    1
  </span>
  In the days of Amraphel, king of Shinar; Arioch, king of Ellasar; Chedorlaomer, king of Elam; and Tidal, king of Goiim,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V2">
    2
  </span>
  they made war with Bera, king of Sodom; Birsha, king of Gomorrah; Shinab, king of Admah; Shemeber, king of Zeboiim; and the king of Bela (also called Zoar).
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V3">
    3
  </span>
  All these joined together in the valley of Siddim (also called the Salt Sea).
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V4">
    4
  </span>
  They served Chedorlaomer for twelve years, and in the thirteenth year they rebelled.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V5">
    5
  </span>
  In the fourteenth year Chedorlaomer and the kings who were with him came and struck the Rephaim in Ashteroth Karnaim, the Zuzim in Ham, the Emim in Shaveh Kiriathaim,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V6">
    6
  </span>
  and the Horites in their Mount Seir, to El Paran, which is by the wilderness.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V7">
    7
  </span>
  They returned, and came to En Mishpat (also called Kadesh), and struck all the country of the Amalekites, and also the Amorites, that lived in Hazazon Tamar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V8">
    8
  </span>
  The king of Sodom, and the king of Gomorrah, the king of Admah, the king of Zeboiim, and the king of Bela (also called Zoar) went out; and they set the battle in array against them in the valley of Siddim
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V9">
    9
  </span>
  against Chedorlaomer king of Elam, Tidal king of Goiim, Amraphel king of Shinar, and Arioch king of Ellasar; four kings against the five.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V10">
    10
  </span>
  Now the valley of Siddim was full of tar pits; and the kings of Sodom and Gomorrah fled, and some fell there. Those who remained fled to the hills.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V11">
    11
  </span>
  They took all the goods of Sodom and Gomorrah, and all their food, and went their way.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V12">
    12
  </span>
  They took Lot, Abram’s brother’s son, who lived in Sodom, and his goods, and departed.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V13">
    13
  </span>
  One who had escaped came and told Abram, the Hebrew. At that time, he lived by the oaks of Mamre, the Amorite, brother of Eshcol and brother of Aner. They were allies of Abram.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V14">
    14
  </span>
  When Abram heard that his relative was taken captive, he led out his three hundred eighteen trained men, born in his house, and pursued as far as Dan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V15">
    15
  </span>
  He divided himself against them by night, he and his servants, and struck them, and pursued them to Hobah, which is on the left hand of Damascus.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V16">
    16
  </span>
  He brought back all the goods, and also brought back his relative Lot and his goods, and the women also, and the other people.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V17">
    17
  </span>
  The king of Sodom went out to meet him after his return from the slaughter of Chedorlaomer and the kings who were with him, at the valley of Shaveh (that is, the King’s Valley).
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V18">
    18
  </span>
  Melchizedek king of Salem brought out bread and wine. He was priest of God Most High.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V19">
    19
  </span>
  He blessed him, and said, “Blessed be Abram of God Most High, possessor of heaven and earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V20">
    20
  </span>
  Blessed be God Most High, who has delivered your enemies into your hand.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Abram gave him a tenth of all.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V21">
    21
  </span>
  The king of Sodom said to Abram, “Give me the people, and take the goods for yourself.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V22">
    22
  </span>
  Abram said to the king of Sodom, “I have lifted up my hand to Yahweh, God Most High, possessor of heaven and earth,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V23">
    23
  </span>
  that I will not take a thread nor a sandal strap nor anything that is yours, lest you should say, ‘I have made Abram rich.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN14V24">
    24
  </span>
  I will accept nothing from you except that which the young men have eaten, and the portion of the men who went with me: Aner, Eshcol, and Mamre. Let them take their portion.”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 15

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V1">
    1
  </span>
  After these things Yahweh’s word came to Abram in a vision, saying, “Don’t be afraid, Abram. I am your shield, your exceedingly great reward.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V2">
    2
  </span>
  Abram said, “Lord
  <a href="#GEN15FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      The word translated “Lord” is “Adonai”.
    </span>
  </a>
  Yahweh, what will you give me, since I go childless, and he who will inherit my estate is Eliezer of Damascus?”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V3">
    3
  </span>
  Abram said, “Behold, you have given no children to me: and, behold, one born in my house is my heir.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V4">
    4
  </span>
  Behold, Yahweh’s word came to him, saying, “This man will not be your heir, but he who will come out of your own body will be your heir.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V5">
    5
  </span>
  Yahweh brought him outside, and said, “Look now toward the sky, and count the stars, if you are able to count them.” He said to Abram, “So your offspring will be.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V6">
    6
  </span>
  He believed in Yahweh, who credited it to him for righteousness.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V7">
    7
  </span>
  He said to Abram, “I am Yahweh who brought you out of Ur of the Chaldees, to give you this land to inherit it.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V8">
    8
  </span>
  He said, “Lord Yahweh, how will I know that I will inherit it?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V9">
    9
  </span>
  He said to him, “Bring me a heifer three years old, a female goat three years old, a ram three years old, a turtledove, and a young pigeon.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V10">
    10
  </span>
  He brought him all these, and divided them in the middle, and laid each half opposite the other; but he didn’t divide the birds.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V11">
    11
  </span>
  The birds of prey came down on the carcasses, and Abram drove them away.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V12">
    12
  </span>
  When the sun was going down, a deep sleep fell on Abram. Now terror and great darkness fell on him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V13">
    13
  </span>
  He said to Abram, “Know for sure that your offspring will live as foreigners in a land that is not theirs, and will serve them. They will afflict them four hundred years.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V14">
    14
  </span>
  I will also judge that nation, whom they will serve. Afterward they will come out with great wealth;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V15">
    15
  </span>
  but you will go to your fathers in peace. You will be buried at a good old age.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V16">
    16
  </span>
  In the fourth generation they will come here again, for the iniquity of the Amorite is not yet full.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V17">
    17
  </span>
  It came to pass that, when the sun went down, and it was dark, behold, a smoking furnace and a flaming torch passed between these pieces.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V18">
    18
  </span>
  In that day Yahweh made a covenant with Abram, saying, “I have given this land to your offspring, from the river of Egypt to the great river, the river Euphrates:
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V19">
    19
  </span>
  the land of the Kenites, the Kenizzites, the Kadmonites,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V20">
    20
  </span>
  the Hittites, the Perizzites, the Rephaim,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN15V21">
    21
  </span>
  the Amorites, the Canaanites, the Girgashites, and the Jebusites.”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN15FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN15V2">
      15:2
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      The word translated “Lord” is “Adonai”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 16

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V1">
    1
  </span>
  Now Sarai, Abram’s wife, bore him no children. She had a servant, an Egyptian, whose name was Hagar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V2">
    2
  </span>
  Sarai said to Abram, “See now, Yahweh has restrained me from bearing. Please go in to my servant. It may be that I will obtain children by her.” Abram listened to the voice of Sarai.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V3">
    3
  </span>
  Sarai, Abram’s wife, took Hagar the Egyptian, her servant, after Abram had lived ten years in the land of Canaan, and gave her to Abram her husband to be his wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V4">
    4
  </span>
  He went in to Hagar, and she conceived. When she saw that she had conceived, her mistress was despised in her eyes.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V5">
    5
  </span>
  Sarai said to Abram, “This wrong is your fault. I gave my servant into your bosom, and when she saw that she had conceived, she despised me. May Yahweh judge between me and you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V6">
    6
  </span>
  But Abram said to Sarai, “Behold, your maid is in your hand. Do to her whatever is good in your eyes.” Sarai dealt harshly with her, and she fled from her face.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V7">
    7
  </span>
  Yahweh’s angel found her by a fountain of water in the wilderness, by the fountain on the way to Shur.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V8">
    8
  </span>
  He said, “Hagar, Sarai’s servant, where did you come from? Where are you going?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  She said, “I am fleeing from the face of my mistress Sarai.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V9">
    9
  </span>
  Yahweh’s angel said to her, “Return to your mistress, and submit yourself under her hands.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V10">
    10
  </span>
  Yahweh’s angel said to her, “I will greatly multiply your offspring, that they will not be counted for multitude.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V11">
    11
  </span>
  Yahweh’s angel said to her, “Behold, you are with child, and will bear a son. You shall call his name Ishmael, because Yahweh has heard your affliction.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V12">
    12
  </span>
  He will be like a wild donkey among men. His hand will be against every man, and every man’s hand against him. He will live opposed to all of his brothers.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V13">
    13
  </span>
  She called the name of Yahweh who spoke to her, “You are a God who sees,” for she said, “Have I even stayed alive after seeing him?”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V14">
    14
  </span>
  Therefore the well was called Beer Lahai Roi.
  <a href="#GEN16FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Beer Lahai Roi means “well of the one who lives and sees me”.
    </span>
  </a>
  Behold, it is between Kadesh and Bered.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V15">
    15
  </span>
  Hagar bore a son for Abram. Abram called the name of his son, whom Hagar bore, Ishmael.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN16V16">
    16
  </span>
  Abram was eighty-six years old when Hagar bore Ishmael to Abram.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN16FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN16V14">
      16:14
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Beer Lahai Roi means “well of the one who lives and sees me”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 17

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V1">
    1
  </span>
  When Abram was ninety-nine years old, Yahweh appeared to Abram and said to him, “I am God Almighty. Walk before me and be blameless.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V2">
    2
  </span>
  I will make my covenant between me and you, and will multiply you exceedingly.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V3">
    3
  </span>
  Abram fell on his face. God talked with him, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V4">
    4
  </span>
  “As for me, behold, my covenant is with you. You will be the father of a multitude of nations.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V5">
    5
  </span>
  Your name will no more be called Abram, but your name will be Abraham; for I have made you the father of a multitude of nations.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V6">
    6
  </span>
  I will make you exceedingly fruitful, and I will make nations of you. Kings will come out of you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V7">
    7
  </span>
  I will establish my covenant between me and you and your offspring after you throughout their generations for an everlasting covenant, to be a God to you and to your offspring after you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V8">
    8
  </span>
  I will give to you, and to your offspring after you, the land where you are traveling, all the land of Canaan, for an everlasting possession. I will be their God.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V9">
    9
  </span>
  God said to Abraham, “As for you, you shall keep my covenant, you and your offspring after you throughout their generations.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V10">
    10
  </span>
  This is my covenant, which you shall keep, between me and you and your offspring after you. Every male among you shall be circumcised.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V11">
    11
  </span>
  You shall be circumcised in the flesh of your foreskin. It will be a token of the covenant between me and you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V12">
    12
  </span>
  He who is eight days old shall be circumcised among you, every male throughout your generations, he who is born in the house, or bought with money from any foreigner who is not of your offspring.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V13">
    13
  </span>
  He who is born in your house, and he who is bought with your money, must be circumcised. My covenant shall be in your flesh for an everlasting covenant.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V14">
    14
  </span>
  The uncircumcised male who is not circumcised in the flesh of his foreskin, that soul shall be cut off from his people. He has broken my covenant.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V15">
    15
  </span>
