  God said to Abraham, “As for Sarai your wife, you shall not call her name Sarai, but her name shall be Sarah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V16">
    16
  </span>
  I will bless her, and moreover I will give you a son by her. Yes, I will bless her, and she will be a mother of nations. Kings of peoples will come from her.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V17">
    17
  </span>
  Then Abraham fell on his face, and laughed, and said in his heart, “Will a child be born to him who is one hundred years old? Will Sarah, who is ninety years old, give birth?”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V18">
    18
  </span>
  Abraham said to God, “Oh that Ishmael might live before you!”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V19">
    19
  </span>
  God said, “No, but Sarah, your wife, will bear you a son. You shall call his name Isaac.
  <a href="#GEN17FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Isaac means “he laughs”.
    </span>
  </a>
  I will establish my covenant with him for an everlasting covenant for his offspring after him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V20">
    20
  </span>
  As for Ishmael, I have heard you. Behold, I have blessed him, and will make him fruitful, and will multiply him exceedingly. He will become the father of twelve princes, and I will make him a great nation.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V21">
    21
  </span>
  But I will establish my covenant with Isaac, whom Sarah will bear to you at this set time next year.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V22">
    22
  </span>
  When he finished talking with him, God went up from Abraham.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V23">
    23
  </span>
  Abraham took Ishmael his son, all who were born in his house, and all who were bought with his money: every male among the men of Abraham’s house, and circumcised the flesh of their foreskin in the same day, as God had said to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V24">
    24
  </span>
  Abraham was ninety-nine years old when he was circumcised in the flesh of his foreskin.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V25">
    25
  </span>
  Ishmael, his son, was thirteen years old when he was circumcised in the flesh of his foreskin.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V26">
    26
  </span>
  In the same day both Abraham and Ishmael, his son, were circumcised.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN17V27">
    27
  </span>
  All the men of his house, those born in the house, and those bought with money from a foreigner, were circumcised with him.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN17FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN17V19">
      17:19
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Isaac means “he laughs”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 18

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V1">
    1
  </span>
  Yahweh appeared to him by the oaks of Mamre, as he sat in the tent door in the heat of the day.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V2">
    2
  </span>
  He lifted up his eyes and looked, and saw that three men stood near him. When he saw them, he ran to meet them from the tent door, and bowed himself to the earth,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V3">
    3
  </span>
  and said, “My lord, if now I have found favor in your sight, please don’t go away from your servant.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V4">
    4
  </span>
  Now let a little water be fetched, wash your feet, and rest yourselves under the tree.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V5">
    5
  </span>
  I will get a piece of bread so you can refresh your heart. After that you may go your way, now that you have come to your servant.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They said, “Very well, do as you have said.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V6">
    6
  </span>
  Abraham hurried into the tent to Sarah, and said, “Quickly prepare three seahs
  <a href="#GEN18FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      1 seah is about 7 liters or 1.9 gallons or 0.8 pecks
    </span>
  </a>
  of fine meal, knead it, and make cakes.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V7">
    7
  </span>
  Abraham ran to the herd, and fetched a tender and good calf, and gave it to the servant. He hurried to dress it.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V8">
    8
  </span>
  He took butter, milk, and the calf which he had dressed, and set it before them. He stood by them under the tree, and they ate.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V9">
    9
  </span>
  They asked him, “Where is Sarah, your wife?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “There, in the tent.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V10">
    10
  </span>
  He said, “I will certainly return to you at about this time next year; and behold, Sarah your wife will have a son.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Sarah heard in the tent door, which was behind him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V11">
    11
  </span>
  Now Abraham and Sarah were old, well advanced in age. Sarah had passed the age of childbearing.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V12">
    12
  </span>
  Sarah laughed within herself, saying, “After I have grown old will I have pleasure, my lord being old also?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V13">
    13
  </span>
  Yahweh said to Abraham, “Why did Sarah laugh, saying, ‘Will I really bear a child when I am old?’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V14">
    14
  </span>
  Is anything too hard for Yahweh? At the set time I will return to you, when the season comes around, and Sarah will have a son.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V15">
    15
  </span>
  Then Sarah denied it, saying, “I didn’t laugh,” for she was afraid.
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “No, but you did laugh.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V16">
    16
  </span>
  The men rose up from there, and looked toward Sodom. Abraham went with them to see them on their way.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V17">
    17
  </span>
  Yahweh said, “Will I hide from Abraham what I do,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V18">
    18
  </span>
  since Abraham will surely become a great and mighty nation, and all the nations of the earth will be blessed in him?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V19">
    19
  </span>
  For I have known him, to the end that he may command his children and his household after him, that they may keep the way of Yahweh, to do righteousness and justice; to the end that Yahweh may bring on Abraham that which he has spoken of him.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V20">
    20
  </span>
  Yahweh said, “Because the cry of Sodom and Gomorrah is great, and because their sin is very grievous,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V21">
    21
  </span>
  I will go down now, and see whether their deeds are as bad as the reports which have come to me. If not, I will know.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V22">
    22
  </span>
  The men turned from there, and went toward Sodom, but Abraham stood yet before Yahweh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V23">
    23
  </span>
  Abraham came near, and said, “Will you consume the righteous with the wicked?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V24">
    24
  </span>
  What if there are fifty righteous within the city? Will you consume and not spare the place for the fifty righteous who are in it?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V25">
    25
  </span>
  May it be far from you to do things like that, to kill the righteous with the wicked, so that the righteous should be like the wicked. May that be far from you. Shouldn’t the Judge of all the earth do right?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V26">
    26
  </span>
  Yahweh said, “If I find in Sodom fifty righteous within the city, then I will spare the whole place for their sake.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V27">
    27
  </span>
  Abraham answered, “See now, I have taken it on myself to speak to the Lord, although I am dust and ashes.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V28">
    28
  </span>
  What if there will lack five of the fifty righteous? Will you destroy all the city for lack of five?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “I will not destroy it if I find forty-five there.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V29">
    29
  </span>
  He spoke to him yet again, and said, “What if there are forty found there?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “I will not do it for the forty’s sake.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V30">
    30
  </span>
  He said, “Oh don’t let the Lord be angry, and I will speak. What if there are thirty found there?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “I will not do it if I find thirty there.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V31">
    31
  </span>
  He said, “See now, I have taken it on myself to speak to the Lord. What if there are twenty found there?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “I will not destroy it for the twenty’s sake.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V32">
    32
  </span>
  He said, “Oh don’t let the Lord be angry, and I will speak just once more. What if ten are found there?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “I will not destroy it for the ten’s sake.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN18V33">
    33
  </span>
  Yahweh went his way as soon as he had finished communing with Abraham, and Abraham returned to his place.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN18FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN18V6">
      18:6
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      1 seah is about 7 liters or 1.9 gallons or 0.8 pecks
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 19

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V1">
    1
  </span>
  The two angels came to Sodom at evening. Lot sat in the gate of Sodom. Lot saw them, and rose up to meet them. He bowed himself with his face to the earth,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V2">
    2
  </span>
  and he said, “See now, my lords, please come into your servant’s house, stay all night, wash your feet, and you can rise up early, and go on your way.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They said, “No, but we will stay in the street all night.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V3">
    3
  </span>
  He urged them greatly, and they came in with him, and entered into his house. He made them a feast, and baked unleavened bread, and they ate.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V4">
    4
  </span>
  But before they lay down, the men of the city, the men of Sodom, surrounded the house, both young and old, all the people from every quarter.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V5">
    5
  </span>
  They called to Lot, and said to him, “Where are the men who came in to you this night? Bring them out to us, that we may have sex with them.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V6">
    6
  </span>
  Lot went out to them through the door, and shut the door after himself.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V7">
    7
  </span>
  He said, “Please, my brothers, don’t act so wickedly.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V8">
    8
  </span>
  See now, I have two virgin daughters. Please let me bring them out to you, and you may do to them what seems good to you. Only don’t do anything to these men, because they have come under the shadow of my roof.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V9">
    9
  </span>
  They said, “Stand back!” Then they said, “This one fellow came in to live as a foreigner, and he appoints himself a judge. Now we will deal worse with you than with them!” They pressed hard on the man Lot, and came near to break the door.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V10">
    10
  </span>
  But the men reached out their hand, and brought Lot into the house to them, and shut the door.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V11">
    11
  </span>
  They struck the men who were at the door of the house with blindness, both small and great, so that they wearied themselves to find the door.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V12">
    12
  </span>
  The men said to Lot, “Do you have anybody else here? Sons-in-law, your sons, your daughters, and whomever you have in the city, bring them out of the place:
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V13">
    13
  </span>
  for we will destroy this place, because the outcry against them has grown so great before Yahweh that Yahweh has sent us to destroy it.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V14">
    14
  </span>
  Lot went out, and spoke to his sons-in-law, who were pledged to marry his daughters, and said, “Get up! Get out of this place, for Yahweh will destroy the city!”
</div>
<div class="p">
  But he seemed to his sons-in-law to be joking.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V15">
    15
  </span>
  When the morning came, then the angels hurried Lot, saying, “Get up! Take your wife and your two daughters who are here, lest you be consumed in the iniquity of the city.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V16">
    16
  </span>
  But he lingered; and the men grabbed his hand, his wife’s hand, and his two daughters’ hands, Yahweh being merciful to him; and they took him out, and set him outside of the city.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V17">
    17
  </span>
  It came to pass, when they had taken them out, that he said, “Escape for your life! Don’t look behind you, and don’t stay anywhere in the plain. Escape to the mountains, lest you be consumed!”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V18">
    18
  </span>
  Lot said to them, “Oh, not so, my lord.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V19">
    19
  </span>
  See now, your servant has found favor in your sight, and you have magnified your loving kindness, which you have shown to me in saving my life. I can’t escape to the mountain, lest evil overtake me, and I die.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V20">
    20
  </span>
  See now, this city is near to flee to, and it is a little one. Oh let me escape there (isn’t it a little one?), and my soul will live.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V21">
    21
  </span>
  He said to him, “Behold, I have granted your request concerning this thing also, that I will not overthrow the city of which you have spoken.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V22">
    22
  </span>
  Hurry, escape there, for I can’t do anything until you get there.” Therefore the name of the city was called Zoar.
  <a href="#GEN19FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Zoar means “little”.
    </span>
  </a>
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V23">
    23
  </span>
  The sun had risen on the earth when Lot came to Zoar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V24">
    24
  </span>
  Then Yahweh rained on Sodom and on Gomorrah sulfur and fire from Yahweh out of the sky.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V25">
    25
  </span>
  He overthrew those cities, all the plain, all the inhabitants of the cities, and that which grew on the ground.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V26">
    26
  </span>
  But Lot’s wife looked back from behind him, and she became a pillar of salt.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V27">
    27
  </span>
  Abraham went up early in the morning to the place where he had stood before Yahweh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V28">
    28
  </span>
  He looked toward Sodom and Gomorrah, and toward all the land of the plain, and saw that the smoke of the land went up as the smoke of a furnace.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V29">
    29
  </span>
  When God destroyed the cities of the plain, God remembered Abraham, and sent Lot out of the middle of the overthrow, when he overthrew the cities in which Lot lived.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V30">
    30
  </span>
  Lot went up out of Zoar, and lived in the mountain, and his two daughters with him; for he was afraid to live in Zoar. He lived in a cave with his two daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V31">
    31
  </span>
  The firstborn said to the younger, “Our father is old, and there is not a man in the earth to come in to us in the way of all the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V32">
    32
  </span>
  Come, let’s make our father drink wine, and we will lie with him, that we may preserve our father’s family line.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V33">
    33
  </span>
  They made their father drink wine that night: and the firstborn went in, and lay with her father. He didn’t know when she lay down, nor when she arose.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V34">
    34
  </span>
  It came to pass on the next day, that the firstborn said to the younger, “Behold, I lay last night with my father. Let’s make him drink wine again tonight. You go in, and lie with him, that we may preserve our father’s family line.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V35">
    35
  </span>
  They made their father drink wine that night also. The younger went and lay with him. He didn’t know when she lay down, nor when she got up.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V36">
    36
  </span>
  Thus both of Lot’s daughters were with child by their father.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V37">
    37
  </span>
  The firstborn bore a son, and named him Moab. He is the father of the Moabites to this day.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN19V38">
    38
  </span>
  The younger also bore a son, and called his name Ben Ammi. He is the father of the children of Ammon to this day.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN19FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN19V22">
      19:22
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Zoar means “little”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 20

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V1">
    1
  </span>
  Abraham traveled from there toward the land of the South, and lived between Kadesh and Shur. He lived as a foreigner in Gerar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V2">
    2
  </span>
  Abraham said about Sarah his wife, “She is my sister.” Abimelech king of Gerar sent, and took Sarah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V3">
    3
  </span>
  But God came to Abimelech in a dream of the night, and said to him, “Behold, you are a dead man, because of the woman whom you have taken; for she is a man’s wife.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V4">
    4
  </span>
  Now Abimelech had not come near her. He said, “Lord, will you kill even a righteous nation?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V5">
    5
  </span>
  Didn’t he tell me, ‘She is my sister’? She, even she herself, said, ‘He is my brother.’ I have done this in the integrity of my heart and the innocence of my hands.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V6">
    6
  </span>
  God said to him in the dream, “Yes, I know that in the integrity of your heart you have done this, and I also withheld you from sinning against me. Therefore I didn’t allow you to touch her.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V7">
    7
  </span>
  Now therefore, restore the man’s wife. For he is a prophet, and he will pray for you, and you will live. If you don’t restore her, know for sure that you will die, you, and all who are yours.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V8">
    8
  </span>
  Abimelech rose early in the morning, and called all his servants, and told all these things in their ear. The men were very scared.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V9">
    9
  </span>
  Then Abimelech called Abraham, and said to him, “What have you done to us? How have I sinned against you, that you have brought on me and on my kingdom a great sin? You have done deeds to me that ought not to be done!”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V10">
    10
  </span>
  Abimelech said to Abraham, “What did you see, that you have done this thing?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V11">
    11
  </span>
  Abraham said, “Because I thought, ‘Surely the fear of God is not in this place. They will kill me for my wife’s sake.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V12">
    12
  </span>
  Besides, she is indeed my sister, the daughter of my father, but not the daughter of my mother; and she became my wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V13">
    13
  </span>
  When God caused me to wander from my father’s house, I said to her, ‘This is your kindness which you shall show to me. Everywhere that we go, say of me, “He is my brother.” ’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V14">
    14
  </span>
  Abimelech took sheep and cattle, male servants and female servants, and gave them to Abraham, and restored Sarah, his wife, to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V15">
    15
  </span>
  Abimelech said, “Behold, my land is before you. Dwell where it pleases you.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V16">
    16
  </span>
  To Sarah he said, “Behold, I have given your brother a thousand pieces of silver. Behold, it is for you a covering of the eyes to all that are with you. In front of all you are vindicated.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V17">
    17
  </span>
  Abraham prayed to God. So God healed Abimelech, his wife, and his female servants, and they bore children.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN20V18">
    18
  </span>
  For Yahweh had closed up tight all the wombs of the house of Abimelech, because of Sarah, Abraham’s wife.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 21

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V1">
    1
  </span>
  Yahweh visited Sarah as he had said, and Yahweh did to Sarah as he had spoken.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V2">
    2
  </span>
  Sarah conceived, and bore Abraham a son in his old age, at the set time of which God had spoken to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V3">
    3
  </span>
  Abraham called his son who was born to him, whom Sarah bore to him, Isaac.
  <a href="#GEN21FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Isaac means “He laughs”.
    </span>
  </a>
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V4">
    4
  </span>
  Abraham circumcised his son, Isaac, when he was eight days old, as God had commanded him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V5">
    5
  </span>
  Abraham was one hundred years old when his son, Isaac, was born to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V6">
    6
  </span>
  Sarah said, “God has made me laugh. Everyone who hears will laugh with me.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V7">
    7
  </span>
  She said, “Who would have said to Abraham that Sarah would nurse children? For I have borne him a son in his old age.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V8">
    8
  </span>
  The child grew and was weaned. Abraham made a great feast on the day that Isaac was weaned.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V9">
    9
  </span>
  Sarah saw the son of Hagar the Egyptian, whom she had borne to Abraham, mocking.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V10">
    10
  </span>
  Therefore she said to Abraham, “Cast out this servant and her son! For the son of this servant will not be heir with my son, Isaac.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V11">
    11
  </span>
  The thing was very grievous in Abraham’s sight on account of his son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V12">
    12
  </span>
  God said to Abraham, “Don’t let it be grievous in your sight because of the boy, and because of your servant. In all that Sarah says to you, listen to her voice. For your offspring will be named through Isaac.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V13">
    13
  </span>
  I will also make a nation of the son of the servant, because he is your child.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V14">
    14
  </span>
  Abraham rose up early in the morning, and took bread and a container of water, and gave it to Hagar, putting it on her shoulder; and gave her the child, and sent her away. She departed, and wandered in the wilderness of Beersheba.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V15">
    15
  </span>
  The water in the container was spent, and she put the child under one of the shrubs.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V16">
    16
  </span>
  She went and sat down opposite him, a good way off, about a bow shot away. For she said, “Don’t let me see the death of the child.” She sat opposite him, and lifted up her voice, and wept.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V17">
    17
  </span>
  God heard the voice of the boy.
</div>
<div class="p">
  The angel of God called to Hagar out of the sky, and said to her, “What troubles you, Hagar? Don’t be afraid. For God has heard the voice of the boy where he is.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V18">
    18
  </span>
  Get up, lift up the boy, and hold him with your hand. For I will make him a great nation.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V19">
    19
  </span>
  God opened her eyes, and she saw a well of water. She went, filled the container with water, and gave the boy a drink.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V20">
    20
  </span>
  God was with the boy, and he grew. He lived in the wilderness, and as he grew up, he became an archer.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V21">
    21
  </span>
  He lived in the wilderness of Paran. His mother got a wife for him out of the land of Egypt.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V22">
    22
  </span>
  At that time, Abimelech and Phicol the captain of his army spoke to Abraham, saying, “God is with you in all that you do.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V23">
    23
  </span>
  Now, therefore, swear to me here by God that you will not deal falsely with me, nor with my son, nor with my son’s son. But according to the kindness that I have done to you, you shall do to me, and to the land in which you have lived as a foreigner.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V24">
    24
  </span>
  Abraham said, “I will swear.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V25">
    25
  </span>
  Abraham complained to Abimelech because of a water well, which Abimelech’s servants had violently taken away.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V26">
    26
  </span>
  Abimelech said, “I don’t know who has done this thing. You didn’t tell me, and I didn’t hear of it until today.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V27">
    27
  </span>
  Abraham took sheep and cattle, and gave them to Abimelech. Those two made a covenant.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V28">
    28
  </span>
  Abraham set seven ewe lambs of the flock by themselves.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V29">
    29
  </span>
  Abimelech said to Abraham, “What do these seven ewe lambs, which you have set by themselves, mean?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V30">
    30
  </span>
  He said, “You shall take these seven ewe lambs from my hand, that it may be a witness to me, that I have dug this well.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V31">
    31
  </span>
  Therefore he called that place Beersheba,
  <a href="#GEN21FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      Beersheba can mean “well of the oath” or “well of seven”.
    </span>
  </a>
  because they both swore an oath there.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V32">
    32
  </span>
  So they made a covenant at Beersheba. Abimelech rose up with Phicol, the captain of his army, and they returned into the land of the Philistines.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V33">
    33
  </span>
  Abraham planted a tamarisk tree in Beersheba, and there he called on the name of Yahweh, the Everlasting God.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN21V34">
    34
  </span>
  Abraham lived as a foreigner in the land of the Philistines many days.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN21FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN21V3">
      21:3
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Isaac means “He laughs”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN21FN2">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN21V31">
      21:31
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Beersheba can mean “well of the oath” or “well of seven”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 22

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V1">
    1
  </span>
  After these things, God tested Abraham, and said to him, “Abraham!”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Here I am.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V2">
    2
  </span>
  He said, “Now take your son, your only son, Isaac, whom you love, and go into the land of Moriah. Offer him there as a burnt offering on one of the mountains which I will tell you of.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V3">
    3
  </span>
  Abraham rose early in the morning, and saddled his donkey; and took two of his young men with him, and Isaac his son. He split the wood for the burnt offering, and rose up, and went to the place of which God had told him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V4">
    4
  </span>
  On the third day Abraham lifted up his eyes, and saw the place far off.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V5">
    5
  </span>
  Abraham said to his young men, “Stay here with the donkey. The boy and I will go over there. We will worship, and come back to you.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V6">
    6
  </span>
  Abraham took the wood of the burnt offering and laid it on Isaac his son. He took in his hand the fire and the knife. They both went together.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V7">
    7
  </span>
  Isaac spoke to Abraham his father, and said, “My father?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Here I am, my son.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Here is the fire and the wood, but where is the lamb for a burnt offering?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V8">
    8
  </span>
  Abraham said, “God will provide himself the lamb for a burnt offering, my son.” So they both went together.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V9">
    9
  </span>
  They came to the place which God had told him of. Abraham built the altar there, and laid the wood in order, bound Isaac his son, and laid him on the altar, on the wood.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V10">
    10
  </span>
  Abraham stretched out his hand, and took the knife to kill his son.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V11">
    11
  </span>
  Yahweh’s angel called to him out of the sky, and said, “Abraham, Abraham!”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Here I am.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V12">
    12
  </span>
  He said, “Don’t lay your hand on the boy or do anything to him. For now I know that you fear God, since you have not withheld your son, your only son, from me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V13">
    13
  </span>
  Abraham lifted up his eyes, and looked, and saw that behind him was a ram caught in the thicket by his horns. Abraham went and took the ram, and offered him up for a burnt offering instead of his son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V14">
    14
  </span>
  Abraham called the name of that place “Yahweh Will Provide”.
  <a href="#GEN22FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      or, Yahweh-Jireh, or, Yahweh-Seeing
    </span>
  </a>
  As it is said to this day, “On Yahweh’s mountain, it will be provided.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V15">
    15
  </span>
  Yahweh’s angel called to Abraham a second time out of the sky,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V16">
    16
  </span>
  and said, “ ‘I have sworn by myself,’ says Yahweh, ‘because you have done this thing, and have not withheld your son, your only son,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V17">
    17
  </span>
  that I will bless you greatly, and I will multiply your offspring greatly like the stars of the heavens, and like the sand which is on the seashore. Your offspring will possess the gate of his enemies.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V18">
    18
  </span>
  All the nations of the earth will be blessed by your offspring, because you have obeyed my voice.’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V19">
    19
  </span>
  So Abraham returned to his young men, and they rose up and went together to Beersheba. Abraham lived at Beersheba.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V20">
    20
  </span>
  After these things, Abraham was told, “Behold, Milcah, she also has borne children to your brother Nahor:
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V21">
    21
  </span>
  Uz his firstborn, Buz his brother, Kemuel the father of Aram,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V22">
    22
  </span>
  Chesed, Hazo, Pildash, Jidlaph, and Bethuel.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V23">
    23
  </span>
  Bethuel became the father of Rebekah. These eight Milcah bore to Nahor, Abraham’s brother.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN22V24">
    24
  </span>
  His concubine, whose name was Reumah, also bore Tebah, Gaham, Tahash, and Maacah.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN22FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN22V14">
      22:14
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      or, Yahweh-Jireh, or, Yahweh-Seeing
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 23

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V1">
    1
  </span>
  Sarah lived one hundred twenty-seven years. This was the length of Sarah’s life.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V2">
    2
  </span>
  Sarah died in Kiriath Arba (also called Hebron), in the land of Canaan. Abraham came to mourn for Sarah, and to weep for her.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V3">
    3
  </span>
  Abraham rose up from before his dead and spoke to the children of Heth, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V4">
    4
  </span>
  “I am a stranger and a foreigner living with you. Give me a possession of a burying-place with you, that I may bury my dead out of my sight.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V5">
    5
  </span>
  The children of Heth answered Abraham, saying to him,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V6">
    6
  </span>
  “Hear us, my lord. You are a prince of God among us. Bury your dead in the best of our tombs. None of us will withhold from you his tomb. Bury your dead.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V7">
    7
  </span>
  Abraham rose up, and bowed himself to the people of the land, to the children of Heth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V8">
    8
  </span>
  He talked with them, saying, “If you agree that I should bury my dead out of my sight, hear me, and entreat for me to Ephron the son of Zohar,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V9">
    9
  </span>
  that he may sell me the cave of Machpelah, which he has, which is in the end of his field. For the full price let him sell it to me among you as a possession for a burial place.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V10">
    10
  </span>
  Now Ephron was sitting in the middle of the children of Heth. Ephron the Hittite answered Abraham in the hearing of the children of Heth, even of all who went in at the gate of his city, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V11">
    11
  </span>
  “No, my lord, hear me. I give you the field, and I give you the cave that is in it. In the presence of the children of my people I give it to you. Bury your dead.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V12">
    12
  </span>
  Abraham bowed himself down before the people of the land.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V13">
    13
  </span>
  He spoke to Ephron in the audience of the people of the land, saying, “But if you will, please hear me. I will give the price of the field. Take it from me, and I will bury my dead there.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V14">
    14
  </span>
  Ephron answered Abraham, saying to him,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V15">
    15
  </span>
  “My lord, listen to me. What is a piece of land worth four hundred shekels of silver
  <a href="#GEN23FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      A shekel is about 10 grams, so 400 shekels would be about 4 kg. or 8.8 pounds.
    </span>
  </a>
  between me and you? Therefore bury your dead.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V16">
    16
  </span>
  Abraham listened to Ephron. Abraham weighed to Ephron the silver which he had named in the hearing of the children of Heth, four hundred shekels of silver, according to the current merchants’ standard.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V17">
    17
  </span>
  So the field of Ephron, which was in Machpelah, which was before Mamre, the field, the cave which was in it, and all the trees that were in the field, that were in all of its borders, were deeded
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V18">
    18
  </span>
  to Abraham for a possession in the presence of the children of Heth, before all who went in at the gate of his city.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V19">
    19
  </span>
  After this, Abraham buried Sarah his wife in the cave of the field of Machpelah before Mamre (that is, Hebron), in the land of Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN23V20">
    20
  </span>
  The field, and the cave that is in it, were deeded to Abraham by the children of Heth as a possession for a burial place.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN23FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN23V15">
      23:15
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      A shekel is about 10 grams, so 400 shekels would be about 4 kg. or 8.8 pounds.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 24

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V1">
    1
  </span>
  Abraham was old, and well advanced in age. Yahweh had blessed Abraham in all things.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V2">
    2
  </span>
  Abraham said to his servant, the elder of his house, who ruled over all that he had, “Please put your hand under my thigh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V3">
    3
  </span>
  I will make you swear by Yahweh, the God of heaven and the God of the earth, that you shall not take a wife for my son of the daughters of the Canaanites, among whom I live.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V4">
    4
  </span>
  But you shall go to my country, and to my relatives, and take a wife for my son Isaac.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V5">
    5
  </span>
  The servant said to him, “What if the woman isn’t willing to follow me to this land? Must I bring your son again to the land you came from?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V6">
    6
  </span>
  Abraham said to him, “Beware that you don’t bring my son there again.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V7">
    7
  </span>
  Yahweh, the God of heaven—who took me from my father’s house, and from the land of my birth, who spoke to me, and who swore to me, saying, ‘I will give this land to your offspring—he will send his angel before you, and you shall take a wife for my son from there.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V8">
    8
  </span>
  If the woman isn’t willing to follow you, then you shall be clear from this oath to me. Only you shall not bring my son there again.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V9">
    9
  </span>
  The servant put his hand under the thigh of Abraham his master, and swore to him concerning this matter.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V10">
    10
  </span>
  The servant took ten of his master’s camels, and departed, having a variety of good things of his master’s with him. He arose, and went to Mesopotamia, to the city of Nahor.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V11">
    11
  </span>
  He made the camels kneel down outside the city by the well of water at the time of evening, the time that women go out to draw water.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V12">
    12
  </span>
  He said, “Yahweh, the God of my master Abraham, please give me success today, and show kindness to my master Abraham.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V13">
    13
  </span>
  Behold, I am standing by the spring of water. The daughters of the men of the city are coming out to draw water.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V14">
    14
  </span>
  Let it happen, that the young lady to whom I will say, ‘Please let down your pitcher, that I may drink,’ then she says, ‘Drink, and I will also give your camels a drink,’—let her be the one you have appointed for your servant Isaac. By this I will know that you have shown kindness to my master.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V15">
    15
  </span>
  Before he had finished speaking, behold, Rebekah came out, who was born to Bethuel the son of Milcah, the wife of Nahor, Abraham’s brother, with her pitcher on her shoulder.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V16">
    16
  </span>
  The young lady was very beautiful to look at, a virgin. No man had known her. She went down to the spring, filled her pitcher, and came up.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V17">
    17
  </span>
  The servant ran to meet her, and said, “Please give me a drink, a little water from your pitcher.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V18">
    18
  </span>
  She said, “Drink, my lord.” She hurried, and let down her pitcher on her hand, and gave him a drink.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V19">
    19
  </span>
  When she had finished giving him a drink, she said, “I will also draw for your camels, until they have finished drinking.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V20">
    20
  </span>
  She hurried, and emptied her pitcher into the trough, and ran again to the well to draw, and drew for all his camels.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V21">
    21
  </span>
  The man looked steadfastly at her, remaining silent, to know whether Yahweh had made his journey prosperous or not.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V22">
    22
  </span>
  As the camels had done drinking, the man took a golden ring of half a shekel
  <a href="#GEN24FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      A shekel is about 10 grams or about 0.35 ounces.
    </span>
  </a>
  weight, and two bracelets for her hands of ten shekels weight of gold,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V23">
    23
  </span>
  and said, “Whose daughter are you? Please tell me. Is there room in your father’s house for us to stay?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V24">
    24
  </span>
  She said to him, “I am the daughter of Bethuel the son of Milcah, whom she bore to Nahor.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V25">
    25
  </span>
  She said moreover to him, “We have both straw and feed enough, and room to lodge in.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V26">
    26
  </span>
  The man bowed his head, and worshiped Yahweh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V27">
    27
  </span>
  He said, “Blessed be Yahweh, the God of my master Abraham, who has not forsaken his loving kindness and his truth toward my master. As for me, Yahweh has led me on the way to the house of my master’s relatives.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V28">
    28
  </span>
  The young lady ran, and told her mother’s house about these words.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V29">
    29
  </span>
  Rebekah had a brother, and his name was Laban. Laban ran out to the man, to the spring.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V30">
    30
  </span>
  When he saw the ring, and the bracelets on his sister’s hands, and when he heard the words of Rebekah his sister, saying, “This is what the man said to me,” he came to the man. Behold, he was standing by the camels at the spring.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V31">
    31
  </span>
  He said, “Come in, you blessed of Yahweh. Why do you stand outside? For I have prepared the house, and room for the camels.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V32">
    32
  </span>
  The man came into the house, and he unloaded the camels. He gave straw and feed for the camels, and water to wash his feet and the feet of the men who were with him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V33">
    33
  </span>
  Food was set before him to eat, but he said, “I will not eat until I have told my message.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Laban said, “Speak on.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V34">
    34
  </span>
  He said, “I am Abraham’s servant.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V35">
    35
  </span>
  Yahweh has blessed my master greatly. He has become great. Yahweh has given him flocks and herds, silver and gold, male servants and female servants, and camels and donkeys.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V36">
    36
  </span>
  Sarah, my master’s wife, bore a son to my master when she was old. He has given all that he has to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V37">
    37
  </span>
  My master made me swear, saying, ‘You shall not take a wife for my son from the daughters of the Canaanites, in whose land I live,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V38">
    38
  </span>
  but you shall go to my father’s house, and to my relatives, and take a wife for my son.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V39">
    39
  </span>
  I asked my master, ‘What if the woman will not follow me?’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V40">
    40
  </span>
  He said to me, ‘Yahweh, before whom I walk, will send his angel with you, and prosper your way. You shall take a wife for my son from my relatives, and of my father’s house.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V41">
    41
  </span>
  Then you will be clear from my oath, when you come to my relatives. If they don’t give her to you, you shall be clear from my oath.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V42">
    42
  </span>
  I came today to the spring, and said, ‘Yahweh, the God of my master Abraham, if now you do prosper my way which I go—
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V43">
    43
  </span>
  behold, I am standing by this spring of water. Let it happen, that the maiden who comes out to draw, to whom I will say, “Please give me a little water from your pitcher to drink,”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V44">
    44
  </span>
  then she tells me, “Drink, and I will also draw for your camels,”—let her be the woman whom Yahweh has appointed for my master’s son.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V45">
    45
  </span>
  Before I had finished speaking in my heart, behold, Rebekah came out with her pitcher on her shoulder. She went down to the spring, and drew. I said to her, ‘Please let me drink.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V46">
    46
  </span>
  She hurried and let down her pitcher from her shoulder, and said, ‘Drink, and I will also give your camels a drink.’ So I drank, and she also gave the camels a drink.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V47">
    47
  </span>
  I asked her, and said, ‘Whose daughter are you?’ She said, ‘The daughter of Bethuel, Nahor’s son, whom Milcah bore to him.’ I put the ring on her nose, and the bracelets on her hands.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V48">
    48
  </span>
  I bowed my head, and worshiped Yahweh, and blessed Yahweh, the God of my master Abraham, who had led me in the right way to take my master’s brother’s daughter for his son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V49">
    49
  </span>
  Now if you will deal kindly and truly with my master, tell me. If not, tell me, that I may turn to the right hand, or to the left.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V50">
    50
  </span>
  Then Laban and Bethuel answered, “The thing proceeds from Yahweh. We can’t speak to you bad or good.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V51">
    51
  </span>
  Behold, Rebekah is before you. Take her, and go, and let her be your master’s son’s wife, as Yahweh has spoken.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V52">
    52
  </span>
  When Abraham’s servant heard their words, he bowed himself down to the earth to Yahweh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V53">
    53
  </span>
  The servant brought out jewels of silver, and jewels of gold, and clothing, and gave them to Rebekah. He also gave precious things to her brother and her mother.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V54">
    54
  </span>
  They ate and drank, he and the men who were with him, and stayed all night. They rose up in the morning, and he said, “Send me away to my master.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V55">
    55
  </span>
  Her brother and her mother said, “Let the young lady stay with us a few days, at least ten. After that she will go.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V56">
    56
  </span>
  He said to them, “Don’t hinder me, since Yahweh has prospered my way. Send me away that I may go to my master.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V57">
    57
  </span>
  They said, “We will call the young lady, and ask her.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V58">
    58
  </span>
  They called Rebekah, and said to her, “Will you go with this man?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  She said, “I will go.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V59">
    59
  </span>
  They sent away Rebekah, their sister, with her nurse, Abraham’s servant, and his men.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V60">
    60
  </span>
  They blessed Rebekah, and said to her, “Our sister, may you be the mother of thousands of ten thousands, and let your offspring possess the gate of those who hate them.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V61">
    61
  </span>
  Rebekah arose with her ladies. They rode on the camels, and followed the man. The servant took Rebekah, and went his way.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V62">
    62
  </span>
  Isaac came from the way of Beer Lahai Roi, for he lived in the land of the South.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V63">
    63
  </span>
  Isaac went out to meditate in the field at the evening. He lifted up his eyes and looked. Behold, there were camels coming.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V64">
    64
  </span>
  Rebekah lifted up her eyes, and when she saw Isaac, she got off the camel.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V65">
    65
  </span>
  She said to the servant, “Who is the man who is walking in the field to meet us?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  The servant said, “It is my master.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  She took her veil, and covered herself.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V66">
    66
  </span>
  The servant told Isaac all the things that he had done.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN24V67">
    67
  </span>
  Isaac brought her into his mother Sarah’s tent, and took Rebekah, and she became his wife. He loved her. So Isaac was comforted after his mother’s death.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN24FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN24V22">
      24:22
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      A shekel is about 10 grams or about 0.35 ounces.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 25

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V1">
    1
  </span>
  Abraham took another wife, and her name was Keturah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V2">
    2
  </span>
  She bore him Zimran, Jokshan, Medan, Midian, Ishbak, and Shuah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V3">
    3
  </span>
  Jokshan became the father of Sheba, and Dedan. The sons of Dedan were Asshurim, Letushim, and Leummim.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V4">
    4
  </span>
  The sons of Midian were Ephah, Epher, Hanoch, Abida, and Eldaah. All these were the children of Keturah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V5">
    5
  </span>
  Abraham gave all that he had to Isaac,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V6">
    6
  </span>
  but Abraham gave gifts to the sons of Abraham’s concubines. While he still lived, he sent them away from Isaac his son, eastward, to the east country.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V7">
    7
  </span>
  These are the days of the years of Abraham’s life which he lived: one hundred seventy-five years.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V8">
    8
  </span>
  Abraham gave up his spirit, and died at a good old age, an old man, and full of years, and was gathered to his people.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V9">
    9
  </span>
  Isaac and Ishmael, his sons, buried him in the cave of Machpelah, in the field of Ephron, the son of Zohar the Hittite, which is near Mamre,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V10">
    10
  </span>
  the field which Abraham purchased from the children of Heth. Abraham was buried there with Sarah, his wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V11">
    11
  </span>
  After the death of Abraham, God blessed Isaac, his son. Isaac lived by Beer Lahai Roi.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V12">
    12
  </span>
  Now this is the history of the generations of Ishmael, Abraham’s son, whom Hagar the Egyptian, Sarah’s servant, bore to Abraham.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V13">
    13
  </span>
  These are the names of the sons of Ishmael, by their names, according to the order of their birth: the firstborn of Ishmael, Nebaioth, then Kedar, Adbeel, Mibsam,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V14">
    14
  </span>
  Mishma, Dumah, Massa,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V15">
    15
  </span>
  Hadad, Tema, Jetur, Naphish, and Kedemah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V16">
    16
  </span>
  These are the sons of Ishmael, and these are their names, by their villages, and by their encampments: twelve princes, according to their nations.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V17">
    17
  </span>
  These are the years of the life of Ishmael: one hundred thirty-seven years. He gave up his spirit and died, and was gathered to his people.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V18">
    18
  </span>
  They lived from Havilah to Shur that is before Egypt, as you go toward Assyria. He lived opposite all his relatives.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V19">
    19
  </span>
  This is the history of the generations of Isaac, Abraham’s son. Abraham became the father of Isaac.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V20">
    20
  </span>
  Isaac was forty years old when he took Rebekah, the daughter of Bethuel the Syrian of Paddan Aram, the sister of Laban the Syrian, to be his wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V21">
    21
  </span>
  Isaac entreated Yahweh for his wife, because she was barren. Yahweh was entreated by him, and Rebekah his wife conceived.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V22">
    22
  </span>
  The children struggled together within her. She said, “If it is like this, why do I live?” She went to inquire of Yahweh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V23">
    23
  </span>
  Yahweh said to her,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “Two nations are in your womb.
</div>
<div class="q">
  Two peoples will be separated from your body.
</div>
<div class="q">
  The one people will be stronger than the other people.
</div>
<div class="q">
  The elder will serve the younger.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V24">
    24
  </span>
  When her days to be delivered were fulfilled, behold, there were twins in her womb.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V25">
    25
  </span>
  The first came out red all over, like a hairy garment. They named him Esau.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V26">
    26
  </span>
  After that, his brother came out, and his hand had hold on Esau’s heel. He was named Jacob. Isaac was sixty years old when she bore them.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V27">
    27
  </span>
  The boys grew. Esau was a skillful hunter, a man of the field. Jacob was a quiet man, living in tents.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V28">
    28
  </span>
  Now Isaac loved Esau, because he ate his venison. Rebekah loved Jacob.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V29">
    29
  </span>
  Jacob boiled stew. Esau came in from the field, and he was famished.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V30">
    30
  </span>
  Esau said to Jacob, “Please feed me with some of that red stew, for I am famished.” Therefore his name was called Edom.
  <a href="#GEN25FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      “Edom” means “red”.
    </span>
  </a>
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V31">
    31
  </span>
  Jacob said, “First, sell me your birthright.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V32">
    32
  </span>
  Esau said, “Behold, I am about to die. What good is the birthright to me?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V33">
    33
  </span>
  Jacob said, “Swear to me first.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He swore to him. He sold his birthright to Jacob.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN25V34">
    34
  </span>
  Jacob gave Esau bread and lentil stew. He ate and drank, rose up, and went his way. So Esau despised his birthright.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN25FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN25V30">
      25:30
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Edom” means “red”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 26

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V1">
    1
  </span>
  There was a famine in the land, in addition to the first famine that was in the days of Abraham. Isaac went to Abimelech king of the Philistines, to Gerar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V2">
    2
  </span>
  Yahweh appeared to him, and said, “Don’t go down into Egypt. Live in the land I will tell you about.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V3">
    3
  </span>
  Live in this land, and I will be with you, and will bless you. For I will give to you, and to your offspring, all these lands, and I will establish the oath which I swore to Abraham your father.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V4">
    4
  </span>
  I will multiply your offspring as the stars of the sky, and will give all these lands to your offspring. In your offspring all the nations of the earth will be blessed,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V5">
    5
  </span>
  because Abraham obeyed my voice, and kept my requirements, my commandments, my statutes, and my laws.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V6">
    6
  </span>
  Isaac lived in Gerar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V7">
    7
  </span>
  The men of the place asked him about his wife. He said, “She is my sister,” for he was afraid to say, “My wife”, lest, he thought, “the men of the place might kill me for Rebekah, because she is beautiful to look at.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V8">
    8
  </span>
  When he had been there a long time, Abimelech king of the Philistines looked out at a window, and saw, and, behold, Isaac was caressing Rebekah, his wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V9">
    9
  </span>
  Abimelech called Isaac, and said, “Behold, surely she is your wife. Why did you say, ‘She is my sister’?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Isaac said to him, “Because I said, ‘Lest I die because of her.’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V10">
    10
  </span>
  Abimelech said, “What is this you have done to us? One of the people might easily have lain with your wife, and you would have brought guilt on us!”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V11">
    11
  </span>
  Abimelech commanded all the people, saying, “He who touches this man or his wife will surely be put to death.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V12">
    12
  </span>
  Isaac sowed in that land, and reaped in the same year one hundred times what he planted. Yahweh blessed him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V13">
    13
  </span>
  The man grew great, and grew more and more until he became very great.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V14">
    14
  </span>
  He had possessions of flocks, possessions of herds, and a great household. The Philistines envied him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V15">
    15
  </span>
  Now all the wells which his father’s servants had dug in the days of Abraham his father, the Philistines had stopped, and filled with earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V16">
    16
  </span>
  Abimelech said to Isaac, “Go away from us, for you are much mightier than we.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V17">
    17
  </span>
  Isaac departed from there, encamped in the valley of Gerar, and lived there.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V18">
    18
  </span>
  Isaac dug again the wells of water, which they had dug in the days of Abraham his father, for the Philistines had stopped them after the death of Abraham. He called their names after the names by which his father had called them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V19">
    19
  </span>
  Isaac’s servants dug in the valley, and found there a well of flowing
  <a href="#GEN26FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Or, living. Or, fresh.
    </span>
  </a>
  water.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V20">
    20
  </span>
  The herdsmen of Gerar argued with Isaac’s herdsmen, saying, “The water is ours.” So he called the name of the well Esek,
  <a href="#GEN26FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      “Esek” means “contention”.
    </span>
  </a>
  because they contended with him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V21">
    21
  </span>
  They dug another well, and they argued over that, also. So he called its name Sitnah.
  <a href="#GEN26FN3" class="notemark">
    §
    <span class="popup">
      “Sitnah” means “hostility”.
    </span>
  </a>
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V22">
    22
  </span>
  He left that place, and dug another well. They didn’t argue over that one. So he called it Rehoboth.
  <a href="#GEN26FN4" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      “Rehoboth” means “broad places”.
    </span>
  </a>
  He said, “For now Yahweh has made room for us, and we will be fruitful in the land.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V23">
    23
  </span>
  He went up from there to Beersheba.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V24">
    24
  </span>
  Yahweh appeared to him the same night, and said, “I am the God of Abraham your father. Don’t be afraid, for I am with you, and will bless you, and multiply your offspring for my servant Abraham’s sake.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V25">
    25
  </span>
  He built an altar there, and called on Yahweh’s name, and pitched his tent there. There Isaac’s servants dug a well.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V26">
    26
  </span>
  Then Abimelech went to him from Gerar with Ahuzzath his friend, and Phicol the captain of his army.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V27">
    27
  </span>
  Isaac said to them, “Why have you come to me, since you hate me, and have sent me away from you?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V28">
    28
  </span>
  They said, “We saw plainly that Yahweh was with you. We said, ‘Let there now be an oath between us, even between us and you, and let’s make a covenant with you,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V29">
    29
  </span>
  that you will do us no harm, as we have not touched you, and as we have done to you nothing but good, and have sent you away in peace.’ You are now the blessed of Yahweh.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V30">
    30
  </span>
  He made them a feast, and they ate and drank.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V31">
    31
  </span>
  They rose up some time in the morning, and swore an oath to one another. Isaac sent them away, and they departed from him in peace.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V32">
    32
  </span>
  The same day, Isaac’s servants came, and told him concerning the well which they had dug, and said to him, “We have found water.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V33">
    33
  </span>
  He called it “Shibah”.
  <a href="#GEN26FN5" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      Shibah means “oath” or “seven”.
    </span>
  </a>
  Therefore the name of the city is “Beersheba”
  <a href="#GEN26FN6" class="notemark">
    §
    <span class="popup">
      Beersheba means “well of the oath” or “well of the seven”
    </span>
  </a>
  to this day.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V34">
    34
  </span>
  When Esau was forty years old, he took as wife Judith, the daughter of Beeri the Hittite, and Basemath, the daughter of Elon the Hittite.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN26V35">
    35
  </span>
  They grieved Isaac’s and Rebekah’s spirits.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN26FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN26V19">
      26:19
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Or, living. Or, fresh.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN26FN2">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN26V20">
      26:20
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Esek” means “contention”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN26FN3">
    <span class="notemark">
      §
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN26V21">
      26:21
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Sitnah” means “hostility”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN26FN4">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN26V22">
      26:22
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Rehoboth” means “broad places”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN26FN5">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN26V33">
      26:33
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Shibah means “oath” or “seven”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN26FN6">
    <span class="notemark">
      §
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN26V33">
      26:33
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Beersheba means “well of the oath” or “well of the seven”
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 27

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V1">
    1
  </span>
  When Isaac was old, and his eyes were dim, so that he could not see, he called Esau his elder son, and said to him, “My son?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said to him, “Here I am.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V2">
    2
  </span>
  He said, “See now, I am old. I don’t know the day of my death.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V3">
    3
  </span>
  Now therefore, please take your weapons, your quiver and your bow, and go out to the field, and get me venison.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V4">
    4
  </span>
  Make me savory food, such as I love, and bring it to me, that I may eat, and that my soul may bless you before I die.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V5">
    5
  </span>
  Rebekah heard when Isaac spoke to Esau his son. Esau went to the field to hunt for venison, and to bring it.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V6">
    6
  </span>
  Rebekah spoke to Jacob her son, saying, “Behold, I heard your father speak to Esau your brother, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V7">
    7
  </span>
  ‘Bring me venison, and make me savory food, that I may eat, and bless you before Yahweh before my death.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V8">
    8
  </span>
  Now therefore, my son, obey my voice according to that which I command you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V9">
    9
  </span>
  Go now to the flock and get me two good young goats from there. I will make them savory food for your father, such as he loves.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V10">
    10
  </span>
  You shall bring it to your father, that he may eat, so that he may bless you before his death.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V11">
    11
  </span>
  Jacob said to Rebekah his mother, “Behold, Esau my brother is a hairy man, and I am a smooth man.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V12">
    12
  </span>
  What if my father touches me? I will seem to him as a deceiver, and I would bring a curse on myself, and not a blessing.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V13">
    13
  </span>
  His mother said to him, “Let your curse be on me, my son. Only obey my voice, and go get them for me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V14">
    14
  </span>
  He went, and got them, and brought them to his mother. His mother made savory food, such as his father loved.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V15">
    15
  </span>
  Rebekah took the good clothes of Esau, her elder son, which were with her in the house, and put them on Jacob, her younger son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V16">
    16
  </span>
  She put the skins of the young goats on his hands, and on the smooth of his neck.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V17">
    17
  </span>
  She gave the savory food and the bread, which she had prepared, into the hand of her son Jacob.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V18">
    18
  </span>
  He came to his father, and said, “My father?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Here I am. Who are you, my son?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V19">
    19
  </span>
  Jacob said to his father, “I am Esau your firstborn. I have done what you asked me to do. Please arise, sit and eat of my venison, that your soul may bless me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V20">
    20
  </span>
  Isaac said to his son, “How is it that you have found it so quickly, my son?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Because Yahweh your God gave me success.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V21">
    21
  </span>
  Isaac said to Jacob, “Please come near, that I may feel you, my son, whether you are really my son Esau or not.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V22">
    22
  </span>
  Jacob went near to Isaac his father. He felt him, and said, “The voice is Jacob’s voice, but the hands are the hands of Esau.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V23">
    23
  </span>
  He didn’t recognize him, because his hands were hairy, like his brother Esau’s hands. So he blessed him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V24">
    24
  </span>
  He said, “Are you really my son Esau?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “I am.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V25">
    25
  </span>
  He said, “Bring it near to me, and I will eat of my son’s venison, that my soul may bless you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He brought it near to him, and he ate. He brought him wine, and he drank.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V26">
    26
  </span>
  His father Isaac said to him, “Come near now, and kiss me, my son.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V27">
    27
  </span>
  He came near, and kissed him. He smelled the smell of his clothing, and blessed him, and said,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “Behold, the smell of my son
</div>
<div class="q2">
  is as the smell of a field which Yahweh has blessed.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V28">
    28
  </span>
  God give you of the dew of the sky,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  of the fatness of the earth,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and plenty of grain and new wine.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V29">
    29
  </span>
  Let peoples serve you,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and nations bow down to you.
</div>
<div class="q">
  Be lord over your brothers.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Let your mother’s sons bow down to you.
</div>
<div class="q">
  Cursed be everyone who curses you.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Blessed be everyone who blesses you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V30">
    30
  </span>
  As soon as Isaac had finished blessing Jacob, and Jacob had just gone out from the presence of Isaac his father, Esau his brother came in from his hunting.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V31">
    31
  </span>
  He also made savory food, and brought it to his father. He said to his father, “Let my father arise, and eat of his son’s venison, that your soul may bless me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V32">
    32
  </span>
  Isaac his father said to him, “Who are you?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “I am your son, your firstborn, Esau.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V33">
    33
  </span>
  Isaac trembled violently, and said, “Who, then, is he who has taken venison, and brought it to me, and I have eaten of all before you came, and have blessed him? Yes, he will be blessed.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V34">
    34
  </span>
  When Esau heard the words of his father, he cried with an exceedingly great and bitter cry, and said to his father, “Bless me, even me also, my father.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V35">
    35
  </span>
  He said, “Your brother came with deceit, and has taken away your blessing.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V36">
    36
  </span>
  He said, “Isn’t he rightly named Jacob? For he has supplanted me these two times. He took away my birthright. See, now he has taken away my blessing.” He said, “Haven’t you reserved a blessing for me?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V37">
    37
  </span>
  Isaac answered Esau, “Behold, I have made him your lord, and all his brothers I have given to him for servants. I have sustained him with grain and new wine. What then will I do for you, my son?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V38">
    38
  </span>
  Esau said to his father, “Do you have just one blessing, my father? Bless me, even me also, my father.” Esau lifted up his voice, and wept.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V39">
    39
  </span>
  Isaac his father answered him,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “Behold, your dwelling will be of the fatness of the earth,
</div>
<div class="q">
  and of the dew of the sky from above.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V40">
    40
  </span>
  You will live by your sword, and you will serve your brother.
</div>
<div class="q">
  It will happen, when you will break loose,
</div>
<div class="q">
  that you will shake his yoke from off your neck.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V41">
    41
  </span>
  Esau hated Jacob because of the blessing with which his father blessed him. Esau said in his heart, “The days of mourning for my father are at hand. Then I will kill my brother Jacob.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V42">
    42
  </span>
  The words of Esau, her elder son, were told to Rebekah. She sent and called Jacob, her younger son, and said to him, “Behold, your brother Esau comforts himself about you by planning to kill you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V43">
    43
  </span>
  Now therefore, my son, obey my voice. Arise, flee to Laban, my brother, in Haran.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V44">
    44
  </span>
  Stay with him a few days, until your brother’s fury turns away—
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V45">
    45
  </span>
  until your brother’s anger turns away from you, and he forgets what you have done to him. Then I will send, and get you from there. Why should I be bereaved of you both in one day?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN27V46">
    46
  </span>
  Rebekah said to Isaac, “I am weary of my life because of the daughters of Heth. If Jacob takes a wife of the daughters of Heth, such as these, of the daughters of the land, what good will my life do me?”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 28

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V1">
    1
  </span>
  Isaac called Jacob, blessed him, and commanded him, “You shall not take a wife of the daughters of Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V2">
    2
  </span>
  Arise, go to Paddan Aram, to the house of Bethuel your mother’s father. Take a wife from there from the daughters of Laban, your mother’s brother.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V3">
    3
  </span>
  May God Almighty bless you, and make you fruitful, and multiply you, that you may be a company of peoples,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V4">
    4
  </span>
  and give you the blessing of Abraham, to you and to your offspring with you, that you may inherit the land where you travel, which God gave to Abraham.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V5">
    5
  </span>
  Isaac sent Jacob away. He went to Paddan Aram to Laban, son of Bethuel the Syrian, the brother of Rebekah, Jacob’s and Esau’s mother.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V6">
    6
  </span>
  Now Esau saw that Isaac had blessed Jacob and sent him away to Paddan Aram, to take him a wife from there, and that as he blessed him he gave him a command, saying, “You shall not take a wife of the daughters of Canaan;”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V7">
    7
  </span>
  and that Jacob obeyed his father and his mother, and was gone to Paddan Aram.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V8">
    8
  </span>
  Esau saw that the daughters of Canaan didn’t please Isaac, his father.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V9">
    9
  </span>
  So Esau went to Ishmael, and took, in addition to the wives that he had, Mahalath the daughter of Ishmael, Abraham’s son, the sister of Nebaioth, to be his wife.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V10">
    10
  </span>
  Jacob went out from Beersheba, and went toward Haran.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V11">
    11
  </span>
  He came to a certain place, and stayed there all night, because the sun had set. He took one of the stones of the place, and put it under his head, and lay down in that place to sleep.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V12">
    12
  </span>
  He dreamed and saw a stairway set upon the earth, and its top reached to heaven. Behold, the angels of God were ascending and descending on it.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V13">
    13
  </span>
  Behold, Yahweh stood above it, and said, “I am Yahweh, the God of Abraham your father, and the God of Isaac. I will give the land you lie on to you and to your offspring.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V14">
    14
  </span>
  Your offspring will be as the dust of the earth, and you will spread abroad to the west, and to the east, and to the north, and to the south. In you and in your offspring, all the families of the earth will be blessed.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V15">
    15
  </span>
  Behold, I am with you, and will keep you, wherever you go, and will bring you again into this land. For I will not leave you until I have done that which I have spoken of to you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V16">
    16
  </span>
  Jacob awakened out of his sleep, and he said, “Surely Yahweh is in this place, and I didn’t know it.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V17">
    17
  </span>
  He was afraid, and said, “How awesome this place is! This is none other than God’s house, and this is the gate of heaven.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V18">
    18
  </span>
  Jacob rose up early in the morning, and took the stone that he had put under his head, and set it up for a pillar, and poured oil on its top.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V19">
    19
  </span>
  He called the name of that place Bethel, but the name of the city was Luz at the first.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V20">
    20
  </span>
  Jacob vowed a vow, saying, “If God will be with me, and will keep me in this way that I go, and will give me bread to eat, and clothing to put on,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V21">
    21
  </span>
  so that I come again to my father’s house in peace, and Yahweh will be my God,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN28V22">
    22
  </span>
  then this stone, which I have set up for a pillar, will be God’s house. Of all that you will give me I will surely give a tenth to you.”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 29

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V1">
    1
  </span>
  Then Jacob went on his journey, and came to the land of the children of the east.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V2">
    2
  </span>
  He looked, and saw a well in the field, and saw three flocks of sheep lying there by it. For out of that well they watered the flocks. The stone on the well’s mouth was large.
