  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V3">
    3
  </span>
  There all the flocks were gathered. They rolled the stone from the well’s mouth, and watered the sheep, and put the stone back on the well’s mouth in its place.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V4">
    4
  </span>
  Jacob said to them, “My relatives, where are you from?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They said, “We are from Haran.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V5">
    5
  </span>
  He said to them, “Do you know Laban, the son of Nahor?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They said, “We know him.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V6">
    6
  </span>
  He said to them, “Is it well with him?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They said, “It is well. See, Rachel, his daughter, is coming with the sheep.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V7">
    7
  </span>
  He said, “Behold, it is still the middle of the day, not time to gather the livestock together. Water the sheep, and go and feed them.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V8">
    8
  </span>
  They said, “We can’t, until all the flocks are gathered together, and they roll the stone from the well’s mouth. Then we will water the sheep.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V9">
    9
  </span>
  While he was yet speaking with them, Rachel came with her father’s sheep, for she kept them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V10">
    10
  </span>
  When Jacob saw Rachel the daughter of Laban, his mother’s brother, and the sheep of Laban, his mother’s brother, Jacob went near, and rolled the stone from the well’s mouth, and watered the flock of Laban his mother’s brother.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V11">
    11
  </span>
  Jacob kissed Rachel, and lifted up his voice, and wept.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V12">
    12
  </span>
  Jacob told Rachel that he was her father’s relative, and that he was Rebekah’s son. She ran and told her father.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V13">
    13
  </span>
  When Laban heard the news of Jacob, his sister’s son, he ran to meet Jacob, and embraced him, and kissed him, and brought him to his house. Jacob told Laban all these things.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V14">
    14
  </span>
  Laban said to him, “Surely you are my bone and my flesh.” Jacob stayed with him for a month.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V15">
    15
  </span>
  Laban said to Jacob, “Because you are my relative, should you therefore serve me for nothing? Tell me, what will your wages be?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V16">
    16
  </span>
  Laban had two daughters. The name of the elder was Leah, and the name of the younger was Rachel.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V17">
    17
  </span>
  Leah’s eyes were weak, but Rachel was beautiful in form and attractive.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V18">
    18
  </span>
  Jacob loved Rachel. He said, “I will serve you seven years for Rachel, your younger daughter.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V19">
    19
  </span>
  Laban said, “It is better that I give her to you, than that I should give her to another man. Stay with me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V20">
    20
  </span>
  Jacob served seven years for Rachel. They seemed to him but a few days, for the love he had for her.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V21">
    21
  </span>
  Jacob said to Laban, “Give me my wife, for my days are fulfilled, that I may go in to her.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V22">
    22
  </span>
  Laban gathered together all the men of the place, and made a feast.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V23">
    23
  </span>
  In the evening, he took Leah his daughter, and brought her to Jacob. He went in to her.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V24">
    24
  </span>
  Laban gave Zilpah his servant to his daughter Leah for a servant.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V25">
    25
  </span>
  In the morning, behold, it was Leah! He said to Laban, “What is this you have done to me? Didn’t I serve with you for Rachel? Why then have you deceived me?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V26">
    26
  </span>
  Laban said, “It is not done so in our place, to give the younger before the firstborn.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V27">
    27
  </span>
  Fulfill the week of this one, and we will give you the other also for the service which you will serve with me for seven more years.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V28">
    28
  </span>
  Jacob did so, and fulfilled her week. He gave him Rachel his daughter as wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V29">
    29
  </span>
  Laban gave Bilhah, his servant, to his daughter Rachel to be her servant.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V30">
    30
  </span>
  He went in also to Rachel, and he loved also Rachel more than Leah, and served with him seven more years.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V31">
    31
  </span>
  Yahweh saw that Leah was hated, and he opened her womb, but Rachel was barren.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V32">
    32
  </span>
  Leah conceived, and bore a son, and she named him Reuben. For she said, “Because Yahweh has looked at my affliction; for now my husband will love me.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V33">
    33
  </span>
  She conceived again, and bore a son, and said, “Because Yahweh has heard that I am hated, he has therefore given me this son also.” She named him Simeon.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V34">
    34
  </span>
  She conceived again, and bore a son. She said, “Now this time my husband will be joined to me, because I have borne him three sons.” Therefore his name was called Levi.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN29V35">
    35
  </span>
  She conceived again, and bore a son. She said, “This time I will praise Yahweh.” Therefore she named him Judah. Then she stopped bearing.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 30

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V1">
    1
  </span>
  When Rachel saw that she bore Jacob no children, Rachel envied her sister. She said to Jacob, “Give me children, or else I will die.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V2">
    2
  </span>
  Jacob’s anger burned against Rachel, and he said, “Am I in God’s place, who has withheld from you the fruit of the womb?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V3">
    3
  </span>
  She said, “Behold, my maid Bilhah. Go in to her, that she may bear on my knees, and I also may obtain children by her.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V4">
    4
  </span>
  She gave him Bilhah her servant as wife, and Jacob went in to her.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V5">
    5
  </span>
  Bilhah conceived, and bore Jacob a son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V6">
    6
  </span>
  Rachel said, “God has judged me, and has also heard my voice, and has given me a son.” Therefore she called his name Dan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V7">
    7
  </span>
  Bilhah, Rachel’s servant, conceived again, and bore Jacob a second son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V8">
    8
  </span>
  Rachel said, “I have wrestled with my sister with mighty wrestlings, and have prevailed.” She named him Naphtali.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V9">
    9
  </span>
  When Leah saw that she had finished bearing, she took Zilpah, her servant, and gave her to Jacob as a wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V10">
    10
  </span>
  Zilpah, Leah’s servant, bore Jacob a son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V11">
    11
  </span>
  Leah said, “How fortunate!” She named him Gad.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V12">
    12
  </span>
  Zilpah, Leah’s servant, bore Jacob a second son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V13">
    13
  </span>
  Leah said, “Happy am I, for the daughters will call me happy.” She named him Asher.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V14">
    14
  </span>
  Reuben went in the days of wheat harvest, and found mandrakes in the field, and brought them to his mother, Leah. Then Rachel said to Leah, “Please give me some of your son’s mandrakes.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V15">
    15
  </span>
  Leah said to her, “Is it a small matter that you have taken away my husband? Would you take away my son’s mandrakes, also?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Rachel said, “Therefore he will lie with you tonight for your son’s mandrakes.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V16">
    16
  </span>
  Jacob came from the field in the evening, and Leah went out to meet him, and said, “You must come in to me; for I have surely hired you with my son’s mandrakes.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He lay with her that night.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V17">
    17
  </span>
  God listened to Leah, and she conceived, and bore Jacob a fifth son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V18">
    18
  </span>
  Leah said, “God has given me my hire, because I gave my servant to my husband.” She named him Issachar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V19">
    19
  </span>
  Leah conceived again, and bore a sixth son to Jacob.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V20">
    20
  </span>
  Leah said, “God has endowed me with a good dowry. Now my husband will live with me, because I have borne him six sons.” She named him Zebulun.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V21">
    21
  </span>
  Afterwards, she bore a daughter, and named her Dinah.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V22">
    22
  </span>
  God remembered Rachel, and God listened to her, and opened her womb.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V23">
    23
  </span>
  She conceived, bore a son, and said, “God has taken away my reproach.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V24">
    24
  </span>
  She named him Joseph,
  <a href="#GEN30FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Joseph means “may he add”.
    </span>
  </a>
  saying, “May Yahweh add another son to me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V25">
    25
  </span>
  When Rachel had borne Joseph, Jacob said to Laban, “Send me away, that I may go to my own place, and to my country.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V26">
    26
  </span>
  Give me my wives and my children for whom I have served you, and let me go; for you know my service with which I have served you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V27">
    27
  </span>
  Laban said to him, “If now I have found favor in your eyes, stay here, for I have divined that Yahweh has blessed me for your sake.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V28">
    28
  </span>
  He said, “Appoint me your wages, and I will give it.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V29">
    29
  </span>
  Jacob said to him, “You know how I have served you, and how your livestock have fared with me.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V30">
    30
  </span>
  For it was little which you had before I came, and it has increased to a multitude. Yahweh has blessed you wherever I turned. Now when will I provide for my own house also?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V31">
    31
  </span>
  Laban said, “What shall I give you?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Jacob said, “You shall not give me anything. If you will do this thing for me, I will again feed your flock and keep it.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V32">
    32
  </span>
  I will pass through all your flock today, removing from there every speckled and spotted one, and every black one among the sheep, and the spotted and speckled among the goats. This will be my hire.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V33">
    33
  </span>
  So my righteousness will answer for me hereafter, when you come concerning my hire that is before you. Every one that is not speckled and spotted among the goats, and black among the sheep, that might be with me, will be considered stolen.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V34">
    34
  </span>
  Laban said, “Behold, let it be according to your word.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V35">
    35
  </span>
  That day, he removed the male goats that were streaked and spotted, and all the female goats that were speckled and spotted, every one that had white in it, and all the black ones among the sheep, and gave them into the hand of his sons.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V36">
    36
  </span>
  He set three days’ journey between himself and Jacob, and Jacob fed the rest of Laban’s flocks.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V37">
    37
  </span>
  Jacob took to himself rods of fresh poplar, almond, and plane tree, peeled white streaks in them, and made the white appear which was in the rods.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V38">
    38
  </span>
  He set the rods which he had peeled opposite the flocks in the watering troughs where the flocks came to drink. They conceived when they came to drink.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V39">
    39
  </span>
  The flocks conceived before the rods, and the flocks produced streaked, speckled, and spotted.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V40">
    40
  </span>
  Jacob separated the lambs, and set the faces of the flocks toward the streaked and all the black in Laban’s flock. He put his own droves apart, and didn’t put them into Laban’s flock.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V41">
    41
  </span>
  Whenever the stronger of the flock conceived, Jacob laid the rods in front of the eyes of the flock in the watering troughs, that they might conceive among the rods;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V42">
    42
  </span>
  but when the flock were feeble, he didn’t put them in. So the feebler were Laban’s, and the stronger Jacob’s.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN30V43">
    43
  </span>
  The man increased exceedingly, and had large flocks, female servants and male servants, and camels and donkeys.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN30FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN30V24">
      30:24
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Joseph means “may he add”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 31

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V1">
    1
  </span>
  Jacob heard Laban’s sons’ words, saying, “Jacob has taken away all that was our father’s. He has obtained all this wealth from that which was our father’s.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V2">
    2
  </span>
  Jacob saw the expression on Laban’s face, and, behold, it was not toward him as before.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V3">
    3
  </span>
  Yahweh said to Jacob, “Return to the land of your fathers, and to your relatives, and I will be with you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V4">
    4
  </span>
  Jacob sent and called Rachel and Leah to the field to his flock,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V5">
    5
  </span>
  and said to them, “I see the expression on your father’s face, that it is not toward me as before; but the God of my father has been with me.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V6">
    6
  </span>
  You know that I have served your father with all of my strength.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V7">
    7
  </span>
  Your father has deceived me, and changed my wages ten times, but God didn’t allow him to hurt me.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V8">
    8
  </span>
  If he said, ‘The speckled will be your wages,’ then all the flock bore speckled. If he said, ‘The streaked will be your wages,’ then all the flock bore streaked.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V9">
    9
  </span>
  Thus God has taken away your father’s livestock, and given them to me.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V10">
    10
  </span>
  During mating season, I lifted up my eyes, and saw in a dream, and behold, the male goats which leaped on the flock were streaked, speckled, and grizzled.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V11">
    11
  </span>
  The angel of God said to me in the dream, ‘Jacob,’ and I said, ‘Here I am.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V12">
    12
  </span>
  He said, ‘Now lift up your eyes, and behold, all the male goats which leap on the flock are streaked, speckled, and grizzled, for I have seen all that Laban does to you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V13">
    13
  </span>
  I am the God of Bethel, where you anointed a pillar, where you vowed a vow to me. Now arise, get out from this land, and return to the land of your birth.’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V14">
    14
  </span>
  Rachel and Leah answered him, “Is there yet any portion or inheritance for us in our father’s house?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V15">
    15
  </span>
  Aren’t we considered as foreigners by him? For he has sold us, and has also used up our money.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V16">
    16
  </span>
  For all the riches which God has taken away from our father are ours and our children’s. Now then, whatever God has said to you, do.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V17">
    17
  </span>
  Then Jacob rose up, and set his sons and his wives on the camels,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V18">
    18
  </span>
  and he took away all his livestock, and all his possessions which he had gathered, including the livestock which he had gained in Paddan Aram, to go to Isaac his father, to the land of Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V19">
    19
  </span>
  Now Laban had gone to shear his sheep; and Rachel stole the teraphim
  <a href="#GEN31FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      teraphim were household idols that may have been associated with inheritance rights to the household property.
    </span>
  </a>
  that were her father’s.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V20">
    20
  </span>
  Jacob deceived Laban the Syrian, in that he didn’t tell him that he was running away.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V21">
    21
  </span>
  So he fled with all that he had. He rose up, passed over the River, and set his face toward the mountain of Gilead.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V22">
    22
  </span>
  Laban was told on the third day that Jacob had fled.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V23">
    23
  </span>
  He took his relatives with him, and pursued him seven days’ journey. He overtook him in the mountain of Gilead.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V24">
    24
  </span>
  God came to Laban the Syrian in a dream of the night, and said to him, “Be careful that you don’t speak to Jacob either good or bad.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V25">
    25
  </span>
  Laban caught up with Jacob. Now Jacob had pitched his tent in the mountain, and Laban with his relatives encamped in the mountain of Gilead.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V26">
    26
  </span>
  Laban said to Jacob, “What have you done, that you have deceived me, and carried away my daughters like captives of the sword?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V27">
    27
  </span>
  Why did you flee secretly, and deceive me, and didn’t tell me, that I might have sent you away with mirth and with songs, with tambourine and with harp;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V28">
    28
  </span>
  and didn’t allow me to kiss my sons and my daughters? Now have you done foolishly.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V29">
    29
  </span>
  It is in the power of my hand to hurt you, but the God of your father spoke to me last night, saying, ‘Be careful that you don’t speak to Jacob either good or bad.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V30">
    30
  </span>
  Now, you want to be gone, because you greatly longed for your father’s house, but why have you stolen my gods?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V31">
    31
  </span>
  Jacob answered Laban, “Because I was afraid, for I said, ‘Lest you should take your daughters from me by force.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V32">
    32
  </span>
  Anyone you find your gods with shall not live. Before our relatives, discern what is yours with me, and take it.” For Jacob didn’t know that Rachel had stolen them.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V33">
    33
  </span>
  Laban went into Jacob’s tent, into Leah’s tent, and into the tent of the two female servants; but he didn’t find them. He went out of Leah’s tent, and entered into Rachel’s tent.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V34">
    34
  </span>
  Now Rachel had taken the teraphim, put them in the camel’s saddle, and sat on them. Laban felt around all the tent, but didn’t find them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V35">
    35
  </span>
  She said to her father, “Don’t let my lord be angry that I can’t rise up before you; for I’m having my period.” He searched, but didn’t find the teraphim.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V36">
    36
  </span>
  Jacob was angry, and argued with Laban. Jacob answered Laban, “What is my trespass? What is my sin, that you have hotly pursued me?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V37">
    37
  </span>
  Now that you have felt around in all my stuff, what have you found of all your household stuff? Set it here before my relatives and your relatives, that they may judge between us two.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V38">
    38
  </span>
  “These twenty years I have been with you. Your ewes and your female goats have not cast their young, and I haven’t eaten the rams of your flocks.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V39">
    39
  </span>
  That which was torn of animals, I didn’t bring to you. I bore its loss. Of my hand you required it, whether stolen by day or stolen by night.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V40">
    40
  </span>
  This was my situation: in the day the drought consumed me, and the frost by night; and my sleep fled from my eyes.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V41">
    41
  </span>
  These twenty years I have been in your house. I served you fourteen years for your two daughters, and six years for your flock, and you have changed my wages ten times.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V42">
    42
  </span>
  Unless the God of my father, the God of Abraham, and the fear of Isaac, had been with me, surely now you would have sent me away empty. God has seen my affliction and the labor of my hands, and rebuked you last night.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V43">
    43
  </span>
  Laban answered Jacob, “The daughters are my daughters, the children are my children, the flocks are my flocks, and all that you see is mine! What can I do today to these my daughters, or to their children whom they have borne?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V44">
    44
  </span>
  Now come, let’s make a covenant, you and I. Let it be for a witness between me and you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V45">
    45
  </span>
  Jacob took a stone, and set it up for a pillar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V46">
    46
  </span>
  Jacob said to his relatives, “Gather stones.” They took stones, and made a heap. They ate there by the heap.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V47">
    47
  </span>
  Laban called it Jegar Sahadutha,
  <a href="#GEN31FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      “Jegar Sahadutha” means “Witness Heap” in Aramaic.
    </span>
  </a>
  but Jacob called it Galeed.
  <a href="#GEN31FN3" class="notemark">
    §
    <span class="popup">
      “Galeed” means “Witness Heap” in Hebrew.
    </span>
  </a>
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V48">
    48
  </span>
  Laban said, “This heap is witness between me and you today.” Therefore it was named Galeed
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V49">
    49
  </span>
  and Mizpah, for he said, “Yahweh watch between me and you, when we are absent one from another.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V50">
    50
  </span>
  If you afflict my daughters, or if you take wives in addition to my daughters, no man is with us; behold, God is witness between me and you.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V51">
    51
  </span>
  Laban said to Jacob, “See this heap, and see the pillar, which I have set between me and you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V52">
    52
  </span>
  May this heap be a witness, and the pillar be a witness, that I will not pass over this heap to you, and that you will not pass over this heap and this pillar to me, for harm.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V53">
    53
  </span>
  The God of Abraham, and the God of Nahor, the God of their father, judge between us.” Then Jacob swore by the fear of his father, Isaac.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V54">
    54
  </span>
  Jacob offered a sacrifice in the mountain, and called his relatives to eat bread. They ate bread, and stayed all night in the mountain.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN31V55">
    55
  </span>
  Early in the morning, Laban rose up, and kissed his sons and his daughters, and blessed them. Laban departed and returned to his place.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN31FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN31V19">
      31:19
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      teraphim were household idols that may have been associated with inheritance rights to the household property.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN31FN2">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN31V47">
      31:47
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Jegar Sahadutha” means “Witness Heap” in Aramaic.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN31FN3">
    <span class="notemark">
      §
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN31V47">
      31:47
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Galeed” means “Witness Heap” in Hebrew.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 32

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V1">
    1
  </span>
  Jacob went on his way, and the angels of God met him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V2">
    2
  </span>
  When he saw them, Jacob said, “This is God’s army.” He called the name of that place Mahanaim.
  <a href="#GEN32FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      “Mahanaim” means “two camps”.
    </span>
  </a>
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V3">
    3
  </span>
  Jacob sent messengers in front of him to Esau, his brother, to the land of Seir, the field of Edom.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V4">
    4
  </span>
  He commanded them, saying, “This is what you shall tell my lord, Esau: ‘This is what your servant, Jacob, says. I have lived as a foreigner with Laban, and stayed until now.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V5">
    5
  </span>
  I have cattle, donkeys, flocks, male servants, and female servants. I have sent to tell my lord, that I may find favor in your sight.’ ”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V6">
    6
  </span>
  The messengers returned to Jacob, saying, “We came to your brother Esau. He is coming to meet you, and four hundred men are with him.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V7">
    7
  </span>
  Then Jacob was greatly afraid and was distressed. He divided the people who were with him, along with the flocks, the herds, and the camels, into two companies.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V8">
    8
  </span>
  He said, “If Esau comes to the one company, and strikes it, then the company which is left will escape.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V9">
    9
  </span>
  Jacob said, “God of my father Abraham, and God of my father Isaac, Yahweh, who said to me, ‘Return to your country, and to your relatives, and I will do you good,’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V10">
    10
  </span>
  I am not worthy of the least of all the loving kindnesses, and of all the truth, which you have shown to your servant; for with just my staff I crossed over this Jordan; and now I have become two companies.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V11">
    11
  </span>
  Please deliver me from the hand of my brother, from the hand of Esau; for I fear him, lest he come and strike me and the mothers with the children.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V12">
    12
  </span>
  You said, ‘I will surely do you good, and make your offspring as the sand of the sea, which can’t be counted because there are so many.’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V13">
    13
  </span>
  He stayed there that night, and took from that which he had with him a present for Esau, his brother:
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V14">
    14
  </span>
  two hundred female goats and twenty male goats, two hundred ewes and twenty rams,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V15">
    15
  </span>
  thirty milk camels and their colts, forty cows, ten bulls, twenty female donkeys and ten foals.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V16">
    16
  </span>
  He delivered them into the hands of his servants, every herd by itself, and said to his servants, “Pass over before me, and put a space between herd and herd.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V17">
    17
  </span>
  He commanded the foremost, saying, “When Esau, my brother, meets you, and asks you, saying, ‘Whose are you? Where are you going? Whose are these before you?’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V18">
    18
  </span>
  Then you shall say, ‘They are your servant, Jacob’s. It is a present sent to my lord, Esau. Behold, he also is behind us.’ ”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V19">
    19
  </span>
  He commanded also the second, and the third, and all that followed the herds, saying, “This is how you shall speak to Esau, when you find him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V20">
    20
  </span>
  You shall say, ‘Not only that, but behold, your servant, Jacob, is behind us.’ ” For, he said, “I will appease him with the present that goes before me, and afterward I will see his face. Perhaps he will accept me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V21">
    21
  </span>
  So the present passed over before him, and he himself stayed that night in the camp.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V22">
    22
  </span>
  He rose up that night, and took his two wives, and his two servants, and his eleven sons, and crossed over the ford of the Jabbok.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V23">
    23
  </span>
  He took them, and sent them over the stream, and sent over that which he had.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V24">
    24
  </span>
  Jacob was left alone, and wrestled with a man there until the breaking of the day.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V25">
    25
  </span>
  When he saw that he didn’t prevail against him, the man touched the hollow of his thigh, and the hollow of Jacob’s thigh was strained as he wrestled.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V26">
    26
  </span>
  The man said, “Let me go, for the day breaks.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Jacob said, “I won’t let you go unless you bless me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V27">
    27
  </span>
  He said to him, “What is your name?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Jacob”.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V28">
    28
  </span>
  He said, “Your name will no longer be called Jacob, but Israel; for you have fought with God and with men, and have prevailed.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V29">
    29
  </span>
  Jacob asked him, “Please tell me your name.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Why is it that you ask what my name is?” So he blessed him there.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V30">
    30
  </span>
  Jacob called the name of the place Peniel;
  <a href="#GEN32FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      Peniel means “face of God”.
    </span>
  </a>
  for he said, “I have seen God face to face, and my life is preserved.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V31">
    31
  </span>
  The sun rose on him as he passed over Peniel, and he limped because of his thigh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN32V32">
    32
  </span>
  Therefore the children of Israel don’t eat the sinew of the hip, which is on the hollow of the thigh, to this day, because he touched the hollow of Jacob’s thigh in the sinew of the hip.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN32FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN32V2">
      32:2
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Mahanaim” means “two camps”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN32FN2">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN32V30">
      32:30
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Peniel means “face of God”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 33

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V1">
    1
  </span>
  Jacob lifted up his eyes, and looked, and, behold, Esau was coming, and with him four hundred men. He divided the children between Leah, Rachel, and the two servants.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V2">
    2
  </span>
  He put the servants and their children in front, Leah and her children after, and Rachel and Joseph at the rear.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V3">
    3
  </span>
  He himself passed over in front of them, and bowed himself to the ground seven times, until he came near to his brother.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V4">
    4
  </span>
  Esau ran to meet him, embraced him, fell on his neck, kissed him, and they wept.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V5">
    5
  </span>
  He lifted up his eyes, and saw the women and the children; and said, “Who are these with you?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “The children whom God has graciously given your servant.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V6">
    6
  </span>
  Then the servants came near with their children, and they bowed themselves.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V7">
    7
  </span>
  Leah also and her children came near, and bowed themselves. After them, Joseph came near with Rachel, and they bowed themselves.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V8">
    8
  </span>
  Esau said, “What do you mean by all this company which I met?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Jacob said, “To find favor in the sight of my lord.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V9">
    9
  </span>
  Esau said, “I have enough, my brother; let that which you have be yours.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V10">
    10
  </span>
  Jacob said, “Please, no, if I have now found favor in your sight, then receive my present at my hand, because I have seen your face, as one sees the face of God, and you were pleased with me.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V11">
    11
  </span>
  Please take the gift that I brought to you, because God has dealt graciously with me, and because I have enough.” He urged him, and he took it.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V12">
    12
  </span>
  Esau said, “Let’s take our journey, and let’s go, and I will go before you.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V13">
    13
  </span>
  Jacob said to him, “My lord knows that the children are tender, and that the flocks and herds with me have their young, and if they overdrive them one day, all the flocks will die.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V14">
    14
  </span>
  Please let my lord pass over before his servant, and I will lead on gently, according to the pace of the livestock that are before me and according to the pace of the children, until I come to my lord to Seir.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V15">
    15
  </span>
  Esau said, “Let me now leave with you some of the people who are with me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Why? Let me find favor in the sight of my lord.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V16">
    16
  </span>
  So Esau returned that day on his way to Seir.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V17">
    17
  </span>
  Jacob traveled to Succoth, built himself a house, and made shelters for his livestock. Therefore the name of the place is called Succoth.
  <a href="#GEN33FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      succoth means shelters or booths.
    </span>
  </a>
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V18">
    18
  </span>
  Jacob came in peace to the city of Shechem, which is in the land of Canaan, when he came from Paddan Aram; and encamped before the city.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V19">
    19
  </span>
  He bought the parcel of ground where he had spread his tent, at the hand of the children of Hamor, Shechem’s father, for one hundred pieces of money.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN33V20">
    20
  </span>
  He erected an altar there, and called it El Elohe Israel.
  <a href="#GEN33FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      El Elohe Israel means “God, the God of Israel” or “The God of Israel is mighty”.
    </span>
  </a>
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN33FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN33V17">
      33:17
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      succoth means shelters or booths.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN33FN2">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN33V20">
      33:20
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      El Elohe Israel means “God, the God of Israel” or “The God of Israel is mighty”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 34

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V1">
    1
  </span>
  Dinah, the daughter of Leah, whom she bore to Jacob, went out to see the daughters of the land.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V2">
    2
  </span>
  Shechem the son of Hamor the Hivite, the prince of the land, saw her. He took her, lay with her, and humbled her.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V3">
    3
  </span>
  His soul joined to Dinah, the daughter of Jacob, and he loved the young lady, and spoke kindly to the young lady.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V4">
    4
  </span>
  Shechem spoke to his father, Hamor, saying, “Get me this young lady as a wife.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V5">
    5
  </span>
  Now Jacob heard that he had defiled Dinah, his daughter; and his sons were with his livestock in the field. Jacob held his peace until they came.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V6">
    6
  </span>
  Hamor the father of Shechem went out to Jacob to talk with him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V7">
    7
  </span>
  The sons of Jacob came in from the field when they heard it. The men were grieved, and they were very angry, because he had done folly in Israel in lying with Jacob’s daughter, a thing that ought not to be done.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V8">
    8
  </span>
  Hamor talked with them, saying, “The soul of my son, Shechem, longs for your daughter. Please give her to him as a wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V9">
    9
  </span>
  Make marriages with us. Give your daughters to us, and take our daughters for yourselves.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V10">
    10
  </span>
  You shall dwell with us, and the land will be before you. Live and trade in it, and get possessions in it.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V11">
    11
  </span>
  Shechem said to her father and to her brothers, “Let me find favor in your eyes, and whatever you will tell me I will give.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V12">
    12
  </span>
  Ask me a great amount for a dowry, and I will give whatever you ask of me, but give me the young lady as a wife.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V13">
    13
  </span>
  The sons of Jacob answered Shechem and Hamor his father with deceit when they spoke, because he had defiled Dinah their sister,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V14">
    14
  </span>
  and said to them, “We can’t do this thing, to give our sister to one who is uncircumcised; for that is a reproach to us.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V15">
    15
  </span>
  Only on this condition will we consent to you. If you will be as we are, that every male of you be circumcised,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V16">
    16
  </span>
  then will we give our daughters to you; and we will take your daughters to us, and we will dwell with you, and we will become one people.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V17">
    17
  </span>
  But if you will not listen to us and be circumcised, then we will take our sister,
  <a href="#GEN34FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Hebrew has, literally, “daughter”
    </span>
  </a>
  and we will be gone.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V18">
    18
  </span>
  Their words pleased Hamor and Shechem, Hamor’s son.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V19">
    19
  </span>
  The young man didn’t wait to do this thing, because he had delight in Jacob’s daughter, and he was honored above all the house of his father.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V20">
    20
  </span>
  Hamor and Shechem, his son, came to the gate of their city, and talked with the men of their city, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V21">
    21
  </span>
  “These men are peaceful with us. Therefore let them live in the land and trade in it. For behold, the land is large enough for them. Let’s take their daughters to us for wives, and let’s give them our daughters.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V22">
    22
  </span>
  Only on this condition will the men consent to us to live with us, to become one people, if every male among us is circumcised, as they are circumcised.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V23">
    23
  </span>
  Won’t their livestock and their possessions and all their animals be ours? Only let’s give our consent to them, and they will dwell with us.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V24">
    24
  </span>
  All who went out of the gate of his city listened to Hamor, and to Shechem his son; and every male was circumcised, all who went out of the gate of his city.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V25">
    25
  </span>
  On the third day, when they were sore, two of Jacob’s sons, Simeon and Levi, Dinah’s brothers, each took his sword, came upon the unsuspecting city, and killed all the males.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V26">
    26
  </span>
  They killed Hamor and Shechem, his son, with the edge of the sword, and took Dinah out of Shechem’s house, and went away.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V27">
    27
  </span>
  Jacob’s sons came on the dead, and plundered the city, because they had defiled their sister.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V28">
    28
  </span>
  They took their flocks, their herds, their donkeys, that which was in the city, that which was in the field,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V29">
    29
  </span>
  and all their wealth. They took captive all their little ones and their wives, and took as plunder everything that was in the house.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V30">
    30
  </span>
  Jacob said to Simeon and Levi, “You have troubled me, to make me odious to the inhabitants of the land, among the Canaanites and the Perizzites. I am few in number. They will gather themselves together against me and strike me, and I will be destroyed, I and my house.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN34V31">
    31
  </span>
  They said, “Should he deal with our sister as with a prostitute?”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN34FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN34V17">
      34:17
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Hebrew has, literally, “daughter”
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 35

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V1">
    1
  </span>
  God said to Jacob, “Arise, go up to Bethel, and live there. Make there an altar to God, who appeared to you when you fled from the face of Esau your brother.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V2">
    2
  </span>
  Then Jacob said to his household, and to all who were with him, “Put away the foreign gods that are among you, purify yourselves, and change your garments.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V3">
    3
  </span>
  Let’s arise, and go up to Bethel. I will make there an altar to God, who answered me in the day of my distress, and was with me on the way which I went.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V4">
    4
  </span>
  They gave to Jacob all the foreign gods which were in their hands, and the rings which were in their ears; and Jacob hid them under the oak which was by Shechem.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V5">
    5
  </span>
  They traveled, and a terror of God was on the cities that were around them, and they didn’t pursue the sons of Jacob.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V6">
    6
  </span>
  So Jacob came to Luz (that is, Bethel), which is in the land of Canaan, he and all the people who were with him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V7">
    7
  </span>
  He built an altar there, and called the place El Beth El; because there God was revealed to him, when he fled from the face of his brother.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V8">
    8
  </span>
  Deborah, Rebekah’s nurse, died, and she was buried below Bethel under the oak; and its name was called Allon Bacuth.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V9">
    9
  </span>
  God appeared to Jacob again, when he came from Paddan Aram, and blessed him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V10">
    10
  </span>
  God said to him, “Your name is Jacob. Your name shall not be Jacob any more, but your name will be Israel.” He named him Israel.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V11">
    11
  </span>
  God said to him, “I am God Almighty. Be fruitful and multiply. A nation and a company of nations will be from you, and kings will come out of your body.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V12">
    12
  </span>
  The land which I gave to Abraham and Isaac, I will give it to you, and to your offspring after you I will give the land.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V13">
    13
  </span>
  God went up from him in the place where he spoke with him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V14">
    14
  </span>
  Jacob set up a pillar in the place where he spoke with him, a pillar of stone. He poured out a drink offering on it, and poured oil on it.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V15">
    15
  </span>
  Jacob called the name of the place where God spoke with him “Bethel”.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V16">
    16
  </span>
  They traveled from Bethel. There was still some distance to come to Ephrath, and Rachel travailed. She had hard labor.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V17">
    17
  </span>
  When she was in hard labor, the midwife said to her, “Don’t be afraid, for now you will have another son.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V18">
    18
  </span>
  As her soul was departing (for she died), she named him Benoni,
  <a href="#GEN35FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      “Benoni” means “son of my trouble”.
    </span>
  </a>
  but his father named him Benjamin.
  <a href="#GEN35FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      “Benjamin” means “son of my right hand”.
    </span>
  </a>
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V19">
    19
  </span>
  Rachel died, and was buried on the way to Ephrath (also called Bethlehem).
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V20">
    20
  </span>
  Jacob set up a pillar on her grave. The same is the Pillar of Rachel’s grave to this day.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V21">
    21
  </span>
  Israel traveled, and spread his tent beyond the tower of Eder.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V22">
    22
  </span>
  While Israel lived in that land, Reuben went and lay with Bilhah, his father’s concubine, and Israel heard of it.
</div>
<div class="p">
  Now the sons of Jacob were twelve.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V23">
    23
  </span>
  The sons of Leah: Reuben (Jacob’s firstborn), Simeon, Levi, Judah, Issachar, and Zebulun.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V24">
    24
  </span>
  The sons of Rachel: Joseph and Benjamin.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V25">
    25
  </span>
  The sons of Bilhah (Rachel’s servant): Dan and Naphtali.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V26">
    26
  </span>
  The sons of Zilpah (Leah’s servant): Gad and Asher. These are the sons of Jacob, who were born to him in Paddan Aram.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V27">
    27
  </span>
  Jacob came to Isaac his father, to Mamre, to Kiriath Arba (which is Hebron), where Abraham and Isaac lived as foreigners.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V28">
    28
  </span>
  The days of Isaac were one hundred eighty years.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN35V29">
    29
  </span>
  Isaac gave up the spirit and died, and was gathered to his people, old and full of days. Esau and Jacob, his sons, buried him.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN35FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN35V18">
      35:18
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Benoni” means “son of my trouble”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN35FN2">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN35V18">
      35:18
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      “Benjamin” means “son of my right hand”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 36

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V1">
    1
  </span>
  Now this is the history of the generations of Esau (that is, Edom).
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V2">
    2
  </span>
  Esau took his wives from the daughters of Canaan: Adah the daughter of Elon, the Hittite; and Oholibamah the daughter of Anah, the daughter of Zibeon, the Hivite;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V3">
    3
  </span>
  and Basemath, Ishmael’s daughter, sister of Nebaioth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V4">
    4
  </span>
  Adah bore to Esau Eliphaz. Basemath bore Reuel.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V5">
    5
  </span>
  Oholibamah bore Jeush, Jalam, and Korah. These are the sons of Esau, who were born to him in the land of Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V6">
    6
  </span>
  Esau took his wives, his sons, his daughters, and all the members of his household, with his livestock, all his animals, and all his possessions, which he had gathered in the land of Canaan, and went into a land away from his brother Jacob.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V7">
    7
  </span>
  For their substance was too great for them to dwell together, and the land of their travels couldn’t bear them because of their livestock.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V8">
    8
  </span>
  Esau lived in the hill country of Seir. Esau is Edom.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V9">
    9
  </span>
  This is the history of the generations of Esau the father of the Edomites in the hill country of Seir:
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V10">
    10
  </span>
  these are the names of Esau’s sons: Eliphaz, the son of Adah, the wife of Esau; and Reuel, the son of Basemath, the wife of Esau.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V11">
    11
  </span>
  The sons of Eliphaz were Teman, Omar, Zepho, and Gatam, and Kenaz.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V12">
    12
  </span>
  Timna was concubine to Eliphaz, Esau’s son; and she bore to Eliphaz Amalek. These are the descendants of Adah, Esau’s wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V13">
    13
  </span>
  These are the sons of Reuel: Nahath, Zerah, Shammah, and Mizzah. These were the descendants of Basemath, Esau’s wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V14">
    14
  </span>
  These were the sons of Oholibamah, the daughter of Anah, the daughter of Zibeon, Esau’s wife: she bore to Esau Jeush, Jalam, and Korah.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V15">
    15
  </span>
  These are the chiefs of the sons of Esau: the sons of Eliphaz the firstborn of Esau: chief Teman, chief Omar, chief Zepho, chief Kenaz,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V16">
    16
  </span>
  chief Korah, chief Gatam, chief Amalek. These are the chiefs who came of Eliphaz in the land of Edom. These are the sons of Adah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V17">
    17
  </span>
  These are the sons of Reuel, Esau’s son: chief Nahath, chief Zerah, chief Shammah, chief Mizzah. These are the chiefs who came of Reuel in the land of Edom. These are the sons of Basemath, Esau’s wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V18">
    18
  </span>
  These are the sons of Oholibamah, Esau’s wife: chief Jeush, chief Jalam, chief Korah. These are the chiefs who came of Oholibamah the daughter of Anah, Esau’s wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V19">
    19
  </span>
  These are the sons of Esau (that is, Edom), and these are their chiefs.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V20">
    20
  </span>
  These are the sons of Seir the Horite, the inhabitants of the land: Lotan, Shobal, Zibeon, Anah,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V21">
    21
  </span>
  Dishon, Ezer, and Dishan. These are the chiefs who came of the Horites, the children of Seir in the land of Edom.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V22">
    22
  </span>
  The children of Lotan were Hori and Heman. Lotan’s sister was Timna.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V23">
    23
  </span>
  These are the children of Shobal: Alvan, Manahath, Ebal, Shepho, and Onam.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V24">
    24
  </span>
  These are the children of Zibeon: Aiah and Anah. This is Anah who found the hot springs in the wilderness, as he fed the donkeys of Zibeon his father.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V25">
    25
  </span>
  These are the children of Anah: Dishon and Oholibamah, the daughter of Anah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V26">
    26
  </span>
  These are the children of Dishon: Hemdan, Eshban, Ithran, and Cheran.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V27">
    27
  </span>
  These are the children of Ezer: Bilhan, Zaavan, and Akan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V28">
    28
  </span>
  These are the children of Dishan: Uz and Aran.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V29">
    29
  </span>
  These are the chiefs who came of the Horites: chief Lotan, chief Shobal, chief Zibeon, chief Anah,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V30">
    30
  </span>
  chief Dishon, chief Ezer, and chief Dishan. These are the chiefs who came of the Horites, according to their chiefs in the land of Seir.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V31">
    31
  </span>
  These are the kings who reigned in the land of Edom, before any king reigned over the children of Israel.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V32">
    32
  </span>
  Bela, the son of Beor, reigned in Edom. The name of his city was Dinhabah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V33">
    33
  </span>
  Bela died, and Jobab, the son of Zerah of Bozrah, reigned in his place.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V34">
    34
  </span>
  Jobab died, and Husham of the land of the Temanites reigned in his place.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V35">
    35
  </span>
  Husham died, and Hadad, the son of Bedad, who struck Midian in the field of Moab, reigned in his place. The name of his city was Avith.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V36">
    36
  </span>
  Hadad died, and Samlah of Masrekah reigned in his place.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V37">
    37
  </span>
  Samlah died, and Shaul of Rehoboth by the river, reigned in his place.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V38">
    38
  </span>
  Shaul died, and Baal Hanan the son of Achbor reigned in his place.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V39">
    39
  </span>
  Baal Hanan the son of Achbor died, and Hadar reigned in his place. The name of his city was Pau. His wife’s name was Mehetabel, the daughter of Matred, the daughter of Mezahab.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V40">
    40
  </span>
  These are the names of the chiefs who came from Esau, according to their families, after their places, and by their names: chief Timna, chief Alvah, chief Jetheth,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V41">
    41
  </span>
  chief Oholibamah, chief Elah, chief Pinon,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V42">
    42
  </span>
  chief Kenaz, chief Teman, chief Mibzar,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN36V43">
    43
  </span>
  chief Magdiel, and chief Iram. These are the chiefs of Edom, according to their habitations in the land of their possession. This is Esau, the father of the Edomites.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 37

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V1">
    1
  </span>
  Jacob lived in the land of his father’s travels, in the land of Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V2">
    2
  </span>
  This is the history of the generations of Jacob. Joseph, being seventeen years old, was feeding the flock with his brothers. He was a boy with the sons of Bilhah and Zilpah, his father’s wives. Joseph brought an evil report of them to their father.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V3">
    3
  </span>
  Now Israel loved Joseph more than all his children, because he was the son of his old age, and he made him a tunic of many colors.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V4">
    4
  </span>
  His brothers saw that their father loved him more than all his brothers, and they hated him, and couldn’t speak peaceably to him.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V5">
    5
  </span>
  Joseph dreamed a dream, and he told it to his brothers, and they hated him all the more.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V6">
    6
  </span>
  He said to them, “Please hear this dream which I have dreamed:
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V7">
    7
  </span>
  for behold, we were binding sheaves in the field, and behold, my sheaf arose and also stood upright; and behold, your sheaves came around, and bowed down to my sheaf.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V8">
    8
  </span>
  His brothers asked him, “Will you indeed reign over us? Will you indeed have dominion over us?” They hated him all the more for his dreams and for his words.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V9">
    9
  </span>
  He dreamed yet another dream, and told it to his brothers, and said, “Behold, I have dreamed yet another dream: and behold, the sun and the moon and eleven stars bowed down to me.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V10">
    10
  </span>
  He told it to his father and to his brothers. His father rebuked him, and said to him, “What is this dream that you have dreamed? Will I and your mother and your brothers indeed come to bow ourselves down to the earth before you?”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V11">
    11
  </span>
  His brothers envied him, but his father kept this saying in mind.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V12">
    12
  </span>
  His brothers went to feed their father’s flock in Shechem.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V13">
    13
  </span>
  Israel said to Joseph, “Aren’t your brothers feeding the flock in Shechem? Come, and I will send you to them.” He said to him, “Here I am.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V14">
    14
  </span>
  He said to him, “Go now, see whether it is well with your brothers, and well with the flock; and bring me word again.” So he sent him out of the valley of Hebron, and he came to Shechem.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V15">
    15
  </span>
  A certain man found him, and behold, he was wandering in the field. The man asked him, “What are you looking for?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V16">
    16
  </span>
  He said, “I am looking for my brothers. Tell me, please, where they are feeding the flock.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V17">
    17
  </span>
  The man said, “They have left here, for I heard them say, ‘Let’s go to Dothan.’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Joseph went after his brothers, and found them in Dothan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V18">
    18
  </span>
  They saw him afar off, and before he came near to them, they conspired against him to kill him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V19">
    19
  </span>
  They said to one another, “Behold, this dreamer comes.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V20">
    20
  </span>
  Come now therefore, and let’s kill him, and cast him into one of the pits, and we will say, ‘An evil animal has devoured him.’ We will see what will become of his dreams.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V21">
    21
  </span>
  Reuben heard it, and delivered him out of their hand, and said, “Let’s not take his life.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V22">
    22
  </span>
  Reuben said to them, “Shed no blood. Throw him into this pit that is in the wilderness, but lay no hand on him”—that he might deliver him out of their hand, to restore him to his father.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V23">
    23
  </span>
  When Joseph came to his brothers, they stripped Joseph of his tunic, the tunic of many colors that was on him;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V24">
    24
  </span>
  and they took him, and threw him into the pit. The pit was empty. There was no water in it.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V25">
    25
  </span>
  They sat down to eat bread, and they lifted up their eyes and looked, and saw a caravan of Ishmaelites was coming from Gilead, with their camels bearing spices and balm and myrrh, going to carry it down to Egypt.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V26">
    26
  </span>
  Judah said to his brothers, “What profit is it if we kill our brother and conceal his blood?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V27">
    27
  </span>
  Come, and let’s sell him to the Ishmaelites, and not let our hand be on him; for he is our brother, our flesh.” His brothers listened to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V28">
    28
  </span>
  Midianites who were merchants passed by, and they drew and lifted up Joseph out of the pit, and sold Joseph to the Ishmaelites for twenty pieces of silver. The merchants brought Joseph into Egypt.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V29">
    29
  </span>
  Reuben returned to the pit, and saw that Joseph wasn’t in the pit; and he tore his clothes.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V30">
    30
  </span>
  He returned to his brothers, and said, “The child is no more; and I, where will I go?”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V31">
    31
  </span>
  They took Joseph’s tunic, and killed a male goat, and dipped the tunic in the blood.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V32">
    32
  </span>
  They took the tunic of many colors, and they brought it to their father, and said, “We have found this. Examine it, now, and see if it is your son’s tunic or not.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V33">
    33
  </span>
  He recognized it, and said, “It is my son’s tunic. An evil animal has devoured him. Joseph is without doubt torn in pieces.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V34">
    34
  </span>
  Jacob tore his clothes, and put sackcloth on his waist, and mourned for his son many days.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V35">
    35
  </span>
  All his sons and all his daughters rose up to comfort him, but he refused to be comforted. He said, “For I will go down to Sheol
  <a href="#GEN37FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Sheol is the place of the dead.
    </span>
  </a>
  to my son, mourning.” His father wept for him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN37V36">
    36
  </span>
  The Midianites sold him into Egypt to Potiphar, an officer of Pharaoh’s, the captain of the guard.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN37FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN37V35">
      37:35
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Sheol is the place of the dead.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 38

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V1">
    1
  </span>
  At that time, Judah went down from his brothers, and visited a certain Adullamite, whose name was Hirah.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V2">
    2
  </span>
  There, Judah saw the daughter of a certain Canaanite man named Shua. He took her, and went in to her.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V3">
    3
  </span>
  She conceived, and bore a son; and he named him Er.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V4">
    4
  </span>
  She conceived again, and bore a son; and she named him Onan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V5">
    5
  </span>
  She yet again bore a son, and named him Shelah. He was at Chezib when she bore him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V6">
    6
  </span>
  Judah took a wife for Er, his firstborn, and her name was Tamar.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V7">
    7
  </span>
  Er, Judah’s firstborn, was wicked in Yahweh’s sight. So Yahweh killed him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V8">
    8
  </span>
  Judah said to Onan, “Go in to your brother’s wife, and perform the duty of a husband’s brother to her, and raise up offspring for your brother.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V9">
    9
  </span>
  Onan knew that the offspring wouldn’t be his; and when he went in to his brother’s wife, he spilled his semen on the ground, lest he should give offspring to his brother.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V10">
    10
  </span>
  The thing which he did was evil in Yahweh’s sight, and he killed him also.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V11">
    11
  </span>
  Then Judah said to Tamar, his daughter-in-law, “Remain a widow in your father’s house, until Shelah, my son, is grown up;” for he said, “Lest he also die, like his brothers.” Tamar went and lived in her father’s house.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V12">
    12
  </span>
  After many days, Shua’s daughter, the wife of Judah, died. Judah was comforted, and went up to his sheep shearers to Timnah, he and his friend Hirah, the Adullamite.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V13">
    13
  </span>
  Tamar was told, “Behold, your father-in-law is going up to Timnah to shear his sheep.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V14">
    14
  </span>
  She took off the garments of her widowhood, and covered herself with her veil, and wrapped herself, and sat in the gate of Enaim, which is on the way to Timnah; for she saw that Shelah was grown up, and she wasn’t given to him as a wife.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V15">
    15
  </span>
  When Judah saw her, he thought that she was a prostitute, for she had covered her face.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V16">
    16
  </span>
  He turned to her by the way, and said, “Please come, let me come in to you,” for he didn’t know that she was his daughter-in-law.
</div>
<div class="p">
  She said, “What will you give me, that you may come in to me?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V17">
    17
  </span>
  He said, “I will send you a young goat from the flock.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  She said, “Will you give me a pledge, until you send it?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V18">
    18
  </span>
  He said, “What pledge will I give you?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  She said, “Your signet and your cord, and your staff that is in your hand.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He gave them to her, and came in to her, and she conceived by him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V19">
    19
  </span>
  She arose, and went away, and put off her veil from her, and put on the garments of her widowhood.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V20">
    20
  </span>
  Judah sent the young goat by the hand of his friend, the Adullamite, to receive the pledge from the woman’s hand, but he didn’t find her.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V21">
    21
  </span>
  Then he asked the men of her place, saying, “Where is the prostitute, that was at Enaim by the road?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They said, “There has been no prostitute here.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V22">
    22
  </span>
  He returned to Judah, and said, “I haven’t found her; and also the men of the place said, ‘There has been no prostitute here.’ ”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V23">
    23
  </span>
  Judah said, “Let her keep it, lest we be shamed. Behold, I sent this young goat, and you haven’t found her.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V24">
    24
  </span>
  About three months later, Judah was told, “Tamar, your daughter-in-law, has played the prostitute. Moreover, behold, she is with child by prostitution.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Judah said, “Bring her out, and let her be burned.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V25">
    25
  </span>
  When she was brought out, she sent to her father-in-law, saying, “I am with child by the man who owns these.” She also said, “Please discern whose these are—the signet, and the cords, and the staff.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V26">
    26
  </span>
  Judah acknowledged them, and said, “She is more righteous than I, because I didn’t give her to Shelah, my son.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He knew her again no more.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V27">
    27
  </span>
  In the time of her travail, behold, twins were in her womb.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V28">
    28
  </span>
  When she travailed, one put out a hand, and the midwife took and tied a scarlet thread on his hand, saying, “This came out first.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V29">
    29
  </span>
  As he drew back his hand, behold, his brother came out, and she said, “Why have you made a breach for yourself?” Therefore his name was called Perez.
  <a href="#GEN38FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Perez means “breaking out”.
    </span>
  </a>
  <span class="verse" id="GEN38V30">
    30
  </span>
  Afterward his brother came out, who had the scarlet thread on his hand, and his name was called Zerah.
  <a href="#GEN38FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      Zerah means “scarlet” or “brightness”.
    </span>
  </a>
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN38FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN38V29">
      38:29
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Perez means “breaking out”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <p class="f" id="GEN38FN2">
    <span class="notemark">
      ‡
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN38V30">
      38:30
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Zerah means “scarlet” or “brightness”.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 39

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V1">
    1
  </span>
  Joseph was brought down to Egypt. Potiphar, an officer of Pharaoh’s, the captain of the guard, an Egyptian, bought him from the hand of the Ishmaelites that had brought him down there.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V2">
    2
  </span>
  Yahweh was with Joseph, and he was a prosperous man. He was in the house of his master the Egyptian.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V3">
    3
  </span>
  His master saw that Yahweh was with him, and that Yahweh made all that he did prosper in his hand.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V4">
    4
  </span>
  Joseph found favor in his sight. He ministered to him, and Potiphar made him overseer over his house, and all that he had he put into his hand.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V5">
    5
  </span>
  From the time that he made him overseer in his house, and over all that he had, Yahweh blessed the Egyptian’s house for Joseph’s sake. Yahweh’s blessing was on all that he had, in the house and in the field.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V6">
    6
  </span>
  He left all that he had in Joseph’s hand. He didn’t concern himself with anything, except for the food which he ate.
</div>
<div class="p">
  Joseph was well-built and handsome.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V7">
    7
  </span>
  After these things, his master’s wife set her eyes on Joseph; and she said, “Lie with me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V8">
    8
  </span>
  But he refused, and said to his master’s wife, “Behold, my master doesn’t know what is with me in the house, and he has put all that he has into my hand.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V9">
    9
  </span>
  No one is greater in this house than I am, and he has not kept back anything from me but you, because you are his wife. How then can I do this great wickedness, and sin against God?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V10">
    10
  </span>
  As she spoke to Joseph day by day, he didn’t listen to her, to lie by her, or to be with her.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V11">
    11
  </span>
  About this time, he went into the house to do his work, and there were none of the men of the house inside.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V12">
    12
  </span>
  She caught him by his garment, saying, “Lie with me!”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He left his garment in her hand, and ran outside.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V13">
    13
  </span>
  When she saw that he had left his garment in her hand, and had run outside,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V14">
    14
  </span>
  she called to the men of her house, and spoke to them, saying, “Behold, he has brought a Hebrew in to us to mock us. He came in to me to lie with me, and I cried with a loud voice.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V15">
    15
  </span>
  When he heard that I lifted up my voice and cried, he left his garment by me, and ran outside.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V16">
    16
  </span>
  She laid up his garment by her, until his master came home.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V17">
    17
  </span>
  She spoke to him according to these words, saying, “The Hebrew servant, whom you have brought to us, came in to me to mock me,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V18">
    18
  </span>
  and as I lifted up my voice and cried, he left his garment by me, and ran outside.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V19">
    19
  </span>
  When his master heard the words of his wife, which she spoke to him, saying, “This is what your servant did to me,” his wrath was kindled.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V20">
    20
  </span>
  Joseph’s master took him, and put him into the prison, the place where the king’s prisoners were bound, and he was there in custody.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V21">
    21
  </span>
  But Yahweh was with Joseph, and showed kindness to him, and gave him favor in the sight of the keeper of the prison.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V22">
    22
  </span>
  The keeper of the prison committed to Joseph’s hand all the prisoners who were in the prison. Whatever they did there, he was responsible for it.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN39V23">
    23
  </span>
  The keeper of the prison didn’t look after anything that was under his hand, because Yahweh was with him; and that which he did, Yahweh made it prosper.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 40

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V1">
    1
  </span>
  After these things, the butler of the king of Egypt and his baker offended their lord, the king of Egypt.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V2">
    2
  </span>
  Pharaoh was angry with his two officers, the chief cup bearer and the chief baker.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V3">
    3
  </span>
  He put them in custody in the house of the captain of the guard, into the prison, the place where Joseph was bound.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V4">
    4
  </span>
  The captain of the guard assigned them to Joseph, and he took care of them. They stayed in prison many days.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V5">
    5
  </span>
  They both dreamed a dream, each man his dream, in one night, each man according to the interpretation of his dream, the cup bearer and the baker of the king of Egypt, who were bound in the prison.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V6">
    6
  </span>
  Joseph came in to them in the morning, and saw them, and saw that they were sad.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V7">
    7
  </span>
  He asked Pharaoh’s officers who were with him in custody in his master’s house, saying, “Why do you look so sad today?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V8">
    8
  </span>
  They said to him, “We have dreamed a dream, and there is no one who can interpret it.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Joseph said to them, “Don’t interpretations belong to God? Please tell it to me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V9">
    9
  </span>
  The chief cup bearer told his dream to Joseph, and said to him, “In my dream, behold, a vine was in front of me,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V10">
    10
  </span>
  and in the vine were three branches. It was as though it budded, it blossomed, and its clusters produced ripe grapes.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V11">
    11
  </span>
  Pharaoh’s cup was in my hand; and I took the grapes, and pressed them into Pharaoh’s cup, and I gave the cup into Pharaoh’s hand.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V12">
    12
  </span>
  Joseph said to him, “This is its interpretation: the three branches are three days.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V13">
    13
  </span>
  Within three more days, Pharaoh will lift up your head, and restore you to your office. You will give Pharaoh’s cup into his hand, the way you did when you were his cup bearer.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V14">
    14
  </span>
  But remember me when it is well with you. Please show kindness to me, and make mention of me to Pharaoh, and bring me out of this house.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V15">
    15
  </span>
  For indeed, I was stolen away out of the land of the Hebrews, and here also I have done nothing that they should put me into the dungeon.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V16">
    16
  </span>
  When the chief baker saw that the interpretation was good, he said to Joseph, “I also was in my dream, and behold, three baskets of white bread were on my head.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V17">
    17
  </span>
  In the uppermost basket there were all kinds of baked food for Pharaoh, and the birds ate them out of the basket on my head.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V18">
    18
  </span>
  Joseph answered, “This is its interpretation. The three baskets are three days.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V19">
    19
  </span>
  Within three more days, Pharaoh will lift up your head from off you, and will hang you on a tree; and the birds will eat your flesh from off you.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V20">
    20
  </span>
  On the third day, which was Pharaoh’s birthday, he made a feast for all his servants, and he lifted up the head of the chief cup bearer and the head of the chief baker among his servants.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V21">
    21
  </span>
  He restored the chief cup bearer to his position again, and he gave the cup into Pharaoh’s hand;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V22">
    22
  </span>
  but he hanged the chief baker, as Joseph had interpreted to them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN40V23">
    23
  </span>
  Yet the chief cup bearer didn’t remember Joseph, but forgot him.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 41

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V1">
    1
  </span>
  At the end of two full years, Pharaoh dreamed, and behold, he stood by the river.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V2">
    2
  </span>
  Behold, seven cattle came up out of the river. They were sleek and fat, and they fed in the marsh grass.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V3">
    3
  </span>
  Behold, seven other cattle came up after them out of the river, ugly and thin, and stood by the other cattle on the brink of the river.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V4">
    4
  </span>
  The ugly and thin cattle ate up the seven sleek and fat cattle. So Pharaoh awoke.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V5">
    5
  </span>
  He slept and dreamed a second time; and behold, seven heads of grain came up on one stalk, healthy and good.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V6">
    6
  </span>
  Behold, seven heads of grain, thin and blasted with the east wind, sprung up after them.
