  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V7">
    7
  </span>
  The thin heads of grain swallowed up the seven healthy and full ears. Pharaoh awoke, and behold, it was a dream.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V8">
    8
  </span>
  In the morning, his spirit was troubled, and he sent and called for all of Egypt’s magicians and wise men. Pharaoh told them his dreams, but there was no one who could interpret them to Pharaoh.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V9">
    9
  </span>
  Then the chief cup bearer spoke to Pharaoh, saying, “I remember my faults today.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V10">
    10
  </span>
  Pharaoh was angry with his servants, and put me in custody in the house of the captain of the guard, with the chief baker.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V11">
    11
  </span>
  We dreamed a dream in one night, he and I. Each man dreamed according to the interpretation of his dream.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V12">
    12
  </span>
  There was with us there a young man, a Hebrew, servant to the captain of the guard, and we told him, and he interpreted to us our dreams. He interpreted to each man according to his dream.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V13">
    13
  </span>
  As he interpreted to us, so it was. He restored me to my office, and he hanged him.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V14">
    14
  </span>
  Then Pharaoh sent and called Joseph, and they brought him hastily out of the dungeon. He shaved himself, changed his clothing, and came in to Pharaoh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V15">
    15
  </span>
  Pharaoh said to Joseph, “I have dreamed a dream, and there is no one who can interpret it. I have heard it said of you, that when you hear a dream you can interpret it.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V16">
    16
  </span>
  Joseph answered Pharaoh, saying, “It isn’t in me. God will give Pharaoh an answer of peace.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V17">
    17
  </span>
  Pharaoh spoke to Joseph, “In my dream, behold, I stood on the brink of the river;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V18">
    18
  </span>
  and behold, seven fat and sleek cattle came up out of the river. They fed in the marsh grass;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V19">
    19
  </span>
  and behold, seven other cattle came up after them, poor and very ugly and thin, such as I never saw in all the land of Egypt for ugliness.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V20">
    20
  </span>
  The thin and ugly cattle ate up the first seven fat cattle;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V21">
    21
  </span>
  and when they had eaten them up, it couldn’t be known that they had eaten them, but they were still ugly, as at the beginning. So I awoke.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V22">
    22
  </span>
  I saw in my dream, and behold, seven heads of grain came up on one stalk, full and good;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V23">
    23
  </span>
  and behold, seven heads of grain, withered, thin, and blasted with the east wind, sprung up after them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V24">
    24
  </span>
  The thin heads of grain swallowed up the seven good heads of grain. I told it to the magicians, but there was no one who could explain it to me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V25">
    25
  </span>
  Joseph said to Pharaoh, “The dream of Pharaoh is one. What God is about to do he has declared to Pharaoh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V26">
    26
  </span>
  The seven good cattle are seven years; and the seven good heads of grain are seven years. The dream is one.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V27">
    27
  </span>
  The seven thin and ugly cattle that came up after them are seven years, and also the seven empty heads of grain blasted with the east wind; they will be seven years of famine.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V28">
    28
  </span>
  That is the thing which I have spoken to Pharaoh. God has shown Pharaoh what he is about to do.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V29">
    29
  </span>
  Behold, seven years of great plenty throughout all the land of Egypt are coming.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V30">
    30
  </span>
  Seven years of famine will arise after them, and all the plenty will be forgotten in the land of Egypt. The famine will consume the land,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V31">
    31
  </span>
  and the plenty will not be known in the land by reason of that famine which follows; for it will be very grievous.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V32">
    32
  </span>
  The dream was doubled to Pharaoh, because the thing is established by God, and God will shortly bring it to pass.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V33">
    33
  </span>
  “Now therefore let Pharaoh look for a discreet and wise man, and set him over the land of Egypt.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V34">
    34
  </span>
  Let Pharaoh do this, and let him appoint overseers over the land, and take up the fifth part of the land of Egypt’s produce in the seven plenteous years.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V35">
    35
  </span>
  Let them gather all the food of these good years that come, and store grain under the hand of Pharaoh for food in the cities, and let them keep it.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V36">
    36
  </span>
  The food will be to supply the land against the seven years of famine, which will be in the land of Egypt; so that the land will not perish through the famine.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V37">
    37
  </span>
  The thing was good in the eyes of Pharaoh, and in the eyes of all his servants.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V38">
    38
  </span>
  Pharaoh said to his servants, “Can we find such a one as this, a man in whom is the Spirit of God?”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V39">
    39
  </span>
  Pharaoh said to Joseph, “Because God has shown you all of this, there is no one so discreet and wise as you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V40">
    40
  </span>
  You shall be over my house. All my people will be ruled according to your word. Only in the throne I will be greater than you.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V41">
    41
  </span>
  Pharaoh said to Joseph, “Behold, I have set you over all the land of Egypt.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V42">
    42
  </span>
  Pharaoh took off his signet ring from his hand, and put it on Joseph’s hand, and arrayed him in robes of fine linen, and put a gold chain about his neck.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V43">
    43
  </span>
  He made him ride in the second chariot which he had. They cried before him, “Bow the knee!” He set him over all the land of Egypt.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V44">
    44
  </span>
  Pharaoh said to Joseph, “I am Pharaoh. Without you, no man shall lift up his hand or his foot in all the land of Egypt.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V45">
    45
  </span>
  Pharaoh called Joseph’s name Zaphenath-Paneah. He gave him Asenath, the daughter of Potiphera priest of On as a wife. Joseph went out over the land of Egypt.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V46">
    46
  </span>
  Joseph was thirty years old when he stood before Pharaoh king of Egypt. Joseph went out from the presence of Pharaoh, and went throughout all the land of Egypt.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V47">
    47
  </span>
  In the seven plenteous years the earth produced abundantly.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V48">
    48
  </span>
  He gathered up all the food of the seven years which were in the land of Egypt, and laid up the food in the cities. He stored food in each city from the fields around that city.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V49">
    49
  </span>
  Joseph laid up grain as the sand of the sea, very much, until he stopped counting, for it was without number.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V50">
    50
  </span>
  To Joseph were born two sons before the year of famine came, whom Asenath, the daughter of Potiphera priest of On, bore to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V51">
    51
  </span>
  Joseph called the name of the firstborn Manasseh,
  <a href="#GEN41FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      “Manasseh” sounds like the Hebrew for “forget”.
    </span>
  </a>
  “For”, he said, “God has made me forget all my toil, and all my father’s house.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V52">
    52
  </span>
  The name of the second, he called Ephraim:
  <a href="#GEN41FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      “Ephraim” sounds like the Hebrew for “twice fruitful”.
    </span>
  </a>
  “For God has made me fruitful in the land of my affliction.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V53">
    53
  </span>
  The seven years of plenty, that were in the land of Egypt, came to an end.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V54">
    54
  </span>
  The seven years of famine began to come, just as Joseph had said. There was famine in all lands, but in all the land of Egypt there was bread.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V55">
    55
  </span>
  When all the land of Egypt was famished, the people cried to Pharaoh for bread, and Pharaoh said to all the Egyptians, “Go to Joseph. What he says to you, do.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V56">
    56
  </span>
  The famine was over all the surface of the earth. Joseph opened all the store houses, and sold to the Egyptians. The famine was severe in the land of Egypt.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN41V57">
    57
  </span>
  All countries came into Egypt, to Joseph, to buy grain, because the famine was severe in all the earth.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN41FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN41V51">

    </a>

    </span>

    </span>

    </a>
    <span class="ft">

    </span>

### 42

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V1">
    1
  </span>
  Now Jacob saw that there was grain in Egypt, and Jacob said to his sons, “Why do you look at one another?”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V2">
    2
  </span>
  He said, “Behold, I have heard that there is grain in Egypt. Go down there, and buy for us from there, so that we may live, and not die.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V3">
    3
  </span>
  Joseph’s ten brothers went down to buy grain from Egypt.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V4">
    4
  </span>
  But Jacob didn’t send Benjamin, Joseph’s brother, with his brothers; for he said, “Lest perhaps harm happen to him.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V5">
    5
  </span>
  The sons of Israel came to buy among those who came, for the famine was in the land of Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V6">
    6
  </span>
  Joseph was the governor over the land. It was he who sold to all the people of the land. Joseph’s brothers came, and bowed themselves down to him with their faces to the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V7">
    7
  </span>
  Joseph saw his brothers, and he recognized them, but acted like a stranger to them, and spoke roughly with them. He said to them, “Where did you come from?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They said, “From the land of Canaan, to buy food.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V8">
    8
  </span>
  Joseph recognized his brothers, but they didn’t recognize him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V9">
    9
  </span>
  Joseph remembered the dreams which he dreamed about them, and said to them, “You are spies! You have come to see the nakedness of the land.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V10">
    10
  </span>
  They said to him, “No, my lord, but your servants have come to buy food.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V11">
    11
  </span>
  We are all one man’s sons; we are honest men. Your servants are not spies.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V12">
    12
  </span>
  He said to them, “No, but you have come to see the nakedness of the land!”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V13">
    13
  </span>
  They said, “We, your servants, are twelve brothers, the sons of one man in the land of Canaan; and behold, the youngest is today with our father, and one is no more.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V14">
    14
  </span>
  Joseph said to them, “It is like I told you, saying, ‘You are spies!’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V15">
    15
  </span>
  By this you shall be tested. By the life of Pharaoh, you shall not go out from here, unless your youngest brother comes here.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V16">
    16
  </span>
  Send one of you, and let him get your brother, and you shall be bound, that your words may be tested, whether there is truth in you, or else by the life of Pharaoh surely you are spies.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V17">
    17
  </span>
  He put them all together into custody for three days.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V18">
    18
  </span>
  Joseph said to them the third day, “Do this, and live, for I fear God.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V19">
    19
  </span>
  If you are honest men, then let one of your brothers be bound in your prison; but you go, carry grain for the famine of your houses.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V20">
    20
  </span>
  Bring your youngest brother to me; so will your words be verified, and you won’t die.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They did so.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V21">
    21
  </span>
  They said to one another, “We are certainly guilty concerning our brother, in that we saw the distress of his soul, when he begged us, and we wouldn’t listen. Therefore this distress has come upon us.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V22">
    22
  </span>
  Reuben answered them, saying, “Didn’t I tell you, saying, ‘Don’t sin against the child,’ and you wouldn’t listen? Therefore also, behold, his blood is required.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V23">
    23
  </span>
  They didn’t know that Joseph understood them; for there was an interpreter between them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V24">
    24
  </span>
  He turned himself away from them, and wept. Then he returned to them, and spoke to them, and took Simeon from among them, and bound him before their eyes.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V25">
    25
  </span>
  Then Joseph gave a command to fill their bags with grain, and to restore each man’s money into his sack, and to give them food for the way. So it was done to them.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V26">
    26
  </span>
  They loaded their donkeys with their grain, and departed from there.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V27">
    27
  </span>
  As one of them opened his sack to give his donkey food in the lodging place, he saw his money. Behold, it was in the mouth of his sack.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V28">
    28
  </span>
  He said to his brothers, “My money is restored! Behold, it is in my sack!” Their hearts failed them, and they turned trembling to one another, saying, “What is this that God has done to us?”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V29">
    29
  </span>
  They came to Jacob their father, to the land of Canaan, and told him all that had happened to them, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V30">
    30
  </span>
  “The man, the lord of the land, spoke roughly with us, and took us for spies of the country.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V31">
    31
  </span>
  We said to him, ‘We are honest men. We are no spies.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V32">
    32
  </span>
  We are twelve brothers, sons of our father; one is no more, and the youngest is today with our father in the land of Canaan.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V33">
    33
  </span>
  The man, the lord of the land, said to us, ‘By this I will know that you are honest men: leave one of your brothers with me, and take grain for the famine of your houses, and go your way.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V34">
    34
  </span>
  Bring your youngest brother to me. Then I will know that you are not spies, but that you are honest men. So I will deliver your brother to you, and you shall trade in the land.’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V35">
    35
  </span>
  As they emptied their sacks, behold, each man’s bundle of money was in his sack. When they and their father saw their bundles of money, they were afraid.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V36">
    36
  </span>
  Jacob, their father, said to them, “You have bereaved me of my children! Joseph is no more, Simeon is no more, and you want to take Benjamin away. All these things are against me.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V37">
    37
  </span>
  Reuben spoke to his father, saying, “Kill my two sons, if I don’t bring him to you. Entrust him to my care, and I will bring him to you again.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN42V38">
    38
  </span>
  He said, “My son shall not go down with you; for his brother is dead, and he only is left. If harm happens to him along the way in which you go, then you will bring down my gray hairs with sorrow to Sheol.”
  <a href="#GEN42FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Sheol is the place of the dead.
    </span>
  </a>
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN42FN1">
    <span class="notemark">
      †
    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN42V38">
      42:38
    </a>
    <span class="ft">
      Sheol is the place of the dead.
    </span>
  </p>
  <hr/>
</div>


### 43

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V1">
    1
  </span>
  The famine was severe in the land.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V2">
    2
  </span>
  When they had eaten up the grain which they had brought out of Egypt, their father said to them, “Go again, buy us a little more food.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V3">
    3
  </span>
  Judah spoke to him, saying, “The man solemnly warned us, saying, ‘You shall not see my face, unless your brother is with you.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V4">
    4
  </span>
  If you’ll send our brother with us, we’ll go down and buy you food;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V5">
    5
  </span>
  but if you don’t send him, we won’t go down, for the man said to us, ‘You shall not see my face, unless your brother is with you.’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V6">
    6
  </span>
  Israel said, “Why did you treat me so badly, telling the man that you had another brother?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V7">
    7
  </span>
  They said, “The man asked directly concerning ourselves, and concerning our relatives, saying, ‘Is your father still alive? Have you another brother?’ We just answered his questions. Is there any way we could know that he would say, ‘Bring your brother down’?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V8">
    8
  </span>
  Judah said to Israel, his father, “Send the boy with me, and we’ll get up and go, so that we may live, and not die, both we, and you, and also our little ones.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V9">
    9
  </span>
  I’ll be collateral for him. From my hand will you require him. If I don’t bring him to you, and set him before you, then let me bear the blame forever;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V10">
    10
  </span>
  for if we hadn’t delayed, surely we would have returned a second time by now.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V11">
    11
  </span>
  Their father, Israel, said to them, “If it must be so, then do this: Take from the choice fruits of the land in your bags, and carry down a present for the man, a little balm, a little honey, spices and myrrh, nuts, and almonds;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V12">
    12
  </span>
  and take double money in your hand, and take back the money that was returned in the mouth of your sacks. Perhaps it was an oversight.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V13">
    13
  </span>
  Take your brother also, get up, and return to the man.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V14">
    14
  </span>
  May God Almighty give you mercy before the man, that he may release to you your other brother and Benjamin. If I am bereaved of my children, I am bereaved.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V15">
    15
  </span>
  The men took that present, and they took double money in their hand, and Benjamin; and got up, went down to Egypt, and stood before Joseph.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V16">
    16
  </span>
  When Joseph saw Benjamin with them, he said to the steward of his house, “Bring the men into the house, and butcher an animal, and prepare; for the men will dine with me at noon.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V17">
    17
  </span>
  The man did as Joseph commanded, and the man brought the men to Joseph’s house.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V18">
    18
  </span>
  The men were afraid, because they were brought to Joseph’s house; and they said, “Because of the money that was returned in our sacks the first time, we’re brought in; that he may seek occasion against us, attack us, and seize us as slaves, along with our donkeys.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V19">
    19
  </span>
  They came near to the steward of Joseph’s house, and they spoke to him at the door of the house,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V20">
    20
  </span>
  and said, “Oh, my lord, we indeed came down the first time to buy food.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V21">
    21
  </span>
  When we came to the lodging place, we opened our sacks, and behold, each man’s money was in the mouth of his sack, our money in full weight. We have brought it back in our hand.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V22">
    22
  </span>
  We have brought down other money in our hand to buy food. We don’t know who put our money in our sacks.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V23">
    23
  </span>
  He said, “Peace be to you. Don’t be afraid. Your God, and the God of your father, has given you treasure in your sacks. I received your money.” He brought Simeon out to them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V24">
    24
  </span>
  The man brought the men into Joseph’s house, and gave them water, and they washed their feet. He gave their donkeys fodder.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V25">
    25
  </span>
  They prepared the present for Joseph’s coming at noon, for they heard that they should eat bread there.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V26">
    26
  </span>
  When Joseph came home, they brought him the present which was in their hand into the house, and bowed themselves down to the earth before him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V27">
    27
  </span>
  He asked them of their welfare, and said, “Is your father well, the old man of whom you spoke? Is he yet alive?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V28">
    28
  </span>
  They said, “Your servant, our father, is well. He is still alive.” They bowed down humbly.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V29">
    29
  </span>
  He lifted up his eyes, and saw Benjamin, his brother, his mother’s son, and said, “Is this your youngest brother, of whom you spoke to me?” He said, “God be gracious to you, my son.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V30">
    30
  </span>
  Joseph hurried, for his heart yearned over his brother; and he sought a place to weep. He entered into his room, and wept there.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V31">
    31
  </span>
  He washed his face, and came out. He controlled himself, and said, “Serve the meal.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V32">
    32
  </span>
  They served him by himself, and them by themselves, and the Egyptians who ate with him by themselves, because the Egyptians don’t eat with the Hebrews, for that is an abomination to the Egyptians.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V33">
    33
  </span>
  They sat before him, the firstborn according to his birthright, and the youngest according to his youth, and the men marveled with one another.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN43V34">
    34
  </span>
  He sent portions to them from before him, but Benjamin’s portion was five times as much as any of theirs. They drank, and were merry with him.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 44

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V1">
    1
  </span>
  He commanded the steward of his house, saying, “Fill the men’s sacks with food, as much as they can carry, and put each man’s money in his sack’s mouth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V2">
    2
  </span>
  Put my cup, the silver cup, in the sack’s mouth of the youngest, with his grain money.” He did according to the word that Joseph had spoken.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V3">
    3
  </span>
  As soon as the morning was light, the men were sent away, they and their donkeys.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V4">
    4
  </span>
  When they had gone out of the city, and were not yet far off, Joseph said to his steward, “Up, follow after the men. When you overtake them, ask them, ‘Why have you rewarded evil for good?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V5">
    5
  </span>
  Isn’t this that from which my lord drinks, and by which he indeed divines? You have done evil in so doing.’ ”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V6">
    6
  </span>
  He overtook them, and he spoke these words to them.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V7">
    7
  </span>
  They said to him, “Why does my lord speak such words as these? Far be it from your servants that they should do such a thing!
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V8">
    8
  </span>
  Behold, the money, which we found in our sacks’ mouths, we brought again to you out of the land of Canaan. How then should we steal silver or gold out of your lord’s house?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V9">
    9
  </span>
  With whomever of your servants it is found, let him die, and we also will be my lord’s slaves.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V10">
    10
  </span>
  He said, “Now also let it be according to your words. He with whom it is found will be my slave; and you will be blameless.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V11">
    11
  </span>
  Then they hurried, and each man took his sack down to the ground, and each man opened his sack.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V12">
    12
  </span>
  He searched, beginning with the oldest, and ending at the youngest. The cup was found in Benjamin’s sack.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V13">
    13
  </span>
  Then they tore their clothes, and each man loaded his donkey, and returned to the city.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V14">
    14
  </span>
  Judah and his brothers came to Joseph’s house, and he was still there. They fell on the ground before him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V15">
    15
  </span>
  Joseph said to them, “What deed is this that you have done? Don’t you know that such a man as I can indeed do divination?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V16">
    16
  </span>
  Judah said, “What will we tell my lord? What will we speak? How will we clear ourselves? God has found out the iniquity of your servants. Behold, we are my lord’s slaves, both we and he also in whose hand the cup is found.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V17">
    17
  </span>
  He said, “Far be it from me that I should do so. The man in whose hand the cup is found, he will be my slave; but as for you, go up in peace to your father.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V18">
    18
  </span>
  Then Judah came near to him, and said, “Oh, my lord, please let your servant speak a word in my lord’s ears, and don’t let your anger burn against your servant; for you are even as Pharaoh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V19">
    19
  </span>
  My lord asked his servants, saying, ‘Have you a father, or a brother?’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V20">
    20
  </span>
  We said to my lord, ‘We have a father, an old man, and a child of his old age, a little one; and his brother is dead, and he alone is left of his mother; and his father loves him.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V21">
    21
  </span>
  You said to your servants, ‘Bring him down to me, that I may set my eyes on him.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V22">
    22
  </span>
  We said to my lord, ‘The boy can’t leave his father, for if he should leave his father, his father would die.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V23">
    23
  </span>
  You said to your servants, ‘Unless your youngest brother comes down with you, you will see my face no more.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V24">
    24
  </span>
  When we came up to your servant my father, we told him the words of my lord.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V25">
    25
  </span>
  Our father said, ‘Go again and buy us a little food.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V26">
    26
  </span>
  We said, ‘We can’t go down. If our youngest brother is with us, then we will go down: for we may not see the man’s face, unless our youngest brother is with us.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V27">
    27
  </span>
  Your servant, my father, said to us, ‘You know that my wife bore me two sons.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V28">
    28
  </span>
  One went out from me, and I said, “Surely he is torn in pieces;” and I haven’t seen him since.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V29">
    29
  </span>
  If you take this one also from me, and harm happens to him, you will bring down my gray hairs with sorrow to Sheol.’
  <a href="#GEN44FN1" class="notemark">
    †
    <span class="popup">
      Sheol is the place of the dead.
    </span>
  </a>
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V30">
    30
  </span>
  Now therefore when I come to your servant my father, and the boy is not with us; since his life is bound up in the boy’s life;
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V31">
    31
  </span>
  it will happen, when he sees that the boy is no more, that he will die. Your servants will bring down the gray hairs of your servant, our father, with sorrow to Sheol.
  <a href="#GEN44FN2" class="notemark">
    ‡
    <span class="popup">
      Sheol is the place of the dead.
    </span>
  </a>
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V32">
    32
  </span>
  For your servant became collateral for the boy to my father, saying, ‘If I don’t bring him to you, then I will bear the blame to my father forever.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V33">
    33
  </span>
  Now therefore, please let your servant stay instead of the boy, my lord’s slave; and let the boy go up with his brothers.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN44V34">
    34
  </span>
  For how will I go up to my father, if the boy isn’t with me?—lest I see the evil that will come on my father.”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
  <p class="f" id="GEN44FN1">

    </span>
    <a class="notebackref" href="#GEN44V29">

    </a>

### 45

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V1">
    1
  </span>
  Then Joseph couldn’t control himself before all those who stood before him, and he called out, “Cause everyone to go out from me!” No one else stood with him, while Joseph made himself known to his brothers.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V2">
    2
  </span>
  He wept aloud. The Egyptians heard, and the house of Pharaoh heard.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V3">
    3
  </span>
  Joseph said to his brothers, “I am Joseph! Does my father still live?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  His brothers couldn’t answer him; for they were terrified at his presence.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V4">
    4
  </span>
  Joseph said to his brothers, “Come near to me, please.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They came near. He said, “I am Joseph, your brother, whom you sold into Egypt.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V5">
    5
  </span>
  Now don’t be grieved, nor angry with yourselves, that you sold me here, for God sent me before you to preserve life.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V6">
    6
  </span>
  For these two years the famine has been in the land, and there are yet five years, in which there will be no plowing and no harvest.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V7">
    7
  </span>
  God sent me before you to preserve for you a remnant in the earth, and to save you alive by a great deliverance.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V8">
    8
  </span>
  So now it wasn’t you who sent me here, but God, and he has made me a father to Pharaoh, lord of all his house, and ruler over all the land of Egypt.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V9">
    9
  </span>
  Hurry, and go up to my father, and tell him, ‘This is what your son Joseph says, “God has made me lord of all Egypt. Come down to me. Don’t wait.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V10">
    10
  </span>
  You shall dwell in the land of Goshen, and you will be near to me, you, your children, your children’s children, your flocks, your herds, and all that you have.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V11">
    11
  </span>
  There I will provide for you; for there are yet five years of famine; lest you come to poverty, you, and your household, and all that you have.” ’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V12">
    12
  </span>
  Behold, your eyes see, and the eyes of my brother Benjamin, that it is my mouth that speaks to you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V13">
    13
  </span>
  You shall tell my father of all my glory in Egypt, and of all that you have seen. You shall hurry and bring my father down here.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V14">
    14
  </span>
  He fell on his brother Benjamin’s neck and wept, and Benjamin wept on his neck.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V15">
    15
  </span>
  He kissed all his brothers, and wept on them. After that his brothers talked with him.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V16">
    16
  </span>
  The report of it was heard in Pharaoh’s house, saying, “Joseph’s brothers have come.” It pleased Pharaoh well, and his servants.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V17">
    17
  </span>
  Pharaoh said to Joseph, “Tell your brothers, ‘Do this: Load your animals, and go, travel to the land of Canaan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V18">
    18
  </span>
  Take your father and your households, and come to me, and I will give you the good of the land of Egypt, and you will eat the fat of the land.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V19">
    19
  </span>
  Now you are commanded to do this: Take wagons out of the land of Egypt for your little ones, and for your wives, and bring your father, and come.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V20">
    20
  </span>
  Also, don’t concern yourselves about your belongings, for the good of all the land of Egypt is yours.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V21">
    21
  </span>
  The sons of Israel did so. Joseph gave them wagons, according to the commandment of Pharaoh, and gave them provision for the way.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V22">
    22
  </span>
  He gave each one of them changes of clothing, but to Benjamin he gave three hundred pieces of silver and five changes of clothing.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V23">
    23
  </span>
  He sent the following to his father: ten donkeys loaded with the good things of Egypt, and ten female donkeys loaded with grain and bread and provision for his father by the way.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V24">
    24
  </span>
  So he sent his brothers away, and they departed. He said to them, “See that you don’t quarrel on the way.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V25">
    25
  </span>
  They went up out of Egypt, and came into the land of Canaan, to Jacob their father.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V26">
    26
  </span>
  They told him, saying, “Joseph is still alive, and he is ruler over all the land of Egypt.” His heart fainted, for he didn’t believe them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V27">
    27
  </span>
  They told him all the words of Joseph, which he had said to them. When he saw the wagons which Joseph had sent to carry him, the spirit of Jacob, their father, revived.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN45V28">
    28
  </span>
  Israel said, “It is enough. Joseph my son is still alive. I will go and see him before I die.”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 46

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V1">
    1
  </span>
  Israel traveled with all that he had, and came to Beersheba, and offered sacrifices to the God of his father, Isaac.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V2">
    2
  </span>
  God spoke to Israel in the visions of the night, and said, “Jacob, Jacob!”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Here I am.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V3">
    3
  </span>
  He said, “I am God, the God of your father. Don’t be afraid to go down into Egypt, for there I will make of you a great nation.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V4">
    4
  </span>
  I will go down with you into Egypt. I will also surely bring you up again. Joseph’s hand will close your eyes.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V5">
    5
  </span>
  Jacob rose up from Beersheba, and the sons of Israel carried Jacob, their father, their little ones, and their wives, in the wagons which Pharaoh had sent to carry him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V6">
    6
  </span>
  They took their livestock, and their goods, which they had gotten in the land of Canaan, and came into Egypt—Jacob, and all his offspring with him,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V7">
    7
  </span>
  his sons, and his sons’ sons with him, his daughters, and his sons’ daughters, and he brought all his offspring with him into Egypt.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V8">
    8
  </span>
  These are the names of the children of Israel, who came into Egypt, Jacob and his sons: Reuben, Jacob’s firstborn.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V9">
    9
  </span>
  The sons of Reuben: Hanoch, Pallu, Hezron, and Carmi.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V10">
    10
  </span>
  The sons of Simeon: Jemuel, Jamin, Ohad, Jachin, Zohar, and Shaul the son of a Canaanite woman.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V11">
    11
  </span>
  The sons of Levi: Gershon, Kohath, and Merari.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V12">
    12
  </span>
  The sons of Judah: Er, Onan, Shelah, Perez, and Zerah; but Er and Onan died in the land of Canaan. The sons of Perez were Hezron and Hamul.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V13">
    13
  </span>
  The sons of Issachar: Tola, Puvah, Iob, and Shimron.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V14">
    14
  </span>
  The sons of Zebulun: Sered, Elon, and Jahleel.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V15">
    15
  </span>
  These are the sons of Leah, whom she bore to Jacob in Paddan Aram, with his daughter Dinah. All the souls of his sons and his daughters were thirty-three.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V16">
    16
  </span>
  The sons of Gad: Ziphion, Haggi, Shuni, Ezbon, Eri, Arodi, and Areli.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V17">
    17
  </span>
  The sons of Asher: Imnah, Ishvah, Ishvi, Beriah, and Serah their sister. The sons of Beriah: Heber and Malchiel.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V18">
    18
  </span>
  These are the sons of Zilpah, whom Laban gave to Leah, his daughter, and these she bore to Jacob, even sixteen souls.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V19">
    19
  </span>
  The sons of Rachel, Jacob’s wife: Joseph and Benjamin.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V20">
    20
  </span>
  To Joseph in the land of Egypt were born Manasseh and Ephraim, whom Asenath, the daughter of Potiphera, priest of On, bore to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V21">
    21
  </span>
  The sons of Benjamin: Bela, Becher, Ashbel, Gera, Naaman, Ehi, Rosh, Muppim, Huppim, and Ard.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V22">
    22
  </span>
  These are the sons of Rachel, who were born to Jacob: all the souls were fourteen.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V23">
    23
  </span>
  The son of Dan: Hushim.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V24">
    24
  </span>
  The sons of Naphtali: Jahzeel, Guni, Jezer, and Shillem.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V25">
    25
  </span>
  These are the sons of Bilhah, whom Laban gave to Rachel, his daughter, and these she bore to Jacob: all the souls were seven.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V26">
    26
  </span>
  All the souls who came with Jacob into Egypt, who were his direct offspring, in addition to Jacob’s sons’ wives, all the souls were sixty-six.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V27">
    27
  </span>
  The sons of Joseph, who were born to him in Egypt, were two souls. All the souls of the house of Jacob, who came into Egypt, were seventy.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V28">
    28
  </span>
  Jacob sent Judah before him to Joseph, to show the way before him to Goshen, and they came into the land of Goshen.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V29">
    29
  </span>
  Joseph prepared his chariot, and went up to meet Israel, his father, in Goshen. He presented himself to him, and fell on his neck, and wept on his neck a good while.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V30">
    30
  </span>
  Israel said to Joseph, “Now let me die, since I have seen your face, that you are still alive.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V31">
    31
  </span>
  Joseph said to his brothers, and to his father’s house, “I will go up, and speak with Pharaoh, and will tell him, ‘My brothers, and my father’s house, who were in the land of Canaan, have come to me.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V32">
    32
  </span>
  These men are shepherds, for they have been keepers of livestock, and they have brought their flocks, and their herds, and all that they have.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V33">
    33
  </span>
  It will happen, when Pharaoh summons you, and will say, ‘What is your occupation?’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN46V34">
    34
  </span>
  that you shall say, ‘Your servants have been keepers of livestock from our youth even until now, both we, and our fathers:’ that you may dwell in the land of Goshen; for every shepherd is an abomination to the Egyptians.”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 47

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V1">
    1
  </span>
  Then Joseph went in and told Pharaoh, and said, “My father and my brothers, with their flocks, their herds, and all that they own, have come out of the land of Canaan; and behold, they are in the land of Goshen.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V2">
    2
  </span>
  From among his brothers he took five men, and presented them to Pharaoh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V3">
    3
  </span>
  Pharaoh said to his brothers, “What is your occupation?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  They said to Pharaoh, “Your servants are shepherds, both we, and our fathers.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V4">
    4
  </span>
  They also said to Pharaoh, “We have come to live as foreigners in the land, for there is no pasture for your servants’ flocks. For the famine is severe in the land of Canaan. Now therefore, please let your servants dwell in the land of Goshen.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V5">
    5
  </span>
  Pharaoh spoke to Joseph, saying, “Your father and your brothers have come to you.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V6">
    6
  </span>
  The land of Egypt is before you. Make your father and your brothers dwell in the best of the land. Let them dwell in the land of Goshen. If you know any able men among them, then put them in charge of my livestock.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V7">
    7
  </span>
  Joseph brought in Jacob, his father, and set him before Pharaoh; and Jacob blessed Pharaoh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V8">
    8
  </span>
  Pharaoh said to Jacob, “How old are you?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V9">
    9
  </span>
  Jacob said to Pharaoh, “The years of my pilgrimage are one hundred thirty years. The days of the years of my life have been few and evil. They have not attained to the days of the years of the life of my fathers in the days of their pilgrimage.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V10">
    10
  </span>
  Jacob blessed Pharaoh, and went out from the presence of Pharaoh.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V11">
    11
  </span>
  Joseph placed his father and his brothers, and gave them a possession in the land of Egypt, in the best of the land, in the land of Rameses, as Pharaoh had commanded.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V12">
    12
  </span>
  Joseph provided his father, his brothers, and all of his father’s household with bread, according to the sizes of their families.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V13">
    13
  </span>
  There was no bread in all the land; for the famine was very severe, so that the land of Egypt and the land of Canaan fainted by reason of the famine.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V14">
    14
  </span>
  Joseph gathered up all the money that was found in the land of Egypt, and in the land of Canaan, for the grain which they bought: and Joseph brought the money into Pharaoh’s house.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V15">
    15
  </span>
  When the money was all spent in the land of Egypt, and in the land of Canaan, all the Egyptians came to Joseph, and said, “Give us bread, for why should we die in your presence? For our money fails.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V16">
    16
  </span>
  Joseph said, “Give me your livestock; and I will give you food for your livestock, if your money is gone.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V17">
    17
  </span>
  They brought their livestock to Joseph, and Joseph gave them bread in exchange for the horses, and for the flocks, and for the herds, and for the donkeys: and he fed them with bread in exchange for all their livestock for that year.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V18">
    18
  </span>
  When that year was ended, they came to him the second year, and said to him, “We will not hide from my lord how our money is all spent, and the herds of livestock are my lord’s. There is nothing left in the sight of my lord, but our bodies, and our lands.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V19">
    19
  </span>
  Why should we die before your eyes, both we and our land? Buy us and our land for bread, and we and our land will be servants to Pharaoh. Give us seed, that we may live, and not die, and that the land won’t be desolate.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V20">
    20
  </span>
  So Joseph bought all the land of Egypt for Pharaoh, for every man of the Egyptians sold his field, because the famine was severe on them, and the land became Pharaoh’s.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V21">
    21
  </span>
  As for the people, he moved them to the cities from one end of the border of Egypt even to the other end of it.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V22">
    22
  </span>
  Only he didn’t buy the land of the priests, for the priests had a portion from Pharaoh, and ate their portion which Pharaoh gave them. That is why they didn’t sell their land.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V23">
    23
  </span>
  Then Joseph said to the people, “Behold, I have bought you and your land today for Pharaoh. Behold, here is seed for you, and you shall sow the land.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V24">
    24
  </span>
  It will happen at the harvests, that you shall give a fifth to Pharaoh, and four parts will be your own, for seed of the field, for your food, for them of your households, and for food for your little ones.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V25">
    25
  </span>
  They said, “You have saved our lives! Let us find favor in the sight of my lord, and we will be Pharaoh’s servants.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V26">
    26
  </span>
  Joseph made it a statute concerning the land of Egypt to this day, that Pharaoh should have the fifth. Only the land of the priests alone didn’t become Pharaoh’s.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V27">
    27
  </span>
  Israel lived in the land of Egypt, in the land of Goshen; and they got themselves possessions therein, and were fruitful, and multiplied exceedingly.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V28">
    28
  </span>
  Jacob lived in the land of Egypt seventeen years. So the days of Jacob, the years of his life, were one hundred forty-seven years.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V29">
    29
  </span>
  The time came near that Israel must die, and he called his son Joseph, and said to him, “If now I have found favor in your sight, please put your hand under my thigh, and deal kindly and truly with me. Please don’t bury me in Egypt,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V30">
    30
  </span>
  but when I sleep with my fathers, you shall carry me out of Egypt, and bury me in their burying place.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  Joseph said, “I will do as you have said.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN47V31">
    31
  </span>
  Israel said, “Swear to me,” and he swore to him. Then Israel bowed himself on the bed’s head.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 48

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V1">
    1
  </span>
  After these things, someone said to Joseph, “Behold, your father is sick.” He took with him his two sons, Manasseh and Ephraim.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V2">
    2
  </span>
  Someone told Jacob, and said, “Behold, your son Joseph comes to you,” and Israel strengthened himself, and sat on the bed.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V3">
    3
  </span>
  Jacob said to Joseph, “God Almighty appeared to me at Luz in the land of Canaan, and blessed me,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V4">
    4
  </span>
  and said to me, ‘Behold, I will make you fruitful, and multiply you, and I will make of you a company of peoples, and will give this land to your offspring after you for an everlasting possession.’
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V5">
    5
  </span>
  Now your two sons, who were born to you in the land of Egypt before I came to you into Egypt, are mine; Ephraim and Manasseh, even as Reuben and Simeon, will be mine.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V6">
    6
  </span>
  Your offspring, whom you become the father of after them, will be yours. They will be called after the name of their brothers in their inheritance.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V7">
    7
  </span>
  As for me, when I came from Paddan, Rachel died beside me in the land of Canaan on the way, when there was still some distance to come to Ephrath, and I buried her there on the way to Ephrath (also called Bethlehem).”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V8">
    8
  </span>
  Israel saw Joseph’s sons, and said, “Who are these?”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V9">
    9
  </span>
  Joseph said to his father, “They are my sons, whom God has given me here.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  He said, “Please bring them to me, and I will bless them.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V10">
    10
  </span>
  Now the eyes of Israel were dim for age, so that he couldn’t see well. Joseph brought them near to him; and he kissed them, and embraced them.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V11">
    11
  </span>
  Israel said to Joseph, “I didn’t think I would see your face, and behold, God has let me see your offspring also.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V12">
    12
  </span>
  Joseph brought them out from between his knees, and he bowed himself with his face to the earth.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V13">
    13
  </span>
  Joseph took them both, Ephraim in his right hand toward Israel’s left hand, and Manasseh in his left hand toward Israel’s right hand, and brought them near to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V14">
    14
  </span>
  Israel stretched out his right hand, and laid it on Ephraim’s head, who was the younger, and his left hand on Manasseh’s head, guiding his hands knowingly, for Manasseh was the firstborn.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V15">
    15
  </span>
  He blessed Joseph, and said,
</div>
<div class="q">
  “The God before whom my fathers Abraham and Isaac walked,
</div>
<div class="q">
  the God who has fed me all my life long to this day,
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V16">
    16
  </span>
  the angel who has redeemed me from all evil, bless the lads,
</div>
<div class="q">
  and let my name be named on them,
</div>
<div class="q">
  and the name of my fathers Abraham and Isaac.
</div>
<div class="q">
  Let them grow into a multitude upon the earth.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V17">
    17
  </span>
  When Joseph saw that his father laid his right hand on the head of Ephraim, it displeased him. He held up his father’s hand, to remove it from Ephraim’s head to Manasseh’s head.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V18">
    18
  </span>
  Joseph said to his father, “Not so, my father, for this is the firstborn. Put your right hand on his head.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V19">
    19
  </span>
  His father refused, and said, “I know, my son, I know. He also will become a people, and he also will be great. However, his younger brother will be greater than he, and his offspring will become a multitude of nations.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V20">
    20
  </span>
  He blessed them that day, saying, “Israel will bless in you, saying, ‘God make you as Ephraim and as Manasseh’ ” He set Ephraim before Manasseh.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V21">
    21
  </span>
  Israel said to Joseph, “Behold, I am dying, but God will be with you, and bring you again to the land of your fathers.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN48V22">
    22
  </span>
  Moreover I have given to you one portion above your brothers, which I took out of the hand of the Amorite with my sword and with my bow.”
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>


### 49

<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V1">
    1
  </span>
  Jacob called to his sons, and said: “Gather yourselves together, that I may tell you that which will happen to you in the days to come.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V2">
    2
  </span>
  Assemble yourselves, and hear, you sons of Jacob.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Listen to Israel, your father.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V3">
    3
  </span>
  “Reuben, you are my firstborn, my might, and the beginning of my strength,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  excelling in dignity, and excelling in power.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V4">
    4
  </span>
  Boiling over like water, you shall not excel,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  because you went up to your father’s bed,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  then defiled it. He went up to my couch.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V5">
    5
  </span>
  “Simeon and Levi are brothers.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Their swords are weapons of violence.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V6">
    6
  </span>
  My soul, don’t come into their council.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  My glory, don’t be united to their assembly;
</div>
<div class="q">
  for in their anger they killed men.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  In their self-will they hamstrung cattle.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V7">
    7
  </span>
  Cursed be their anger, for it was fierce;
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and their wrath, for it was cruel.
</div>
<div class="q">
  I will divide them in Jacob,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and scatter them in Israel.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V8">
    8
  </span>
  “Judah, your brothers will praise you.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Your hand will be on the neck of your enemies.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Your father’s sons will bow down before you.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V9">
    9
  </span>
  Judah is a lion’s cub.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  From the prey, my son, you have gone up.
</div>
<div class="q">
  He stooped down, he crouched as a lion,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  as a lioness.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  Who will rouse him up?
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V10">
    10
  </span>
  The scepter will not depart from Judah,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  nor the ruler’s staff from between his feet,
</div>
<div class="q">
  until he comes to whom it belongs.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  The obedience of the peoples will be to him.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V11">
    11
  </span>
  Binding his foal to the vine,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  his donkey’s colt to the choice vine,
</div>
<div class="q">
  he has washed his garments in wine,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  his robes in the blood of grapes.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V12">
    12
  </span>
  His eyes will be red with wine,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  his teeth white with milk.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V13">
    13
  </span>
  “Zebulun will dwell at the haven of the sea.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  He will be for a haven of ships.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  His border will be on Sidon.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V14">
    14
  </span>
  “Issachar is a strong donkey,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  lying down between the saddlebags.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V15">
    15
  </span>
  He saw a resting place, that it was good,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  the land, that it was pleasant.
</div>
<div class="q">
  He bows his shoulder to the burden,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  and becomes a servant doing forced labor.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V16">
    16
  </span>
  “Dan will judge his people,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  as one of the tribes of Israel.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V17">
    17
  </span>
  Dan will be a serpent on the trail,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  an adder in the path,
</div>
<div class="q">
  that bites the horse’s heels,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  so that his rider falls backward.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V18">
    18
  </span>
  I have waited for your salvation, Yahweh.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V19">
    19
  </span>
  “A troop will press on Gad,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  but he will press on their heel.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V20">
    20
  </span>
  “Asher’s food will be rich.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  He will produce royal dainties.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V21">
    21
  </span>
  “Naphtali is a doe set free,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  who bears beautiful fawns.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V22">
    22
  </span>
  “Joseph is a fruitful vine,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  a fruitful vine by a spring.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  His branches run over the wall.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V23">
    23
  </span>
  The archers have severely grieved him,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  shot at him, and persecuted him:
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V24">
    24
  </span>
  But his bow remained strong.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  The arms of his hands were made strong,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  by the hands of the Mighty One of Jacob,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  (from there is the shepherd, the stone of Israel),
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V25">
    25
  </span>
  even by the God of your father, who will help you,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  by the Almighty, who will bless you,
</div>
<div class="q">
  with blessings of heaven above,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  blessings of the deep that lies below,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  blessings of the breasts, and of the womb.
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V26">
    26
  </span>
  The blessings of your father have prevailed above the blessings of my ancestors,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  above the boundaries of the ancient hills.
</div>
<div class="q">
  They will be on the head of Joseph,
</div>
<div class="q2">
  on the crown of the head of him who is separated from his brothers.
</div>
<div class="b">
</div>
<div class="q">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V27">
    27
  </span>
  “Benjamin is a ravenous wolf.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  In the morning he will devour the prey.
</div>
<div class="q2">
  At evening he will divide the plunder.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V28">
    28
  </span>
  All these are the twelve tribes of Israel, and this is what their father spoke to them, and blessed them. He blessed everyone according to his own blessing.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V29">
    29
  </span>
  He instructed them, and said to them, “I am to be gathered to my people. Bury me with my fathers in the cave that is in the field of Ephron the Hittite,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V30">
    30
  </span>
  in the cave that is in the field of Machpelah, which is before Mamre, in the land of Canaan, which Abraham bought with the field from Ephron the Hittite as a burial place.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V31">
    31
  </span>
  There they buried Abraham and Sarah, his wife. There they buried Isaac and Rebekah, his wife, and there I buried Leah:
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V32">
    32
  </span>
  the field and the cave that is therein, which was purchased from the children of Heth.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN49V33">
    33
  </span>
  When Jacob finished charging his sons, he gathered up his feet into the bed, breathed his last breath, and was gathered to his people.
</div>

### 50

<div class="nb">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V1">
    1
  </span>
  Joseph fell on his father’s face, wept on him, and kissed him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V2">
    2
  </span>
  Joseph commanded his servants, the physicians, to embalm his father; and the physicians embalmed Israel.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V3">
    3
  </span>
  Forty days were used for him, for that is how many days it takes to embalm. The Egyptians wept for Israel for seventy days.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V4">
    4
  </span>
  When the days of weeping for him were past, Joseph spoke to Pharaoh’s staff, saying, “If now I have found favor in your eyes, please speak in the ears of Pharaoh, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V5">
    5
  </span>
  ‘My father made me swear, saying, “Behold, I am dying. Bury me in my grave which I have dug for myself in the land of Canaan.” Now therefore, please let me go up and bury my father, and I will come again.’ ”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V6">
    6
  </span>
  Pharaoh said, “Go up, and bury your father, just like he made you swear.”
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V7">
    7
  </span>
  Joseph went up to bury his father; and with him went up all the servants of Pharaoh, the elders of his house, all the elders of the land of Egypt,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V8">
    8
  </span>
  all the house of Joseph, his brothers, and his father’s house. Only their little ones, their flocks, and their herds, they left in the land of Goshen.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V9">
    9
  </span>
  Both chariots and horsemen went up with him. It was a very great company.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V10">
    10
  </span>
  They came to the threshing floor of Atad, which is beyond the Jordan, and there they lamented with a very great and severe lamentation. He mourned for his father seven days.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V11">
    11
  </span>
  When the inhabitants of the land, the Canaanites, saw the mourning in the floor of Atad, they said, “This is a grievous mourning by the Egyptians.” Therefore its name was called Abel Mizraim, which is beyond the Jordan.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V12">
    12
  </span>
  His sons did to him just as he commanded them,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V13">
    13
  </span>
  for his sons carried him into the land of Canaan, and buried him in the cave of the field of Machpelah, which Abraham bought with the field, as a possession for a burial site, from Ephron the Hittite, near Mamre.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V14">
    14
  </span>
  Joseph returned into Egypt—he, and his brothers, and all that went up with him to bury his father, after he had buried his father.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V15">
    15
  </span>
  When Joseph’s brothers saw that their father was dead, they said, “It may be that Joseph will hate us, and will fully pay us back for all the evil which we did to him.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V16">
    16
  </span>
  They sent a message to Joseph, saying, “Your father commanded before he died, saying,
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V17">
    17
  </span>
  ‘You shall tell Joseph, “Now please forgive the disobedience of your brothers, and their sin, because they did evil to you.” ’ Now, please forgive the disobedience of the servants of the God of your father.” Joseph wept when they spoke to him.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V18">
    18
  </span>
  His brothers also went and fell down before his face; and they said, “Behold, we are your servants.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V19">
    19
  </span>
  Joseph said to them, “Don’t be afraid, for am I in the place of God?
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V20">
    20
  </span>
  As for you, you meant evil against me, but God meant it for good, to save many people alive, as is happening today.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V21">
    21
  </span>
  Now therefore don’t be afraid. I will provide for you and your little ones.” He comforted them, and spoke kindly to them.
</div>
<div class="p">
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V22">
    22
  </span>
  Joseph lived in Egypt, he, and his father’s house. Joseph lived one hundred ten years.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V23">
    23
  </span>
  Joseph saw Ephraim’s children to the third generation. The children also of Machir, the son of Manasseh, were born on Joseph’s knees.
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V24">
    24
  </span>
  Joseph said to his brothers, “I am dying, but God will surely visit you, and bring you up out of this land to the land which he swore to Abraham, to Isaac, and to Jacob.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V25">
    25
  </span>
  Joseph took an oath from the children of Israel, saying, “God will surely visit you, and you shall carry up my bones from here.”
  <span class="verse" id="GEN50V26">
    26
  </span>
  So Joseph died, being one hundred ten years old, and they embalmed him, and he was put in a coffin in Egypt.
</div>
<div class="footnote">
  <hr/>
</div>
